Validity of Immediate Exception in Iqrar
Ruling on the validity of an exception immediately connected to the iqrar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition for a valid exception in iqrar and apply it to judge whether a given exception is valid or invalid.

Core Idea
For an exception in iqrar to be valid, it must be immediately connected to the acknowledgment.

In Hanafi law, an acknowledgment (iqrar) can include an exception (istithna') that reduces the liability. However, this exception must be made immediately after the statement of the iqrar—any delay invalidates it. This lesson unpacks the ruling from the Kitab al-Iqrar and its practical application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its category
Recognize that the act is making an exception (istithna') within an iqrar (acknowledgment). This is part of muamalat (transactions).
2
Identify the hukm level
The ruling is sahih (valid) when the condition is met. The exception is effective and reduces the debt by the value of the excepted item.
3
Identify the key condition
The exception must be muttasil (immediately connected) to the iqrar—said in one breath without delay. A delayed (munfasil) exception is invalid.
4
Apply the condition to examples
If someone says 'I owe you 100 dirhams except 1 dinar', the exception is valid and the debt is reduced by the dinar's value. The value is determined by market price.
5
Note the consequence of invalidity
If the exception is not immediate, the iqrar stands as if no exception was made—the full amount is owed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اقرار کے متصل استثناء کیا تو استثناء درست ہے سو دراہم کا اقرار کیا اور ایک دینار یا ایک قفیز گندم کا استثناء کیا تو دینار اور ایک قفیز گندم کی قیمت مستننی ہوگی
If an exception is made immediately connected to the iqrar, the exception is valid. If someone acknowledges one hundred dirhams and excepts one dinar or one qafiz of wheat, then the value of the dinar and the qafiz of wheat becomes excepted.
Source pages p. 5

Commentary
This is a key ruling from the Kitab al-Iqrar regarding exceptions (istithna'). For an exception to be valid, it must be immediately connected (muttasil) to the iqrar; a delayed exception is not accepted. In the example given, if someone says 'I owe you one hundred dirhams except one dinar,' the exception of the dinar is valid, meaning the debt is reduced by the value of the dinar. Similarly, if wheat is excepted, its value is subtracted. The valuation of the excepted item is based on its market value. This ruling is based on the principle that the iqrar and exception are considered a single statement, and the exception is part of the acknowledgment itself.

Key Terms
استثناء (istithna'): An exception made in an acknowledgment, excluding part of what is acknowledged.
مقر (muqirr): The person making the acknowledgment (i.e., the defendant admitting a right).
مقرلہ (muqarr lahu): The person in whose favor the acknowledgment is made (the claimant).
متصل (muttasil): Immediately connected, without delay or separation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If someone says 'I owe you 100 dirhams, except a dinar,' when is the exception valid?
A) Only if the exception is said immediately after the number.
B) Only if the dinar is explicitly described.
C) Only if the muqirr swears.
D) The exception is never valid in iqrar.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, an exception in an iqrar is valid only if it is immediately connected to the acknowledgment; any delay invalidates the exception.

Division of Property in Joint Possession: Claimants of Whole and Half
Commentary on property division in joint claims.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on division of jointly claimed property when one claimant claims the whole and another claims half, distinguishing between cases with and without joint possession.

Core Idea
When both claimants possess the property, the claimant of the whole prevails entirely; otherwise, the court awards two-thirds to the whole claimant and one-third to the half claimant via 'awl.

This lesson examines a specific case from the chapter on mutual claims (da'wa) in Hanafi fiqh. Two claimants: one claims the entire house (claimant of the whole), the other claims half. The ruling depends critically on whether both are in possession of the property. The text first explains the ordinary division when possession is not shared, then addresses the situation where both are in possession, revealing a nuanced interplay between possession and ownership claims.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two claimants and their claims
There are two parties: one claims the entire property (مدعی کل), the other claims only half (مدعی نصف). These are the only claims before the court.
No other heirs or claimants exist in this scenario.
2
Determine the possession status
The ruling distinguishes between two scenarios: (a) the property is not in the possession of both claimants (e.g., it is in the hands of a third party or unoccupied), or (b) both claimants are in possession. The phrase "and if it were in their hands" signals the second scenario.
Possession here means physical occupation or control.
3
When not both in possession: apply 'awl to divide into three shares
If the property is not jointly possessed, the court finds that the whole and half combine. Base the calculation on the denominator of half (2). Since the total of shares (whole + half = 1 + 1/2 = 3/2) exceeds 1, apply 'awl: increase the denominator from 2 to 3. Thus the claimant of the whole gets 2 shares (2/3), and the claimant of half gets 1 share (1/3).
'Awl is the proportional reduction of shares to fit the total.
4
When both are in possession: claimant of whole takes all
If both are in possession, each is deemed to possess half. The half in the claimant of whole's possession is uncontested (no claimant), so it is his without judicial decree. The other half (in the claimant of half's possession) is claimed by the claimant of whole, who is an outsider to that half. Hanafi principle: the evidence of an outsider (claimant) is preferred over the possessor's evidence in a dispute. Thus the judge awards that half to the claimant of whole by decree.
The outsider's claim prevails over the possessor's because the possessor's possession does not confer irrefutable ownership.
5
Understand the underlying principle
Possession alone does not determine ownership when a valid claim is made by an outsider. The court evaluates evidence: if the outsider proves his claim, it overrides the current possessor's hold. This is a key Hanafi tenet in property disputes.
This ruling illustrates the hierarchy: proof (beyond possession) decides ownership.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب ما يدعيه الرجلان
مکان اثلاثا تقسیم ہو گا۔ یعنی مدعی کل کے لئے دو ثلث اور مدعی نصف کے لئے ایک ثلث۔ کیونکہ مسئلہ میں کل اور نصف مجتمع ہیں۔ تو مسئلہ دو سے ہوگا۔ کیونکہ نصف کا مخرج دو ہے۔ اور دو کا عدد تین کی طرف عول کرتا ہے۔ تو دو ہم بھی کل کے ہوئے اور ایک سہم مدعی نصف کا ہوا۔۔ قوله ولو كانت في أيديهما .... اور اگر وہ مکان مدعیوں کے قبضہ میں ہو تو پورا مکان مدعی کل کے لئے ہوگا۔ نصف بطریق قضا اور نصف بلا قضا اس واسطے کہ جب مکان دونوں کے قبضہ میں ہے تو ہر ایک کے قبضہ میں نصف نصف مکان ہوا تو جو نصف مدعی کل کے قبضہ میں ہے۔ اس کا تو کوئی مدعی ہی نہیں۔ لہذا وہ تو قضا قاضی کے بغیر ہی اس کا ہے اور جو نصف مدعی نصف کے قبضہ میں ہے۔ اس کا مدعی کل کا مدعی ہے۔ اور وہ شخص خارج ہے۔ اور یہ پہلے معلوم ہو چکا کہ شخص خارج کامہینہ معتبر ہوتا ہے نہ کہ قابض کا تو وہ نصف بھی قاضی اسی کو دلا دے گا۔
Chapter of what two men claim. The house will be divided into three parts: two-thirds for the claimant of the whole and one-third for the claimant of half, because the whole and half are combined; the case proceeds from two [as base], since the denominator of half is two, and the number two undergoes 'awl to three, so two shares go to the claimant of the whole and one share to the claimant of half. His statement: 'And if it were in their hands'... And if the house is in the possession of the claimants, then the entire house will be for the claimant of the whole: half by way of judicial decree and half without decree, because when the house is in both hands, each has possession of half; the half in the possession of the claimant of the whole has no claimant, so it is his without a judge's decree; the half in the possession of the claimant of half is claimed by the claimant of the whole, who is an outsider, and it is known that the outsider's [evidence] is considered, not the possessor's, so the judge will award that half to him.
Source pages p. 28

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the commentary on the chapter of mutual claims. It explains the division of a house when one claimant claims the entire property and another claims half, and both have possession. The ruling states that the claimant of the whole gets two-thirds and the claimant of half gets one-third by 'awl. In the case where both are in possession, the claimant of the whole gets the entire house: the half he already possesses is his without judicial decree, and the half possessed by the other is awarded to him by the judge because his claim is against an outsider, and the outsider's evidence prevails over the possessor's.

Key Terms
عول ('awl): Proportional increase of the denominator to accommodate shares exceeding the base, resulting in reduction of each share proportionally.
مدعی کل (mudda'ī al-kull): Claimant of the whole property.
مدعی نصف (mudda'ī an-niṣf): Claimant of half the property.
شخص خارج (shakhṣ khārij): An outsider, i.e., a claimant who does not possess the property in question.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a dispute where both claimants are in possession of a house, one claiming the whole and the other claiming half, how does the Hanafi court divide the house?
A) The house is divided into two equal halves.
B) The house is divided into three parts: two-thirds for the whole claimant, one-third for the half claimant.
C) The whole claimant gets the entire house; half by possession and half by judicial decree.
D) The house is not divided until a third party arbitrates.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi property disputes, when both claimants possess the property, the claimant of the whole takes all; when they do not, the division is two-thirds and one-third via 'awl.

The Four Types of Division (Qismah) in Hanafi Law
Classification of four types of division in disputes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the four types of division in Hanafi property law and identify the grounds for conflict between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Division is either by proportional reduction (ʿawl) or conflict (munaza'at), with intra-madhhab differences in specific cases.

This classification governs how shares are allocated in inheritance, sales, debts, and other joint properties. Understanding the four types helps navigate complex disputes, especially those involving unauthorized agents (fuduli) and differing views of Abu Hanifa and his students.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four overarching types
Recognize that division can be by agreement (first two types) or by disagreement (last two types). The first type uses 'awl (proportional reduction) by mutual consent; the second uses conflict (munaza'at) by agreement, as in the fuduli example. The third and fourth types involve intra-madhhab ikhtilaf on whether 'awl or munaza'at applies.
The third and fourth types reverse the roles of 'awl and munaza'at between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.
2
Examine the first type: ‛awl by agreement
This type applies in eight contexts (e.g., division of inherited property, debts, wills). The parties agree to reduce shares proportionally to resolve a deficiency. It is called 'awl because the total of shares exceeds the property, so they are proportionally reduced.
The eight forms are not listed here but can be found in longer works.
3
Examine the second type: munaza'at by agreement via the fuduli example
When two unauthorized agents sell the same slave—one sells the entire slave for 1000 dirhams, the other sells half for 500 dirhams—and the owner ratifies both sales, the buyers have the option to take the slave proportionally. The buyer of the whole gets 3/4, the buyer of half gets 1/4. This division is by agreement in a state of conflict (munaza'at) because each buyer claims a share.
The division is not by 'awl because the shares are not reduced; they are determined by relative purchase amounts.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf in types three and four
In type three, division is by munaza'at according to Abu Hanifa and by 'awl according to the Sahibayn. In type four, the opposite holds: Abu Hanifa says 'awl, Sahibayn say munaza'at. These differences apply to specific cases (e.g., five cases for type four).
The commentary advises consulting detailed works (Zayla'i, Bahr) for the full list of cases.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فائدة تقسیم کی چار قسمیں ہیں:
اول .... وہ جس میں تقسیم بالا تفاق بطریق عول ہوتی ہے۔ اس کی آٹھ صورتیں ہیں۔
۱۔ قسمت ۲۔ میراث ۳۔ دیون ۴۔ وصیت ۵۔ محابات ۶۔ در اہم مرسلہ ۷۔ سعایت ۸۔ جنایت رقیق
دوم ..... وہ جس میں قسمت بالاتفاق بطریق منازعت ہوتی ہے اور وہ دو فضولیوں کے مسئلے میں ہوتی ہے۔ مثلا ایک فضولی نے کسی کے ہاتھ غلام ہزار درہم میں فروخت کیا۔ اور دوسرے فضولی نے اسی غلام کا نصف دوسرے کے ہاتھ پانچ سو میں فروخت کیا اور آقا نے دونوں بیجوں کو جائز رکھا تو دونوں خریداروں کو اختیار ہے۔ اگر وہ لینا چاہیں۔ مشتری کل تین ربع لے اور مشتری نصف ایک ربع ۔
سوم .. وہ جس میں قسمت امام صاحب کے نزدیک بطریق منازعت ہوتی ہے۔ اور صاحبین کے نزدیک بطریق عول جیسا کہ مسئلہ کتاب میں اوپر مذکور ہوا اس کے علاوہ دو مسئلے اور ہیں)۔ .
چهارم وہ جس میں قسمت امام صاحب کے نزدیک بطریق عول ہوتی ہے۔ اور صاحبین کے نزدیک بطریق منازعت یہ طریقہ پانچ مسلوں میں جاری ہے۔ اگر ہر ایک کی تشریح مطلوب ہو تو مطولات زیلعی بینی ، بحر وغیرہ کی طرف رجوع کرو۔
Benefit: Division is of four types: First: that in which division is by agreement in the manner of 'awl. It has eight forms: [list]. Second: that in which division is by agreement in the manner of conflict (munaza'at), and it occurs in the case of two unauthorized agents (fuduliyyan). For example, one unauthorized agent sold a slave for a thousand dirhams, and another unauthorized agent sold half of the same slave for five hundred dirhams, and the master ratified both sales. Both buyers have the option; if they wish to take, the buyer of the whole takes three-fourths and the buyer of half takes one-fourth. Third: that in which division is in the manner of conflict according to Imam Abu Hanifa, and in the manner of 'awl according to the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), as mentioned above in the book, plus two other cases. Fourth: that in which division is in the manner of 'awl according to Abu Hanifa, and in the manner of conflict according to the two companions; this method applies to five cases. If explanation of each is desired, refer to the lengthy works of Zayla'i, Bahr, etc.
Source pages p. 28

Commentary
This is a benefit (fa'idah) from the commentary, outlining four types of division in property disputes. The first type is division by 'awl (proportional reduction) by agreement, covering eight contexts. The second is division by conflict by agreement, exemplified by two unauthorized agents selling the same slave. The third and fourth involve disagreements between Imam Abu Hanifa and the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) on whether division should be by 'awl or conflict. The commentary directs the reader to longer works for further details.

Key Terms
فضولی (fuduli): An unauthorized agent who sells without the owner's permission.
منازعت (munaza'at): Conflict or disagreement in claiming shares, leading to division based on strength of claim rather than proportional reduction.
عول (ʿawl): Proportional reduction of shares when the total of fixed shares exceeds the available property.
قسمت (qismah): Division of joint property among co-owners.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the second type of division (fuduliyyan), if one unauthorized agent sells the whole slave for 1000 and another sells half for 500, and the master ratifies both, how is the slave divided if both buyers agree to take?
A) Equally
B) Buyer of whole gets 3/4, buyer of half gets 1/4
C) Buyer of whole gets 2/3, buyer of half gets 1/3
D) They cast lots

Key Takeaway
Hanafi law distinguishes four types of division, with a key disagreement between Abu Hanifa and his students on whether ʿawl or munaza'at applies in certain cases.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute: Rider vs. Rein-Holder on Contested Beast
Ruling on priority with intra-Hanafi narration distinction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the Nawadir and Zahir al-Riwayah positions on priority in a beast dispute and identify the mufta-bihi ruling.

Core Idea
In disputes over a beast, the rider's tasarruf gives priority in Nawadir, but Zahir al-Riwayah holds equal sharing.

This passage presents a dispute where two claimants each have a connection to a beast: one rides or carries a load, the other holds reins or a water bag. The initial ruling awards exclusive ownership to the rider, citing more apparent tasarruf (use). However, the commentator clarifies that this is based on a Nawadir narration; the core transmitted texts (Zahir al-Riwayah) divide the beast equally. Understanding this intra-madhhab difference is essential for correct fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conflicting claims
Determine the type of possession each claimant has: one is actively riding or carrying a load (tasarruf), the other merely holds reins or a water bag (ancillary connection).
The examples: rider vs rein-holder, load-bearer vs water-bag holder, wearer vs sleeve-holder.
2
Apply the apparent tasarruf reasoning
The initial ruling states that the one with more apparent tasarruf (the rider/wearer) is prior because riding and wearing are specific to ownership.
Dalīl: 'lianna al-rukūb wa al-lubs yakhtaṣṣān bi al-mulk'
3
Distinguish the two Hanafi narrations
The commentator notes this ruling is from Nawadir al-Mu'alla (rare transmissions). In Zahir al-Riwayah (the relied-upon authoritative texts), the ruling differs: the beast is divided equally.
Zahir al-Riwayah includes works like al-Mabsūṭ, al-Jāmiʿ al-Ṣaghīr, etc.
4
Determine the muftā bihī
Later Hanafi scholars generally adopt the Zahir al-Riwayah position (equal division) as the basis for fatwa, unless strong evidence supports the Nawadir view.
This reflects the hierarchy: Zahir al-Riwayah > Nawādir > Fatāwā.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب ما يدعيه الرجلان۔ کریں اس اونٹ میں جس پر ایک کا بوجھ لدا ہے۔ اور دوسرے کا آبخورہ ٹکا ہے۔ تو بوجھ والا اولی ہے۔ کیونکہ وہی متصرف ہے۔ اسی طرح اگر جھگڑا کریں قمیص میں جس کو ایک پہنے ہوئے ہے اور دوسرا آستین پکڑے ہوئے ہے۔ تو پہنے والا اولیٰ ہے۔ کیونکہ دونوں میں سے اس کا تصرف اظہر ہے۔ تشریح قوله تنازعاً فى دابة ... زید ایک گھوڑے پر سوار ہے اور عمر و اس کے لگام پکڑے ہوئے ہے۔ يازید زین پر سوار ہے اور عمرو اس کا ردیف ہے۔ یا اونٹ پر زید کا بوجھ لدا ہوا ہے اور عمرہ کا آنجورہ اس پر لٹکا ہوا ہے۔ یا زید گرتا پہنے ہوئے ہے اور عمرو اس کی آستینیں پکڑے ہوئے۔ اب گھوڑے یا اونٹ گرتے میں دونوں کا جھگڑا ہوا۔ زید کہتاہ کی میرا ہے اور عمرو کہتا ہے کہ میرا ہے تو گھوڑایا اونٹ یا گر تا زید ہی کا ہوگا۔ کیونکہ اس کا تصرف ظاہر تر ہے۔ لان الركوب واللبس يختصان ب الملك۔ پھر رکوپ دابہ والا مسئلہ ائمہ اربعہ کے یہاں متفق علیہ ہے۔ اور راکب سرج کا اولیٰ ہونا اس روایت پر مبنی ہے۔ جس کو شیخ ناطفی نے اجناس میں نو وادر معلے سے نقل کیا ہے۔ ظاہر الروایہ میں وہ جانور دونوں میں نصف نصف ہو گا۔
Chapter of what two men claim. They dispute over a camel on which one has a load placed and the other has a water bag hung. The one with the load is prior because he is the one using it. Similarly, if they dispute over a shirt which one is wearing and the other is holding the sleeve, the wearer is prior because his use is more apparent. Commentary: His statement: 'They dispute over a beast...' Zayd is riding a horse and Amr is holding its reins, or Zayd is riding the saddle and Amr is his pillion, or on a camel Zayd's load is placed and Amr's water bag is hanging on it, or Zayd is wearing a garment and Amr is holding its sleeve. Now they dispute over the horse or camel or garment. Zayd says it is mine and Amr says it is mine. Then the horse or camel or garment will be Zayd's because his use is more apparent, because riding and wearing are specific to ownership. Then the issue of riding a beast is agreed upon by the four imams. And the rider's priority is based on the narration that Shaykh Natafi transmitted in Ajnas from Nawadir Mu'alla. In Zahir al-Riwayah, the animal will be half between them.
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a contested beast where one person is riding (or has a load) and the other is merely holding the reins (or has a water bag). The author first states the ruling that the rider/load-bearer has priority because his tasarruf (use/possession) is more apparent. He then notes that this ruling is agreed upon by the four imams. However, he clarifies that this is based on a narration from Nawadir Mu'alla (rare transmissions). According to Zahir al-Riwayah (the core transmitted texts), the animal is divided equally between the two claimants. Thus the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) depends on which narration is followed. This highlights the importance of distinguishing between different layers of authority within the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
تصرف (tasarruf): Actual use or control of an object, e.g., riding a horse or wearing a garment.
ظاهر الرواية (Zāhir al-Riwāyah): The core transmitted texts of the Hanafi school (the six works of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani).
نوادر (Nawādir): Rare or non-mashhūr transmissions within the Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Zahir al-Riwayah, what is the ruling when a rider and a rein-holder dispute ownership of a beast?
A) The rider gets exclusive ownership.
B) The rein-holder gets it.
C) They share the beast equally.
D) It is given to a third party.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has two narrations on beast disputes: Nawadir gives exclusive ownership to the rider, but the mufta bihi (Zahir al-Riwayah) divides the beast equally.

Garment Dispute: The Principle of More Apparent Use (Tasarruf Azhar)
Ruling on garment dispute when one wears it and the other holds sleeve

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a garment dispute where one wears and the other holds the sleeve, and apply the qiyas based on the illah of more apparent tasarruf to similar possession disputes.

Core Idea
In a garment dispute, the wearer prevails because his use (tasarruf) is more apparent than the sleeve-holder's.

In cases of possession disputes, the Hanafi school looks at the apparentness of use (tasarruf) as a key indicator. This passage presents a garment dispute: one person is wearing the shirt, another is holding its sleeve. By drawing an analogy (qiyas) to a previously established case of a rider vs. a rein-holder, the ruling is derived. Let's work through the analogy step by step to understand the legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the new case (far')
Recognize that the far' is a dispute over a shirt: one party is wearing it, the other is holding its sleeve.
This case is analogous to the beast dispute in the previous lesson.
2
Recall the original case (asl) and its ruling
The asl is a dispute over a beast: the rider is preferred over the rein-holder. The hukm of the asl is that the rider is prior.
The rider's tasarruf is more apparent than the rein-holder's.
3
Identify the effective cause (illah)
The illah is 'more apparent tasarruf' (tasarruf azhar). In the asl, riding is a more direct and obvious use than merely holding the rein.
The illah is extracted by tanqih al-manat: comparing degrees of apparentness.
4
Apply the illah to the far'
Wearing a garment is a more apparent use (tasarruf) than simply holding its sleeve. Therefore, the illah is present in the far'.
Thus the same ruling applies: the wearer is prior.
5
State the conclusion
The wearer is preferred over the sleeve-holder. This is the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school.
The ruling is consistent with the principle that stronger tasarruf indicates stronger possession.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اسی طرح اگر جھگڑا کریں قمیص میں جس کو ایک پہنے ہوئے ہے اور دوسرا آستین پکڑے ہوئے ہے۔ تو پہنے والا اولیٰ ہے۔ کیونکہ دونوں میں سے اس کا تصرف اظہر ہے۔
Similarly, if they dispute over a shirt which one is wearing and the other is holding the sleeve, then the wearer is prior because his tasarruf (use) is more apparent between them.
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on a garment dispute. The author uses qiyas (analogy) to the previous beast case: just as the rider's use is more apparent than the rein-holder's, so the wearer's use is more apparent than the sleeve-holder's. The illah (effective cause) is the strength and directness of tasarruf. The wearer is actively possessing the garment, while the sleeve-holder merely has a loose connection. Therefore, the wearer is preferred. This ruling is consistent across the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
تصرف اظہر (tasarruf azhar): More apparent use or possession, e.g., wearing a garment versus merely holding its sleeve.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) The wearer

Key Takeaway

Dispute Over a Carpet: Sitting vs. Holding
Ruling on carpet dispute when one sits and other holds

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that sitting does not constitute possession (qabd) to resolve property disputes and explain why the sitter and holder share equally.

Core Idea
Sitting on an item does not give legal possession; without possession, both claimants are equal.

In property disputes, Hanafi fiqh often looks to which party has a stronger claim through possession or use. In this ruling, we examine a scenario where two people claim the same carpet—one sits on it, the other holds it. The judge does not prefer either party arbitrarily; instead, the carpet is divided equally. Why? Because sitting, unlike riding or wearing, does not establish legal possession. This lesson unpacks that reasoning and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Dispute
Two parties claim a carpet. One is sitting on it, the other is holding it. Both assert ownership or right to possession.
This is a common dispute in markets or households.
2
Define Legal Possession (Qabd)
In Hanafi law, qabd means actual physical control that indicates ownership. It is not mere presence or use.
Qabd is required for validity of certain contracts (e.g., sale of moveable items before separation).
3
Evaluate the Acts
Sitting on a carpet is a passive act—it does not give the sitter exclusive control. Holding the carpet does give some control, but the holder is not necessarily the owner.
4
Apply the Rule
Since neither party has clear qabd, their claims are equal. Therefore, the carpet is shared equally between them (nisfa).
This is not a judicial discretion, but a fixed ruling based on equality.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اگر جھگڑا کیا ایک فرش میں جس پر ایک بیٹھا ہے اور دوسرا اس کو پکڑے ہوئے ہے۔ تو وہ ان دونوں میں مشترک ہے۔ اس کے معنی یہ ہیں کہ یہ بطریق قضا نہیں۔ کیونکہ بیٹھنا اس پر قبضہ نہیں ہے تو دونوں برابر ہو گئے۔
If they dispute over a carpet on which one is sitting and the other is holding it, then it is shared between them. The meaning is that this is not by way of judgment, because sitting on it is not possession, so they become equal.
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This passage addresses a carpet dispute. Unlike the previous cases where one party had a more apparent tasarruf (riding or wearing), sitting on a carpet does not constitute qabd (possession) in the legal sense. Therefore, both have an equal claim, and the carpet is divided equally. The author clarifies that this is not a judicial preference but a ruling based on equality of claims. The key distinction is that sitting is passive and does not indicate ownership like wearing does.

Key Terms
قبضہ (qabza): Legal possession or control. Sitting does not amount to qabd.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because sitting is stronger possession
B) Because holding is weaker
C) Because sitting does not constitute possession
D) Because the carpet is immovable

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, passive use like sitting does not create legal possession; without possession, conflicting claims lead to equal division.

Dispute Over a Cloth: Equal Yad, Equal Share
Ruling on cloth when one has full possession and other holds edge

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that possession (yad) triggers equal sharing even when one party has more physical control, and distinguish it from cases where tasarruf is equal.

Core Idea
Equal yad means equal entitlement, regardless of grip strength.

This lesson examines a scenario where one person holds a cloth entirely while another holds only its edge. Despite the disparity in physical control, Hanafi law treats both as having possession, leading to equal division. The reasoning hinges on the legal principle that more of the same type of evidence does not increase entitlement. We will walk through the ruling, its proof, and the underlying qiyas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute and the claims
Two parties both claim a cloth. One has full possession (yad) of the entire cloth, the other holds only the edge. The question is how to distribute the cloth.
2
Recognize that both have yad
In Hanafi law, holding any part of an object is considered a form of possession (yad). Therefore, both parties have a legal claim based on yad.
Holding the edge is not merely touching; it is a recognized form of control.
3
Apply the legal principle: increase in the same type of proof does not increase entitlement
The person with full possession has more of the same kind of proof (yad), not a different, stronger proof. Therefore, the excess does not give him a larger share.
This is the core talil (reasoning) of the passage.
4
Compare with the riding case
If both parties are riding an animal, they share it equally because both have equal tasarruf (control). The cloth case is analogous: both have yad, albeit one more physically, so the same rule applies.
The riding case confirms that equal yad leads to equal sharing.
5
Conclude the ruling
The cloth is divided equally (half-half) between the two parties, as neither has a superior legal proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اگر کپڑا ایک کے قبضہ میں ہو اور اس کا کنارہ دوسرے کے ہاتھ میں ہوتو وہ دونوں میں نصف نصف ہوگا۔ اس لئے کہ زیادتی جنس حجت سے ہے تو یہ استحقاق میں موجب زیادتی نہیں۔ ہے۔ بخلاف اس کے اگر وہ دونوں سوار ہوں کہ جانوران میں مساوی ہو گا۔
If a cloth is in the possession of one and its edge is in the hand of another, then it is half-half between them. Because increase in the kind of proof does not cause increase in entitlement. Contrary to if both are riding, then the animal will be shared equally.
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This passage deals with a cloth where one party has full possession (yad) and the other merely holds the edge. Despite the first having more grip, the ruling is equal sharing. The reasoning is that the additional grip is not an additional legal proof; it's just more of the same kind of evidence (hand-holding). The author contrasts this with the case where both are riding an animal: then they share equally because both have equal tasarruf. Here, the full possession holder does not get priority over the edge-holder.

Key Terms
ید (yad): Possession or control. Having the cloth in hand is yad; holding the edge is also a form of yad.
جنس حجت (jins hujjat): Kind of proof. Here, it refers to the type of evidence (yad) that both parties have.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the edge-holder has stronger proof.
B) Because extra grip is the same type of proof as the edge-holder's grip.
C) Because the cloth is shared only when both ride it.
D) Because the Hanafi school always divides property equally.

Key Takeaway
Equal yad means equal entitlement; more of the same proof does not increase one's share.

Child's Statement on Freedom: When Is It Accepted?
Ruling on child's statement determining slavery/freedom

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a child's claim of freedom and distinguish when the child's statement is accepted based on his ability to express himself.

Core Idea
A child who can speak is in his own possession; his claim of freedom is accepted, but admitting slavery establishes it.

This lesson examines a specific scenario from Hanafi fiqh: a child found in someone's possession. The key is whether the child can 'express himself' (ta'bir 'an nafsihi). The ruling depends on this capacity. We will see how the child's own statement determines his status, and why later claims are rejected.

Guided Path
1
Identify the child's capacity
First, determine if the child can speak and understand (yu'abbiru 'an nafsihi). This is the pivotal condition.
If he can express himself, he has legal capacity regarding his own status.
2
Apply rule for claiming freedom
If the child can speak and says 'I am free,' his statement is accepted because he is considered in his own possession (fi yad nafsihi).
The child's word is taken over the possessor's claim.
3
Apply rule for admitting slavery
If the child can speak but says 'I am a slave of so-and-so,' he becomes the slave of the one in whose hand he is, because he acknowledged that he has no possession over himself.
Admitting slavery negates his own possession.
4
Apply rule if child cannot express himself
If the child cannot speak or understand, he is considered a slave of the possessor, like a chattel, because he has no possession over himself.
His silence is not treated as a statement.
5
Recognize the permanence of childhood status
If a child who was established as a slave later grows up and claims freedom, his claim is not accepted because slavery was apparent upon him in childhood.
The status determined in minority is binding.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بچہ کسی کے قبضہ میں ہو اور وہ اپنی ذات سے تعبیر کر سکتا ہے اس نے کہا میں آزاد ہوں تو اس بچہ کا قول معتبر ہو گا قَالَ وَإِذَا كَانَ الصَّبِيُّ فِي يَدِ رَجُلٍ وَهُوَ يُعَبِّرُ عَنْ نَفْسِهِ فَقَالَ أَنَا حُرِّ فَالْقَوْلُ قَوْلُهُ لِأَنَّهُ فِي يَدِ نَفْسِهِ وَلَوْ قَالَ أَنَا عَبْدٌ لِفُلان فَهُوَ عَبْدَ لِلَّذِي فِي يَدِهِ لأَنَّهُ أَقَرَّ بأنَّهُ لَا يَدَ لَهُ حَيْثُ أَفَرَّ بالرَقِ وَإِنْ كَانَ لَا يُعَبِّرُ عَنْ نَفْسِهِ فَهُوَ عَبْدٌ لِلَّذِي هُوَ فِي يَدِهِ لِأَنَّهُ لَا يَدَ لَهُ عَلَى نَفْسِهِ لِمَا كَانَ لَا يُعَبِّرُ عَنْهَا وَهُوَ بِمَنْزِلَةِ مَتَاعِ بِخِلَافِ مَا إِذَا كَانَ يُعَبِّرُ فَلَوْ كَبِرَ وَادَّعَى الْحُرِّيَّةَ لَا يَكُونُ الْقَوْلُ قَوْلَهُ لِأَنَّهُ ظَهَرَ الرَّقُ عَلَيْهِ فِي حَالِ صَغَرِهِ
A child is in the possession of a man and he can express himself; if he says 'I am free', his statement is accepted because he is in his own possession. If he says 'I am a slave of so-and-so', then he is a slave of the one in whose hand he is, because he acknowledged that he has no hand (possession) over himself when he admitted to slavery. If he cannot express himself, then he is a slave of the one in whose hand he is, because he has no hand over himself since he cannot express himself, and he is like a chattel. Unlike when he can express himself. Then if he grows up and claims freedom, his statement is not accepted because slavery was apparent upon him in his childhood.
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This passage covers the ruling on a child in someone's possession. The key factor is the child's ability to 'express himself' (yu'abbiru 'an nafsihi), meaning he can speak and understand. If the child can speak and claims to be free, his statement is accepted because he is in his own possession (fi yad nafsihi). If he admits to being a slave of someone, he becomes the slave of the possessor because he has effectively negated his own possession. If the child cannot express himself, he is considered a slave of the possessor, akin to a chattel. Importantly, even if such a child later becomes an adult and claims freedom, his claim is not accepted because his slavery was established in childhood. This ruling protects the legal status determined during minority.

Key Terms
تعبیر عن نفسه (ta'bir 'an nafsihi): Ability to speak and express one's own state or condition.
في يد نفسه (fi yad nafsihi): In his own possession; having legal capacity over himself.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a child who can speak says 'I am a slave of Zaid' while in Zaid's possession, what is the ruling?
A) He is free
B) He becomes Zaid's slave
C) He waits until adulthood to decide
D) The statement is ignored

Key Takeaway
A child's ability to express himself determines whether his statement about freedom or slavery is accepted; once slavery is established, later claims are rejected.

Determining Wall Ownership: Beams vs. Water Pipes
Ruling on wall ownership based on evidence of use

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule for determining wall ownership based on visible use and distinguish between strong claims (beams, attachment) and negligible claims (water pipes, mats).

Core Idea
Ownership of a wall is proven by visible use (beams/attachment), not by minor attachments (pipes/mats).

When two parties dispute ownership of a wall, the Hanafi school examines the type of evidence each party can show. Physical integration or clear usage of the wall (like supporting beams) strongly indicates ownership, while minor attachments like water pipes hold no weight. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind this distinction, using a qiyas jaliy (clear analogy) to a previously settled dispute over a beast.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Evidence of Each Party
First, note what each disputant has placed on or in the wall. One may have beams (judu') or interlocking bricks (ittisal); the other may have water pipes (haradi) or mats (bawari).
Beams and attachment indicate structural integration; pipes and mats are mere accessories.
2
Apply the Analogy to a Beast Dispute
The author likens the wall dispute to a case where two people dispute a beast: one has a load on it (indicating use) and the other has a hanging water skin (minimal attachment). The load-bearer is the user (sahib isti'mal), while the water-skin holder is merely attached (sahib ta'alluq). Thus, the one with beams is the user and deserves ownership.
This is clear qiyas jaliy: the illa is usage/possession vs. negligible attachment.
3
Recognize the Implication of Negligible Evidence
The text states that water pipes are 'nothing' – they have no consideration. Similarly for mats, because a wall is not built for them. If only one party has water pipes and the other nothing, the wall is shared equally.
This demonstrates the principle that weak evidence does not tip the scale.
4
Apply the Rule to Scenarios of Equal Evidence
If both parties have three beams each, they are equal, so the wall is shared. The number of beams beyond three is not considered – the threshold of three establishes equality.
Three beams are a sufficient indicator of use; more do not add weight.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَإِذَا كَانَ الْحَائِطُ لِرَجُلٍ عَلَيْهِ جُدُوعٌ اَوْ مُتَّصِلٌ بِبِنَائِهِ وَلِلْآخَرِ عَلَيْهِ هَرَادِيُّ فَهُوَ لِصَاحِبِ الْجُذُوعِ وَالْإِتِصَالِ وَالْهَرَادِيُّ لَيْسَتْ بِشَيْءٍ لِاَنَّ صَاحِبَ الْجُذُوعِ صَاحِبُ اسْتِعْمَالِ وَالْآخَرُ صَاحِبُ تَعَلَّقِ فَصَارَ كَـدَابَّةٍ تَنَازَعَا فِيْهَا وَلَأَحَدِهِمَا عَلَيْهَا حَمَلْ وَلِلْآخَرِ كُوزَ مُعَلَّقَ وَالْمُرَادُ بِالْإِتِصَالِ مُدَاخِلَةٌ لَبِنِ جِدَارِهِ فِيْهِ وَلَبِنُ هَذَا فِي جِدَارِهِ وَقَدْ يُسَمَّى إِتِصَالُ تَرْبِيعِ وَهَذَا شَاهِدٌ ظَاهِرٌ لِصَاحِبِهِ لِأَنَّ بَعْضَ بِنَائِهِ عَلَى بَعْضٍ هَذَا الْحَائِطِ وَقَوْلُهُ الْهَرَادِيُّ لَيْسَتْ بِشَيْءٍ يَدُلُّ عَلَى أَنَّهُ لَا إِعْتِبَارَ لِلْهَرَادِي أَصْلًا وَكَذَا الْبَوَارِي لِاَنَّ الْحَائِطَ لَا. يُبْنَى لَهُمَا أَصْلًا حَتَّى لَوْ تَنَازَعَا فِي حَائِطِ وَلَا حَدِهِمَا عَلَيْهِ هَرَادِي وَلَيْسَ لِلْآخَرِ عَلَيْهِ شَيْءٌ فَهُوَ بَيْنَهُمَا وَلَوْ كَانَ لِكُلِّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا عَلَيْهِ جَدُوعَ ثَلَاثَةُ فَهُوَ بَيْنَهُمَا لِاسْتِوَائِهِمَا وَلَا مُعْتَبَرَ بِالْأَكْثَرِ مِنْهَا بَعْدَ الثَّلَاثَةِ
He said: If a wall belongs to a man and upon it there are beams (judu') or it is attached to his building, and the other has upon it water pipes (haradi), then it is for the owner of the beams/attachment, and the water pipes are nothing, because the owner of beams is the one using it and the other is merely attached. So it becomes like a beast they dispute over, where one has a load and the other has a hanging water skin. And by 'attachment' is meant the intermingling of bricks of his wall in it and his bricks in this wall, which is called 'tarbi' attachment. This is an apparent evidence for its owner because part of his building is upon this wall. And his statement 'water pipes are nothing' indicates that water pipes have no consideration at all. Similarly, mats (bawari) are like this, because a wall is not built for them originally. Even if they dispute over a wall and one has water pipes and the other has nothing, it is between them. And if each of them has three beams upon it, it is between them due to equality, and more than three is not considered.
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage covers disputes over a wall. The author analogizes to the earlier beast dispute: the one with beams (judu') or whose building is interlinked (ittisal) is the user (sahib isti'mal) like the load-bearer, while the one with water pipes (haradi) is merely attached (sahib ta'alluq) like the water skin holder. Therefore, the wall belongs to the beam/attachment owner. The commentary clarifies that haradi and mats (bawari) have no consideration because walls are not built for them. However, if one party has only haradi and the other has nothing, the wall is shared. If both have equal beams (three each), it is shared. Beams beyond three are not given extra weight. This shows careful balancing of evidence.

Key Terms
جذوع (judu'): Plural of jidh': beams of wood placed in a wall for building support.
هرادي (haradi): Water pipes or spouts fixed in a wall for drainage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a dispute over a wall, if one person has three beams and the other has three beams, how is the wall divided?
A) The first person gets it
B) The second gets it
C) They share equally
D) It is given to a third party

Key Takeaway
Wall ownership in Hanafi fiqh is determined by visible structural use (beams, interlocking bricks), not by minor attachments like water pipes or mats.

Equal Division of Shared Courtyard
Ruling on equal division of courtyard

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on division of a shared courtyard and explain why it is divided equally regardless of room count.

Core Idea
Courtyard usage is equal because both occupants pass through it equally.

This passage from the chapter on claims gives a clear ruling: when two people share a house but one has many rooms and the other has few, the courtyard is divided equally. The reason is that both have equal right to use the courtyard for passage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The passage describes a house with two occupants. One has ten rooms, the other has one room. The courtyard is shared.
2
State the ruling
The courtyard is divided equally (half each).
3
Explain the basis
The basis is equal usage: both occupants need to pass through the courtyard to reach their rooms. This usage is equal regardless of room count.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَإِذَا كَانَتْ دَارٌ مِنْهَا فِي يَدِ رَجُلٍ عَشَرَةُ آبَيَاتٍ وَفِي يَدِ اخَرَ بَيْتٌ فَالسَّاحَةُ بَيْنَهُمَا نِصْفَانِ لِإِسْتِوَائِهِمَا فِي اسْتِعْمَالِهَا وَهُوَ الْمُرُورُ فِيهَا
He said: And if there is a house in which ten rooms are in the possession of one man and one room is in the possession of another, then the courtyard is half between them due to their equality in its usage, which is passing through it.
Source pages p. 33

Commentary
This is a ruling from the chapter on claims. The author states that when two people share a house but one has ten rooms and the other one room, the courtyard is divided equally between them. The reason is that both have equal right to use the courtyard, specifically for passing through (al-murūr). The number of rooms is irrelevant because usage of the courtyard is shared. This is a straightforward ruling with no proof mentioned in the text.

Key Terms
الساحة (al-sāḥah): The courtyard or open area of a house shared by occupants.
المرور (al-murūr): Passing through; the right of passage as the basis for equal usage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) In proportion to the number of rooms (10:1)
B) Equally (half each)
C) The one with ten rooms gets the whole courtyard
D) According to the size of the rooms

Key Takeaway
The courtyard is divided equally between occupants regardless of room count because the right of passage is equal.

Three Types of Paternity Claims for a Slave-Girl's Child
Definition of three paternity claims.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between da'wa al-istīlād, da'wa al-tahrīr, and da'wa al-shubha, and state the legal effect of each.

Core Idea
Only a claim of istīlād makes the mother an umm walad.

This lesson introduces three categories of paternity claims that a master may make regarding a child born to his slave-girl. The distinction hinges on when the slave-girl came into the claimant's ownership relative to conception. Only one type — istīlād — carries the consequence that the mother becomes an umm walad, which invalidates her sale and secures her freedom upon the master's death.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three claims
Name the three types: da'wa al-istīlād, da'wa al-tahrīr, and da'wa al-shubha. Note the Arabic phrases.
Da'wa al-tahrīr is also called da'wa al-milk (ownership claim).
2
Determine the condition for each
For istīlād, conception must have occurred while the slave-girl was the claimant's property. For tahrīr, conception occurred before ownership. For shubha, the claimant is a father claiming his son's slave-girl's child, requiring continuous ownership by the son.
Shubha is a special exception based on close relationship.
3
State the legal effect
Istīlād makes the mother an umm walad and retroactively invalidates contracts of sale. Tahrīr does not establish umm walad and does not affect contracts. Shubha depends on the son's continued ownership.
Only istīlād has the strongest effect; the others are limited.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب ما يدعيه الرجلان.
فائدة دعوی کی تین قسمیں ہیں (۱) دعوئی استیلاد، (۲) دھوئی تحریر (جس کو دعوئی ملک بھی کہتے ہیں ) - دعوئی تحریر اس کو کہتے ہیں۔ کہ مدعی کا علوق غیر ملک مدعی میں ہو۔ یہ دعوہ اقرار ولی میں ہو۔ یہ دعوہ اقرار ولی کو متضمن نہیں ہوتا کیونکہ بوقت علوق ملک نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے استیل و غیر متصور ہے۔ اور نہ جاری شدہ عقود کو مسخ کرتا ہے۔ نیز اس کا نفاذ غیر ملک میں نہیں ہوتا۔ لان الحرية تقتصر على وقت الدعوة
دعوۃ شبہ یہ ہے کہ باپ اپنے بیٹے کی باندی کے بچہ کا مدعی ہو۔ اس کے لئے شرط یہ ہے کہ وقت علوق سے وقت دعوہ تک باند اور اس کے ولد میں بیٹے کی ملک قائم رہے۔
Chapter on what two men claim.
Benefit: Claims are of three types: (1) Claim of istīlād (claiming a child born to one's slave-girl), (2) Claim of tahrīr (claiming a child for emancipation, also called claim of ownership). Claim of tahrīr is when the claimant's [child] was conceived not in his ownership. This claim occurs in the acknowledgment of the guardian. This claim does not include acknowledgment of the guardian because at the time of conception, due to lack of ownership, istīlād is not conceivable. And it does not invalidate concluded contracts. Also its effect is not in non-ownership because freedom is confined to the time of the claim.
Claim of doubt (shubha) is when a father claims a child of his son's slave-girl. Its condition is that from the time of conception to the time of claim, the slave-girl and her child remain in the son's ownership.
Source pages p. 35

Commentary
This passage introduces the chapter on conflicting claims of paternity, specifically regarding children born to slave-girls who have been sold. The author defines three categories of such claims. The first is da'wa istīlād, where the claimant asserts that the child was conceived while the mother was his property, making the claimant the father and the mother an umm walad (mother of a child by her master), who cannot be sold. The second is da'wa tahrīr, where the child was conceived before the claimant owned the mother; this claim does not establish istīlād and does not retroactively affect contracts. The third is da'wa shubha, where the claimant is a father claiming the child of his son's slave-girl, contingent on the son's continuous ownership. These categories determine legal effects: only istīlād makes the mother an umm walad and invalidates her sale.

Key Terms
دعوی استیلاد (da'wa al-istīlād): Claim that a child born to a slave-girl was conceived while she was the claimant's property, establishing the child's paternity and making the mother an umm walad.
دعوی تحریر (da'wa al-tahrīr): Claim of paternity when conception occurred outside the claimant's ownership, not establishing istīlād and only affecting the child's freedom.
دعوی شبہ (da'wa al-shubha): A paternity claim based on a close relationship, e.g., a father claiming his son's slave-girl's child, requiring continuous ownership of the son.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which type of paternity claim retroactively invalidates the sale of a slave-girl?
A) Da'wa al-istīlād
B) Da'wa al-tahrīr
C) Da'wa al-shubha
D) All of the above

Key Takeaway
A paternity claim for a slave-girl's child must be classified by ownership at conception: only istīlād creates umm walad.

Child Claimed as Son vs Slave
Ruling on a child claimed by both a Muslim and a Christian

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a child is claimed as a son by a Christian and as a slave by a Muslim, and explain why the claim of lineage prevails over a claim of ownership.

Core Idea
A claim of lineage overrides a claim of ownership in Hanafi law.

In a case where a child is in the joint possession of a Muslim and a Christian, the Muslim claims the child as his slave, while the Christian claims him as his son. The Hidayah gives a clear ruling: the child is declared the son of the Christian and is free. This ruling illustrates a foundational Hanafi principle—lineage, when plausibly established, takes precedence over mere possession or claims of property. Understanding this principle is essential for distinguishing between valid and invalid claims over a person in Islamic law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and claims
Note the two claimants: a Muslim who claims the child as his slave (ghulam) and a Christian who claims the child as his son (ibn). The child is in their joint possession.
The Muslim's claim is based on ownership; the Christian's claim is based on paternity.
2
State the ruling
The text rules that the child is the Christian's son and is free. The Muslim's claim of slavery is rejected.
The ruling is definitive: the child is not a slave.
3
Identify the legal basis
The ruling rests on the principle that a claim of lineage (nasab) takes precedence over a claim of slavery. A free person cannot be enslaved, and the Christian's claim of paternity establishes the child's freedom.
The child's freedom is a direct consequence of the established lineage.
4
Consider the practical effect
The child is free and attributed to the Christian father. The Muslim loses any claim over the child.
This outcome protects the child from wrongful enslavement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بچہ مسلمان اور نصرانی کے قبضہ میں ہو ، نصرانی نے کہا کہ یہ میرا بیٹا ہے، مسلمان نے کہا یہ میر اغلام ہے وہ نصرانی کا بیٹا ہوگا اور آزاد ہوگا قَالَ وَإِذَا كَانَ الصَّبِيُّ فِي يَدِ مُسْلِمٍ وَنَصْرَانِي فَقَالَ النَّصْرَانِيُّ هُوَ ابْنِي وَقَالَ الْمُسْلِمُ هُوَ عَبْدِي فَهُوَ إِبْنُ
A child is in the possession of a Muslim and a Christian. The Christian says 'he is my son' and the Muslim says 'he is my slave'. He is the son of the Christian and will be free. He (the author) said: If a child is in the hand of a Muslim and a Christian, and the Christian says he is my son, and the Muslim says he is my slave, then he is the son...
Source pages p. 43

Commentary
This is a ruling statement from the matn of the Hidayah. The case involves a child who is in the joint possession of a Muslim and a Christian. The Christian claims the child is his son, while the Muslim claims the child is his slave. The ruling is that the child is declared to be the son of the Christian and is free. The basis for this ruling is that the Christian's claim of lineage (nasab) establishes the child's freedom, as a free person cannot be a slave. The Muslim's claim of slavery is overridden by the Christian's claim of paternity. This ruling reflects the Hanafi principle that lineage, when established, takes precedence over property claims. The Arabic text is the beginning of the matn from the Hidayah, part of the chapter on claims between two men. The implication is that the child's freedom is recognized, and the Muslim's claim of ownership is invalid. This ruling is consistent with the Hanafi position that a child's lineage, if plausibly established, prevails over claims of slavery.

Key Terms
نصرانی (nasrani): A Christian; a non-Muslim person of the Christian faith.
غلام (ghulam): Slave; a male slave. In this context, claimed by the Muslim as his property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway

Child Claimed by Muslim and Christian: Ruling Based on Benefit
Ruling on a child in custody of a Muslim and a Christian with conflicting claims

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a Muslim claims a child as his slave and a Christian claims him as his son, and explain the reasoning based on istihsan (juristic preference).

Core Idea
Child given to Christian as free son: immediate freedom and eventual Islam outweigh immediate Islam with slavery.

This ruling from Al-Hidayah addresses a conflict of claims over a child between a Muslim and a Christian. The Hanafi school applies istihsan (juristic preference) to prioritize the child's welfare, even though Islam is generally preferred. We will examine the reasoning and the response to an objection based on Quran 2:221.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conflicting claims
The Muslim claims the child as his slave; the Christian claims him as his son. Both are in possession of the child.
2
State the Hanafi ruling
The child is declared the Christian's son and is free. The Muslim's claim of slavery is rejected.
3
Identify the dalil (proof) for the ruling
The ruling is based on istihsan (juristic preference) derived from the principle of nazar (consideration for the child's best interest).
Dalil is rational, not a direct text.
4
Analyze the benefit (nazar)
Giving the child to the Christian as a free son gives him immediate freedom and eventual Islam (since proofs of tawhid are apparent). The opposite would give immediate Islam only as a follower (of the owner) and lifelong slavery.
Freedom cannot be acquired later, but Islam can be embraced later.
5
Address the objection from Quran 2:221
The verse 'a believing slave is better than a polytheist' suggests the Muslim's claim should prevail. The Hanafi response: the verse is overridden by hadiths emphasizing the child's welfare, and the two claims are not directly comparable because one is for sonship, the other for ownership.
The principle of tarjih (preponderance) is applied: the child's overall benefit outweighs the immediate religious advantage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب ما يدعيه الرجـ اشرف الہدایہ جلد - یازدهم .. النَّصْرَانِي وَهُوَ حُرِّ لَانَّ الْإِسْلَامَ مُرَجَحٌ فَيَسْتَدْعِي تَعَارُضًا وَلَا تَعَارُضَ لِاَنَّ نَظَرَ الصَّبِيِّ فِي هَذَا أَوْفَرُ لَهُ لِأَنَّهُ يَنَالُ شَرَقَ الْحُرِّيَّةِ حَالًا وَشَرَفَ الْإِسْلَامِ مَالًا إِذْ دَلَائِلُ الْوَحْدَانِيَّةِ ظَاهِرَةً وَفِي عَكْسِهِ الْحُكْمُ بِالْإِسْلَامِ تَبَعًا وَحِرْمَانُهُ عَنِ الْحُرِّيَّةِ لِأَنَّهُ لَيْسَ فِي وُسْعِهِ اِكْتَسَابُهَا وَلَوْ كَانَتْ دَعْوَتُهُمَا دَعْوَةُ البُنوَةِ فَالْمُسْلِمُ أَولَى تَرْجِيْحًا لِلْإِسْلَامِ وَهُوَ أَوْفَرُ النَّظَرَيْنِ

ترجمہ اگر کوئی بچہ ایک مسلمان اور ایک نصرانی کے قبضہ میں ہو۔ نصرانی ہے کہ یہ میرا بیٹا ہے اور مسلم کہے کہ میرا غلام ہے تو وہ نصرانی کا بیٹا ہوگا۔ اور آزاد ہو گا۔ کیونکہ اسلام مرجح ہوتا ہے۔ اور مرجح ہونا مقتضی تعارض ہوتا ہے اور یہاں کوئی تعارض نہیں۔ اس لئے کہ اس میں بچہ کے لئے پوری نظر شفقت ہے۔ کیونکہ وہ فی الحال شرف آزادی اور انجام کار شرف اسلام حاصل کرے گا۔ اس لئے کہ دلائل وحدانیت خوب واضح ہیں اور اس کے عکس کی صورت میں اسلام کا حکم تبعا ہے اور شرف آزادی سے محروم ہونا ہے۔ کیونکہ آزادی حاصل کرنا اس کے اختیار میں نہیں ہے۔ اور اگر ان دونوں کا دعوئی بیٹا ہونے کا ہو تو مسلمان اولی ہے۔ اسلام کو ترجیح دیتے ہوئے اور دو شفقتوں میں سے یہی وافر شفقت ہے۔

تشریح قوله واذا كان الصبي الخ کوئی بچہ ایک مسلمان اور ایک نصرانی کے قبضہ میں ہے ۔ اب نصرانی کہتا ہے ۔ کہ یہ میرا بیٹا ہے اور مسلمان کہتا ہے کہ یہ میرا غلام ہے تو وہ نصرانی کا بیٹا قرار دیا جائے گا اور آزاد ہوگا۔ وجہ یہ ہے کہ اسلام ہر موقع پر مر ج ہوتا ہے۔ لیکن مرجح ہونے کے لئے کوئی تعارض ہونا چاہیئے اور یہاں کوئی تعارض نہیں ہے۔ اس واسطے کہ نصرانی کا بیٹا بنانے اور آزاد قرار دینے میں بچہ کے لئے شفقت زیادہ ہے کہ فی الحال تو وہ آزادی کا شرف پا رہا ہے اور انجام کار اسلام کا شرف حاصل کرلے گا۔ کیونکہ دلائل وحدانیت خوب واضح ہیں۔ اور اس کے بر عکس کے جائے یعنی مسلمان کا غلام قرار دیا جائے تو وہ اپنے آقا کے تابع ہو کر فی الحال اسلام کے حکم میں تو داخل ہو جائے گا لیکن آزادی سے محروم ہوگا ۔ کیونکہ آزادی حاصل کرنا اس کے اختیار میں نہیں ہے۔ اور اگر وہ دونوں بیٹا ہونے کا دعوی کروں تو مسلمان کو تر جیح ہوگی کہ اسلام راج ہے ۔ تنبیہ نصرانی کا بیٹا قرار دینے پر یہ اعتراض ہوتا ہے کہ یہ قول باری و بعبد مؤمن خیر من مشرک کے خلاف ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ اسی پر دال ہے کہ عید مومن گو غلام ہو مشرک سے بہتر ہے اگر چہ آزاد ہو۔ رہے دلائل تو حید سووہ اگر چہ ظاہر ہیں۔ تاہم دین سے الفت و انسیت مانع قوی ہے۔ جواب یہ کہ آیت " ادعوهم لا باهم" آباء کے لئے دعوہ اولاد کی موجب ہے اور مدعی نسب باپ ہے۔ کیونکہ اس کا دعوہ حمل نقض نہیں ہے۔ پس دونوں آیتیں متعارض ہو گئیں۔ پھر جو احادیث بچوں کے حق میں نظر و شفقت پر دال ہیں وہ بکثرت ہیں۔ فكانت اقوى من المانع (عنایہ )
The Christian, and he is free, because Islam is a preponderant factor, so it requires a conflict, and there is no conflict because the consideration for the child in this is more beneficial for him, since he attains the honor of freedom immediately and the honor of Islam eventually, as proofs of monotheism are apparent. In the opposite case, the ruling is Islam as a follower and deprivation of freedom because it is not within his capacity to acquire it. If both claims were for sonship, then the Muslim is more worthy, preferring Islam, and that is the more abundant consideration.
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof from the Hanafi school regarding a child held by both a Muslim and a Christian. The Christian claims the child is his son, while the Muslim claims him as his slave. The ruling is that the child is declared the Christian's son and is free. The reasoning is based on giving the child the maximum benefit: he gains immediate freedom and, eventually, will likely embrace Islam since the proofs of monotheism are clear. If the opposite were given (child becomes Muslim's slave), he would gain Islam only secondarily and lose freedom, which he cannot later acquire. The text addresses an objection based on the Quranic verse 'a believing slave is better than a polytheist' by citing the hadith 'call them by their fathers' and the abundant hadiths giving preference to the child's welfare. Thus, Hanafi istihsan (juristic preference) outweighs the literal application of the verse.

Key Terms
صبي (sabi): A minor child, male or female, who has not reached puberty.
مرجح (murajjih): That which gives preponderance; here, Islam is considered a preponderant factor in legal decisions.
نظر (nazar): Consideration or beneficial care; here, the child's best interest.
دعوة البنوة (da'wat al-bunuwwah): Claim of sonship, i.e., that the child is one's son.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway

intermediate
8 min
Conditions for a Married Woman's Claim of Motherhood
Ruling on married woman's claim of motherhood with proof from hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a married woman's claim of motherhood is accepted and identify the evidentiary ruling of the midwife's testimony.

Core Idea
A married woman's claim of motherhood requires a female witness to the birth; the midwife's testimony alone suffices.

This lesson examines the first scenario from the passage: a married woman claiming a child as her own. The Hanafi school requires her to produce a female witness to the birth. Why the difference from a man's claim? Because she seeks to impose lineage on her husband, while a man takes lineage upon himself. The proof is the Prophet's acceptance of the midwife's testimony.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the condition
Recognize that a married woman's claim of motherhood is not accepted without a female witness to the birth. The act is a legal claim (da'wa), and the condition is testimony of birth.
The witness can be a midwife (qabila).
2
Distinguish between woman and man
A woman imposes lineage on another (her husband), so evidence is required. A man imposes lineage on himself, so his claim is accepted without evidence.
This is a key principle: who bears the obligation of proof.
3
Analyze the dalil
The proof is a hadith from Sunan al-Daraqutni that the Prophet accepted the testimony of a midwife for birth. This shows that a single female witness suffices for establishing the fact of birth.
The need is only to identify the child; lineage is then established by the marital bed (firash).
4
Note the intra-Hanafi detail for a woman in iddah
If the woman is in iddah (waiting period after divorce or death), Abu Hanifa requires complete proof (two men or one man and two women) unless the pregnancy is visible or the husband acknowledges.
This is a stricter view; other scholars (mashayikh) did not address this specifically.
5
Conclude the mufta bihi
For a married woman not in iddah, one female witness to birth is sufficient. For a woman in iddah, the relied-upon view is that of Abu Hanifa requiring complete proof.
The mufta bihi follows Abu Hanifa's position for iddah.

قَالَ وَإِذَا ادَّعَتْ اِمْرَأَةٌ صَبِيًّا أَنَّهُ إِبْنُهَا لَمْ يَجُزُ دَعْوَاهَا حَتَّى تَشْهَدَ امْرَأَةٌ عَلَى الْوِلَادَةِ وَمَعْنَى الْمَسْأَلَةِ أَنْ يَكُونَ الْمَرْأَةُ ذَاتَ زَوْجِ لِأَنَّهَا تَدَّعِي تَحْمِيلَ النَسَبِ عَلَى الْغَيْرِ فَلَا تُصَدَّقُ إِلَّا بِحُجَّةٍ بِخِلَافِ الرَّجُلِ لِأَنَّهُ يُحَمِّلُ نَفْسَهُ النَسَبَ ثُمَّ شَهَادَةُ الْقَابِلَةِ كَافِيَةٌ فِيهَا لِاَنَّ الْحَاجَّةِ إِلَى تَعْيِينِ الْوَلَدِ أَمَّا النَسَبُ يَثْبُتُ بِالْفِرَاشِ الْقَائِمِ وَقَدْ سَجَّ أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ قَبِلَ شَهَادَةَ الْقَابِلَةِ عَلَى الْوِلَادَةِ وَلَوْ كَانَتْ مُعْتَدَّةً فَلَابُدَّ مِنْ حُجَّةٍ تَامَّةٍ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةٌ وَقَدْ مَرَّ فِى الطَّلَاقِ وَإِنْ لَمْ تَكُنْ مَنْكُوحَةٌ وَلَا مُعْتَدَّةً قَالُوا يَثْبُتُ النَسَبَ مِنْهَا بِقَوْلِهَا لَانَّ فِيهِ الْزَامًا علَى نَفْسِهَا دُونَ غَيْرِهَا وَإِنْ كَانَ لَهَا زَوْجٌ وَزَعِمَتْ أَنَّهُ إِبْتُهَا مِنْهُ وَصَدَّقَهَا الزَّوْجُ فَهُوَ إِبْنُهُمَا وَإِنْ لَمْ تَشْهَدُ إِبْنُهُ مِنْ غَيْرِهَا امْرَأَةٌ لِأَنَّهُ الْتَزَمَ نَسبَه فَاعْنى ذلِكَ عَنِ الْحُجَّةِ وَإِنْ كَانَ الصَّبِيُّ فِي اَيْدِيهِمَا وَ رَعِمَ الزر bes وَزَعِمَت أَنَّهُ إِبْنُهَا مِنْ غَيْرِهِ فَهُوَ إِبْنُهُمَا لِاَنَّ الظَّاهِرَ أَنَّ الْوَلَدَ مِنْهُمَا لِقِيَامِ أَيْدِيهِمَا أَوْ لِقِيَامِ الْفَرَاشِ بَيْنَهُمَا كُلُّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا يُرِيدُ إِبْطَالَ حَقِ صَاحِبِهِ فَلَا يُصَدَّقُ عَلَيْهِ وَهُوَ نَظِيرُ ثَوْبِ فِي يَدِ رَجُلَيْنِ يَقُولُ كُلُّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا هُوَ بَيْنِي وَبَيْنَ رَجُلٍ آخَرَ غَيْرَ صَاحِبِهِ يَكُونُ التَّوبُ بَيْنَهُمَا إِلَّا أَنَّ هَنَاكَ يَدْخُلُ الْمُقَرُّ لَهُ فِي نَصِيْبِ لْمُقَرِّ لَاتَ الْمَحَلَ يَحْتَمِلُ الشَّرُكَةَ وَههُنَا لَا يَدْخُلُ لِاَنَّ النَّسَبَ لَا يَحْتَمِلُهَا

ترجمہ ایک عورت نے بچہ کی بابت دعوی کیا۔ کہ یہ میرا بیٹا ہے تو اس کا دعوئی جائز نہ ہوگا۔ یہاں تک کہ ایک عورت پیدائش پر گواہی دے۔ مسئلہ کے معنی یہ ہیں کہ عورت شوہر والی ہے کیونکہ وہ نسب کو غیر پر ڈالنے کا دعوی کر رہی ہے تو حجت کے بغیر تصدیق نہیں کی جائے گی۔ بخلاف مرد کے کہ وہ نسب کو خود پر ڈالتا ہے۔ پھر اس میں دایہ کی شہادت کافی ہے۔ کیونکہ ضرورت صرف بچہ کے معین کرنے میں ہے۔ رہا نسب سو وہ فراش سے ثابت ہو جائے گا۔ جو فی الحال قائم ہے۔ اور یہ صیح ثابت ہے کہ حضور علیہ السلام نے پیدائش پر دایہ کی گواہی قبول فرمائی۔ اور وہ عورت معتدہ ہو تو پوری حجت ضروری ہے۔ امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک اور یہ کتاب الطلاق میں گزر چکا۔ اور اگر نہ منکوحہ ہو نہ معتدہ۔ تو مشائخ نے کہا ہے کہ عورت سے بچہ کا نسب صرف اس کے کہنے ہی سے ثابت ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ اس میں خود پر لازم کرنا ہے نہ کہ غیر پر۔ اور اگر اس کا کوئی شوہر ہو اور وہ یہ کہے کہ یہ لڑکا میرا اسی شوہر سے ہے اور شوہر اس کی تصدیق کرے تو وہ ان دونوں کا بیٹا ہو گا۔ اگر چہ کوئی عورت گواہی نہ دے۔ کیونکہ شوہر نے اس کے نسب کا التزام کرلیا اس نے حجت سے بے نیاز کر دیا اور اگر بچہ دونوں کے قبضہ میں ہو۔ اور شوہر کہے کہ یہ بچہ میرا بیٹا اس عورت کے علاوہ سے ہے اور عورت کہے کہ وہ میرا بیٹا اس شوہر کے علاوہ سے ہے تو وہ ان دونوں کا بیٹا ہوگا کیونکہ ظاہر یہی ہے کہ بچہ ان دونوں سے ہے ان دونوں کا قبضہ یا ان کا نکاحی فراش قائم ہونے کی وجہ سے اس کے بعد ان میں سے ہر ایک دوسرے کا حق مٹانا چاہتا ہے۔ تو تصدیق نہیں کی جائے گی۔ اور یہ اس کپڑے کی نظیر ہے۔ جو دو شخصوں کے قبضہ میں ہو۔ اور ان میں سے ہر ایک یہ کہتا ہے۔ کہ یہ میرے اور فلاں کے درمیان مشترک ہے۔ تو کپڑا ان دونوں میں مشترک ہوگا۔ صرف اتنی بات ہے کہ کپڑے کے مسئلہ میں مقررہ مقر کے حصہ میں داخل ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ محل قابل شرکت ہے اور یہاں داخل نہ ہوگا کیونکہ نسب محتمل شرکت نہیں ہے۔

تشریح... قوله واذا ادعت ایک عورت نے دعوی کیا کہ یہ بچہ میرا بیٹا ہے تو جب تک ایک عورت ولادت پر گواہی نہ دے اس کا دعوئی جائز نہ ہوگا۔ صاحب ہدایہ عام مشائخ کی پیروی کرتے ہوئے فرماتے ہیں۔ کہ اس مسئلہ میں یہ قید ہے کہ وہ عورت شوہر والی ہو اور شوہر اس بچہ کا انکار کرتا ہو۔ کیونکہ عورت شوہر پر نسب لازم کرنا چاہتی ہے۔ اور الزام کے لئے حجت ضروری ہے۔ اور لزوم نسب کا سب یعنی نکاح کو قائم ہے۔ لیکن ضرورت اثبات ولادت کی ہے۔ اور نکاح موجب ولادت نہیں ہے۔ تو بلا حجت عورت کے قول کی تصدیق نہ ہوگی۔ بخلاف مرد کے کہ وہ نسب کو خود اپنے معین کرنے کی ہے۔ کہ اس کو اسی عورت نے بجتا ہے۔ رہا اس کا نسب سوہ تو فراش کی وجہ سے ثابت ہو جائے گا۔ جو فی الحال موجود ہے۔ اور یہ بات حدیث سے ثابت ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے دایہ کی گواہی کو جائز رکھا ہے۔ چنانچہ دار قطنی نے سنن میں حضرت حذیفہ سے روایت کی ہے۔ " ان النبی صلى الله عليه وسلّم اجاز شهادة القابلة

قوله ول كانت معندة .... اور اگر وہ عورت معتدہ ہو یعنی طلاق یا وفات کی عدت میں ہو تو امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک حجت نامہ ضروری ہے۔ یعنی دو مردوں یا ایک مرد اور دو عورتوں کی گواہی ضروری ہے۔ الا یہ کہ حمل ظاہر یا شوہر کی طرف سے اعتراف ہو کہ اس صورت میں نسب بلا شہادت ثابت ہو جائے گا۔ اور اگر وہ منکوحہ یا معتدہ نہ ہوتو بقول مشائخ بچہ کا نسب صرف عورت کے کہنے ہی سے ثابت ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ اس صورت میں عورت خود اپنے اوپر لازم کر رہی ہے نہ کہ غیر پر۔
He said: When a woman claims a child is her son, her claim is not permissible until a woman testifies to the birth. The meaning of the case is that the woman is married, because she seeks to impose lineage on another, so she is not believed without evidence, unlike a man because he imposes lineage on himself. Then the testimony of the midwife is sufficient in this because the need is only to identify the child; as for lineage, it is established by the existing marital bed. And it is confirmed that the Prophet (peace be upon him) accepted the testimony of the midwife for birth. If she is in iddah, then a complete proof is necessary according to Abu Hanifa, and this has passed in the chapter on divorce. If she is neither married nor in iddah, they (the scholars) said: lineage is established from her by her statement alone because it entails an obligation on herself and not on others. If she has a husband and she claims it is her son from him and the husband confirms her, then it is their son even if no woman testifies, because he undertook his lineage, so that suffices instead of proof. If the child is in their hands and the husband claims it is his son from someone else and she claims it is her son from someone else, then it is their son because the apparent is that the child is from both of them due to their possession or due to the marital bed between them; each of them wants to invalidate the other's right, so they are not believed. This is analogous to a cloth in the hands of two men, each saying it is between me and another man not the other, so the cloth is between them, except that there the acknowledged person enters into the share of the acknowledger because the subject admits partnership, but here he does not enter because lineage does not admit it.
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This passage presents a comprehensive ruling with proof regarding a woman's claim of motherhood. The text first addresses a married woman: her claim that a child is her son is not accepted without a female witness to the birth. The reason is that she is imposing lineage on her husband (and the child), so evidence is required. In contrast, a man's claim of paternity is accepted without such evidence because he takes the lineage upon himself. The proof for accepting a midwife's testimony is a hadith from Sunan al-Daraqutni that the Prophet accepted the testimony of a midwife for birth. The child's lineage is then established by the marital bed (firash). Next, the text covers a woman in iddah: according to Abu Hanifa, she needs complete proof (two men or one man and two women) unless the pregnancy is visible or the husband acknowledges. If the woman is neither married nor in iddah, the scholars say her word alone establishes lineage because she only imposes on herself. When both spouses claim the child is from the other parent, the child is attributed to both because the apparent condition (possession or marriage) supports that, and each is trying to negate the other's right. A qiyas (analogy) is drawn to a cloth in the hands of two men who each claim it is shared with a third person; the cloth remains shared between the two holders. However, in the cloth case, the third party enters into the share of the acknowledger because property admits partnership, whereas lineage does not admit partnership. This demonstrates the Hanafi method of using analogy while respecting the unique nature of lineage.

Key Terms
دعوى (da'wa): A legal claim, specifically a woman's claim that a child is her son.
قابلة (qabila): Midwife; a female birth attendant whose testimony is accepted for establishing birth.
فراش (firash): Marital bed; the legal basis for establishing paternity to the husband.
نسب (nasab): Lineage; the legal relationship of parentage.
إلتزام (iltizam): Undertaking or acceptance; here, the husband's acceptance of the child's lineage removes the need for proof.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the required evidence for a married woman's claim of motherhood according to the Hanafi school?
A) Two male witnesses
B) One female witness to the birth
C) Her husband's confirmation
D) No evidence is required

Key Takeaway
A married woman's claim of motherhood requires a female witness to the birth; the midwife's testimony is accepted based on prophetic practice.

Unmarried Woman, Husband's Confirmation, and Conflicting Claims
Rulings on unmarried woman, husband's confirmation, and conflicting claims with qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rulings for an unmarried woman's claim of motherhood, husband's confirmation, and conflicting claims between spouses, and explain the qiyas to cloth sharing.

Core Idea
An unmarried woman's word alone establishes maternity; husband's confirmation removes all proof; conflicting claims result in child being attributed to both based on apparent possession.

This lesson covers three remaining scenarios from the passage: a woman without a husband (or in iddah) can establish lineage by her word alone because she only imposes on herself; if the husband confirms her claim, that removes the need for any proof; and if both spouses claim the child is from a third person (each denying the other), the child is attributed to both because each is trying to negate the other's right. The qiyas to a shared cloth illustrates how conflicting claims cancel each other, leaving the apparent state intact.

Guided Path
1
Unmarried woman: identify the ruling
If the woman is neither married nor in iddah, her word alone establishes the child's lineage. The reason is that she is imposing the obligation on herself, not on another.
The scholars (mashayikh) are the source of this position.
2
Husband's confirmation: understand iltizam
If the husband confirms the woman's claim that the child is from him, the child is attributed to both spouses without any witness. The husband's acceptance (iltizam) of the lineage suffices.
This applies even if the woman is married and no birth witness exists.
3
Conflicting claims: analyze the scenario
If both spouses have custody of the child and each claims the child is from someone else (not from the other spouse), then the child is attributed to both. The apparent condition (possession or marital bed) supports that the child is from them, and each is trying to invalidate the other's right, so they are not believed.
The child is not attributed to the third parties mentioned in their claims.
4
Study the qiyas analogy
The ruling is analogous to a cloth held by two men, each claiming it is shared with a third person (not the other holder). The cloth is shared between the two holders. However, in the cloth case, the third person enters into the share because property admits partnership (shirka), but in lineage, the third person does not enter because lineage does not admit partnership.
The analogy is limited to the principle that conflicting claims cancel each other.
5
Identify the legal principle
The underlying principle: when two parties each claim a right that excludes the other, their claims cancel each other, leaving the apparent state (possession or marriage) as the basis for the ruling.
This principle is used in other fiqh areas as well.
