Iqrar with 'Shay': Specification of Value Required
Defines what must be specified when using ambiguous terms like 'shay'' or 'haqq'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for iqrar using ambiguous terms and apply the condition that the specified item must have value.

Core Idea
In iqrar, 'shay'' must be specified as valuable; otherwise, it is retraction.

When someone says 'I owe so-and-so something (shay'),' the law requires clarity. The Hanafi school holds that the item specified must have monetary value, because the word 'ala (upon) implies an obligation, and only valuable things can be obligatory in the dhimmah. This lesson unpacks the ruling, its proof, and the scholarly disagreements surrounding valueless specifications.

Guided Path
1
State the rule for iqrar with 'shay''
Identify that the confessor must specify an item with value. If he specifies something worthless, it is considered a retraction.
The rule also applies to terms like 'haqq' and 'ghasb'.
2
Identify the proof (talil)
The proof is linguistic: 'ala indicates obligation, and only valuable items can be obligatory in the dhimmah. The text states: 'because he informed of obligation in his dhimmah, and what has no value is not obligatory.'
This is a rational proof (talil) based on the nature of obligation.
3
Apply to valueless items
If the confessor specifies a single grain of wheat or other worthless item, the specification is invalid and amounts to retraction from the iqrar.
The iqrar remains valid only if the specification is valuable; otherwise, the original iqrar is void.
4
Examine the intra-Hanafi disputes
The text mentions disagreements: (a) if the confessor claims he intended 'right of Islam,' the three Imams reject it in both separated and connected statements; (b) scholars of Transoxiana reject specification of carrion, vinegar, or wine, while scholars of Iraq accept it.
The mufta bihi follows the Transoxiana view, which is also supported by Malik and al-Shafi'i.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position: specification must be of a valuable item; if not, it is retraction. The claim of intending 'right of Islam' is not accepted.
This is consistent with the zahir al-riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ فَإِنْ قَالَ لِفُلَانٍ عَلَى شَيْءٌ لَزِمَهُ أَنْ يُبَيِّنَ مَالَهُ قِيْمَةً لِأَنَّهُ أَخْبَرَ عَنِ الْوُجُوبِ فِي ذِمَّتِهِ وَمَا لَا قِيْمَةَ لَهُ لَا يَجِبُ فِيْهَا فَإِذَا بَيَّنَ غَيْرَ ذَالِكَ يَكُونُ رُجُوعًا قَالَ وَالْقَوْلُ قَوْلُهُ مَعَ يَمِينِهِ إِنْ ادَّعَى الْمُقَرُّ لَهُ اَكْثَرَ مِنْ ذَالِكَ لِأَنَّهُ هُوَ الْمُنْكَرُ فِيْهِ وَكَذَا إِذَا قَالَ لِفُلَانِ عَلَى حَقُّ لَمَّا بَيْنَا وَكَذَا لَوْ قَالَ غَصَبْتُ مِنْهُ شَيْئًا وَيَجِبُ اَنْ يُبَيِّنَ مَا هُوَ مَالٌ يَجْرِي فِيهِ التَّمَانُعِ تَعْوِيلًا عَلَى الْعَادَةِ
ترجمہ پس اگر اس نے کہا کہ مجھ پر فلاں کی کچھ چیز ہے تو اس کو ایسی چیز بیان کرنا لازم ہوگا۔ جس کی کچھ قیمت ہے ی ہے۔ کیونکہ اس نے اپنے ذمہ واجب ہونے کی خبر دی ہے۔ اور جس کی کچھ قیمت نہ ہو وہ ذمہ میں واجب نہیں ہوتی ۔ مپس جب وہ اس کے علاوہ بیان کرے تو اقرار سے پھرنا ہوگا اور قول اس کا معتبر ہوگا۔ اس کی قسم کے ساتھ اگر مقرلہ اس سے زیادہ کا دعوی کرے۔ کیونکہ منکر وہی ہے۔ اسی طرح اگر اس نے کہا کہ فلاں کا مجھ پر حق ہے یا کہا کہ میں نے اس سے کچھ چیز غصب کرلی تو ایسی چیز بیان کرنا ضروری ہے جو مال ہو اور اس میں با ہم روک جاری ہو عادت پر اعتماد کرتے ہوئے۔
تشریح قوله لفلان على شئى. لفلان على شئی کہنے میں شئی کا بیان ایسی چیز سے ضروری ہوگا جو قیمتی ہو ۔گو کمتر ہو۔ کیونکہ لفظ علی ایجاب و الزام کے لئے ہوتا ہے۔ اور جس چیز کی کوئی قیمت نہ ہو وہ آدمی کے ذمہ واجب نہیں ہوتی۔ پس اگر اس نے یہ بیان کیا کہ گیہوں کا ایک دانہ ہے تو صحیح نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ یہ تو اقرار سے رجوع کرنا ہے۔ محیط میں ہے۔ کہ اگر مقریہ کہے کہ میں نے حق اسلام کا ارادہ کیا ہے تو اس کی تصدیق نہ ہوگی۔ (جب کہ مفصولاً کہا ہو۔ اگر موصولاً کہا تو تصدیق کی جائے گی۔ ائمہ ثلاثہ کے نزدیک دونوں صورتوں میں تصدیق نہ ہوگی ) ۔ اور اگر مردہ یا اسور یا شراب مراد لیا تو مشائخ ماوراء انہر کے نزدیک تصدیق نہ ہوگی۔ کیونکہ ان چیزوں کی کوئی قیمت نہیں۔ ایک وجہ میں امام مالک و شافعی اسی کے قائل ہیں۔ اور مشائخ عراق کے نزدیک تصدیق کی جائے گی۔ اور اگر یہ کہا کہ ایک پیسہ مراد ہے تو تصدیق ہوگی۔
He said: If he says 'I owe something (shay') to so-and-so,' he must specify something that has value, because he informed of obligation in his dhimmah, and what has no value is not obligatory. If he specifies something else, it is retraction. He said: His word is accepted with his oath if the confesstee claims more than that, because he is the denier. Similarly, if he says 'I have a right (haqq)' upon so-and-so' as we mentioned, and similarly if he says 'I usurped something from him,' he must specify something that is wealth (mal) in which exchange occurs, based on custom.
Translation: So if he said 'I owe so-and-so something (shay'),' he must specify something that has value, even if little, because he informed of an obligation in his dhimmah, and what has no value is not obligatory. So if he specifies something else, it is retraction from the iqrar, and his word is accepted with his oath if the confesstee claims more, because he is the denier. Similarly, if he said 'so-and-so has a right upon me' or 'I usurped something from him,' he must specify something that is wealth (mal) in which mutual prohibition occurs, based on custom.
Commentary: His statement 'li-fulan 'alayya shay'' – in saying 'I owe so-and-so something,' the thing must be specified as something valuable, even if little. Because the word 'ala indicates obligation and binding, and what has no value is not obligatory in the dhimmah. If he specifies a single grain of wheat, it is not valid, as that would be retraction from the iqrar. In al-Muhit: if the mukarr (the one making iqrar) says 'I intended the right of Islam,' his statement is not accepted (if said separately; if said connectedly, it is accepted according to the three Imams, both are not accepted). And if he meant a dead animal, or vinegar, or wine, then according to the scholars of Transoxiana it is not accepted, because these things have no value. Imam Malik and al-Shafi'i agree on one view. According to the scholars of Iraq, it would be accepted. If he says he meant a single coin (paisa), it is accepted.
Source pages p. 51

Commentary
This passage clarifies the ruling when a person uses the word 'shay'' (something) in an iqrar. The person must specify something that has a monetary value, even if minimal. The reason is that the word 'ala (upon) implies an obligation, and only valuable items can be obligatory in the dhimmah. If he specifies something worthless, it is considered a retraction from the iqrar, and his word is not accepted; rather, it is a return. The same applies if he uses the word 'haqq' (right) or says 'I usurped something' – he must specify an item that is considered wealth (mal) in which transactions occur, based on custom. The commentary then discusses particular cases: if he says he intended 'the right of Islam' (i.e., religious duty), it is not accepted unless he said it in one breath (muwasulan) according to some, but the three Imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) reject it in both cases. If he meant something valueless like carrion, vinegar, or wine, the scholars of Transoxiana reject it, while the scholars of Iraq accept it. If he meant a coin (paisa), it is accepted because it has value.

Key Terms
شىء (shay'): An unspecified thing; in iqrar, it must be interpreted as something valuable.
علی ('ala): Preposition indicating obligation or liability in iqrar context.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If someone says 'I owe so-and-so something (shay')' and then specifies 'a grain of wheat,' why is this not accepted?
A) Because wheat is not wealth.
B) Because a single grain has no value and specifying it is retraction.
C) Because 'shay'' cannot be used for food.
D) Because the iqrar was invalid from the start.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, an iqrar with 'shay'' requires the specified item to have value; otherwise, it is a retraction.

Iqrar with 'Mal' and 'Mal 'Azim': Minimum Thresholds and Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf
Intra-Hanafi dispute on minimum thresholds for iqrar of wealth terms.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on iqrar with 'mal' and 'mal 'azim', identify the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf regarding the minimum for 'mal 'azim', and apply the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Iqrar of 'mal' requires at least one dirham; 'mal 'azim' requires the zakat nisab of 200 dirhams.

When someone makes an iqrar (judicial confession) using the vague term 'mal', the confessor's specification is generally accepted, but custom excludes less than one dirham. For 'mal 'azim', the description 'great' demands a defined threshold. The Hanafi school has an internal dispute: Abu Hanifa sets it at the theft nisab (10 dirhams), while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) set it at the zakat nisab (200 dirhams). Later authorities have adopted the Sahibayn's view as the relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
Understand the General Rule for 'Mal'
The passage states that if someone says 'I owe so-and-so mal', his specification of the amount is accepted because he made the statement vague. But by istihsan, the minimum is one dirham; less is not considered mal in custom.
Note the use of istihsan over qiyas here.
2
Identify the Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf on 'Mal 'Azim'
For 'mal 'azim', the minimum is disputed: Abu Hanifa says 10 dirhams (nisab of theft), while the Sahibayn say 200 dirhams (nisab of zakat). Another narration from Abu Hanifa agrees with the Sahibayn.
3
Analyze the Reasoning of Each Position
Abu Hanifa: theft nisab is 'great' because the hand is cut. Sahibayn: zakat nisab makes the owner rich, and both Shari'a and custom consider it great.
The text says 'this is the correct view (asah) and the chosen one (ikhtiyar)' for the Sahibayn.
4
Apply the Ruling to Other Currencies and Goods
If iqrar mentions dinars, the minimum is 20 dinars (zakat nisab for gold). For camels, it is 5 camels. For non-zakatable wealth, the value of the zakat nisab applies.
This shows the principle of using Shari'a nisabs as benchmarks.

وَلَوْ قَالَ لِفَلَانِ عَلَيَّ مَالٌ فَالْمَرْجِعُ إِلَيْهِ فِي بَيَانِهِ لِأَنَّهُ هُوَ الْمُجْمَلُ وَيُقْبَلُ قَوْلُهُ فِي الْقَلِيْلِ وَالْكَثِيرِ لِاَنَّ كُلَّ ذَالِكَ مَالٌ فَإِنَّهُ اِسْمٌ لِمَا يَتَمَوَّلُ بِهِ إِلَّا أَنَّهُ لَا يُصَدَّقُ فِى أَقَلَّ مِنْ دِرْهَم لِأَنَّهُ لَا يُعَدُّ مَالًا عُرُفًا وَلَوْ قَالَ مَالٌ عَظِيمٌ لَمْ يُصَّدَقَ فِي أَقَلَّ مِنْ مِانَتَى دِرْهَمٍ لِأَنَّهُ أَقَرَّ بِمَالٍ مَوْصُوفٍ فَلَا يَجُوزُ الْغَاءُ الْوَصْفِ وَالنِّصَابِ مَالٌ عَظِيمٌ حَتَّى اُعْتُبِرَ صَاحِبُهُ غَنِيًّا بِهِ وَالْغِنى عَظِيمٌ عِندَ النَّاسِ وَعِندَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةٌ أَنَّهُ لَا يُصَدَّقُ فِي أَقَلَّ مِنْ عَشَرَةِ دِرَهِمَ وَهِيَ نِصَابُ السَّرْقَةِ لِأَنَّهُ عَظِيمٌ حَيْثُ تُقْطَعُ بِهِ الْيَدُ الْمُحْتَرَمَةُ وَعَنْهُ مِثْلَ جَوَابِ الْكِتَابِ وَهَذَا إِذَا قَالَ مِنَ الدَّرَاهِمِ أَمَّا إِذَا قَالَ مِنَ الدَّنَانِيرِ فَالتَّقْدِيرُ فِيهَا بِالْعِشْرِينَ وَفِي الْإِبِلِ بِخَمْسٍ وَعِشْرِينَ لِأَنَّهُ أَدْنَى نِصَابٍ يَجِبُ فِيْهِ مِنْ جِنْسِهِ وَفِي غَيْرِ مَالِ الزَّكَوةِ بِقِيمَةِ النِّصَابِ
ترجمہ اگر کہا کہ فلاں کا مجھ پر مال ہے۔ تو اس کے بیان میں اسی کی طرف رجوع ہوگا۔ کیونکہ مجمل رکھنے والا وہی ہے اور کم و بیش میں اس کا قول مقبول ہو گا۔ کیونکہ وہ سب مال ہے۔ اس لئے کہ مال اس کا نام ہے جس سے دولت مندی حاصل کی جاتی ہے. مگر ایک درہم سے کم میں تصدیق نہ ہوگی۔ کیونکہ عرف میں اس کو مال شمار نہیں کیا جاتا۔ اور اگر کہا مال عظیم ہے۔ تو دوسو درہم سے کم میں تصدیق نہیں کی جائے گی۔ اس لئے کہ اس نے مال موصوف کا اقرار کیا ہے۔ تو وصف کو لغو کرنا جائز نہ ہوگا۔ اور نصاب مال عظیم ہے۔ اور امام ابو حنیفہ سے روایت ہے کہ دس درہم سے کم میں تصدیق نہ ہوگی۔ اور وہ نصاب سرقہ ہے جو بایں حیثیت عظیم ہے کہ اس کی چوری میں محترم ہاتھ کاٹا جاتا ہے۔ اور ان سے دوسری روایت جواب کتاب کے مثل ہے اور یہ اس وقت ہے جب اس نے من الدرا ہم کہا ہوا گر من الدنانیہ کہا۔ تو اس میں اندازہ ہیں سے ہوگا۔ اور من الابل کہنے میں پچیس سے کیونکہ یہ کمتر نصاب ہے۔ جس میں اسی جنس کا جانور زکوۃ میں واجب ہوتا ہے۔ اور مال زکوۃ کے علاوہ میں نصاب کی قیمت معتبر ہوگی۔
تشریح قوله لفلان علی مال ... اس اقرار میں مقر کم و بیش جو بھی بیان کرے معتبر ہو گا۔ اس لئے کہ وہ قلیل ہو یا کثیر ۔ بہر حال مال ہے ۔ کیونکہ مال تو اسی کو کہتے ہیں جس سے انسان دولت مندی حاصل کرے۔ پھر شیخ الاسلام خواہر زادہ نے اپنی مبسوط میں ذکر کیا ہے۔ کہ بمقتضائے قیاس ایک در ہم سے کم کا بیان بھی مقبول ہونا چاہئے۔ کیونکہ یہ بھی مال ہے۔ لیکن استحسانا تصدیق نہیں کی جائے گی ۔ کیونکہ عرف میں اس کو مال نہیں کہتے ۔ اسیجابی نے شرح کافی میں لو قال له على مال كان القول قوله فيه و در هم مال ذکر کرنے کے بعد لکھا ہے کہ اس سے یہ وہم ہوتا ہے کہ ایک درہم سے کم میں اس کا قول مقبول نہ ہوگا۔ اور بعض نے کہا ہے کہ مقبول ہونا چاہیئے ۔ کیونکہ مال کا اطلاق تو نصف وسدس درہم پر بھی ہوتا ہے۔ لیکن صحیح یہ ہے کہ مقبول نہ ہو گا اس لئے کہ جو مال تحت الالزام داخل ہوتا ہے وہ بحکم عادت ایک درہم سے کم نہیں ہوتا۔ شیخ باطفی نے اجناس میں نوادر ہشام سے امام محمد کا قول لو قال لفلان على مال له ان يقر بدرهم، نقل کرنے کے بعد شیخ ہارونی کا قول ذکر کیا ہے کہ امام ابوحنیفہ وزٹر کے قول میں دس کھرے دراہم سے کم میں تصدیق نہ ہوگی۔ اور امام ابو یوسف فرماتے ہیں کہ تین دراہم میں تصدیق ہوگی اس سے کم میں نہیں۔ قوله مال عظیم . مال عظیم کے اقرار میں نصاب زکوۃ دو سو درہم سے کم میں تصدیق نہ ہوگی۔ امام شافعی کے نزدیک یہ بھی اعلی مال کے مثل ہے۔ ہم یہ کہتے ہیں کہ اس نے مال کو صفت عظیم کے ساتھ موصوف کیا ہے۔ تو اس وصف کو لغو نہیں کیا جاسکتا۔ پھر شریعت میں نصاب زکوۃ مال . عظیم ہے کہ شرع نے صاحب نصاب کو غنی قرار دیا ہے۔ اور عرف میں بھی اس کو فنی سمجھتے ہیں۔ لہذا اسی کا اعتبار ہوگا۔ یہی اصح ہے۔ (اختیار) پھر یہ صاحبین کا قول ہے۔ اس کی بابت امام محمد نے مبسوط میں امام ابو حنیفہ کا قول ذکر نہیں کیا۔ اسی لئے مشائخ کی روایات مختلف ہوگئیں۔ چنانچہ ایک روایت تو یہ ہے۔ کہ نصاب سرقہ یعنی دس درہم سے کم میں تصدیق نہ ہوگی۔ کیونکہ یہ بھی مال عظیم ہے کہ اس کی چوری میں محترم عضو
And if he says 'I owe so-and-so wealth (mal),' then reference is to him in its specification, because he is the one who made it vague. His word is accepted in little and much, because all of that is mal, for it is a name for what one acquires wealth by. However, he is not believed for less than a dirham, because it is not considered mal in custom. And if he says 'great wealth (mal 'azim),' he is not believed for less than two hundred dirhams, because he confessed to described wealth, and nullifying the description is not allowed. And the nisab for 'great wealth' is such that its owner is considered rich by it, and richness is considered great among people. According to Abu Hanifa, he is not believed for less than ten dirhams, which is the nisab of theft, because it is great in the sense that a protected hand is cut off for it. And from him there is another narration like the answer of the book (i.e., 200 dirhams). This is when he says 'of dirhams.' If he says 'of dinars,' then the estimate is twenty. And for camels, it is twenty-five, because that is the minimum nisab in which zakat is obligatory of that type. And for other than zakatable wealth, the value of the nisab is considered.
Translation: If he said 'I owe so-and-so wealth (mal),' then reference is to him in specifying it, because he is the one who made it vague. His word is accepted in little and much, because all of that is mal, for mal is the name for what one acquires wealth by. However, he is not believed for less than a dirham, because it is not considered mal in custom. And if he said 'great wealth,' he will not be believed for less than two hundred dirhams, because he confessed to described wealth, and nullifying the description is not allowed. And the nisab of great wealth is such that the owner is considered rich. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, he is not believed for less than ten dirhams, which is the nisab of theft, because it is great in that a respected hand is cut off for it. And from him there is another narration like the answer of the book. This is when he said 'from dirhams.' If he said 'from dinars,' then the estimate is twenty. And for camels, it is twenty-five, because that is the minimum nisab in which zakat is obligatory of that type. And for non-zakatable wealth, the value of the nisab is considered.
Commentary: His statement 'li-fulan 'alayya mal' – in this iqrar, whatever the confessor specifies, little or much, is accepted, because both little and much are mal, since mal is what one acquires wealth from. Then Shaykh al-Islam Khwahar-zadah mentioned in his Mabsut that according to qiyas, specification of less than a dirham should also be accepted, because it is mal. But by istihsan, it is not accepted, because in custom it is not called mal. As-Sijabi in Sharh al-Kafi, after mentioning 'if he says I owe mal, his word is accepted and a dirham is mal,' wrote that from this it is understood that less than a dirham is not accepted. Some said it should be accepted because the term mal applies to half and sixth of a dirham. But the correct view is that it is not accepted, because wealth that enters under obligation, by custom, is not less than a dirham. Shaykh al-Batiqi in al-Ajnas narrated from Nawadir Hisham the saying of Imam Muhammad: 'If he says I owe so-and-so mal, he must confess a dirham.' Then Shaykh Haruni's saying: According to Abu Hanifa, he is not believed for less than ten pure dirhams. Imam Abu Yusuf says he is believed for three dirhams, not less. His statement 'mal 'azim' – in iqrar of great wealth, he is not believed for less than the nisab of zakat, i.e., 200 dirhams. According to Imam al-Shafi'i, this is like ordinary mal. We say: He described mal with the attribute great, so nullifying the attribute is not allowed. In Shari'a, the nisab of zakat is great wealth, and Shar'a considers the owner of nisab rich. In custom, he is also considered wealthy. So this is the relied-upon view. This is the saying of the Sahibayn. Imam Muhammad did not mention Imam Abu Hanifa's saying in al-Mabsut; hence, the narrations of the mashayikh differed. One narration: he is not believed for less than the nisab of theft, i.e., ten dirhams, because that is also great wealth, as a respected limb is cut off for it.
Source pages p. 51

Commentary
This passage deals with iqrar using the word 'mal' (wealth) and 'mal 'azim' (great wealth). For 'mal,' the confessor's specification is accepted for any amount, because everything that can be considered wealth is mal. However, by istihsan (preference), less than one dirham is not accepted because custom does not consider it mal. There is debate about this: some argue qiyas would allow even half a dirham, but the relied-upon view is that a minimum of one dirham is required. For 'mal 'azim,' the minimum is 200 dirhams (nisab of zakat) according to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). Imam Abu Hanifa has a different view: he sets the minimum at 10 dirhams (nisab of theft), because that is considered 'azim (great) in Shari'a due to the cutting of the hand. Another narration from Abu Hanifa agrees with the Sahibayn. The commentary then addresses other currencies: if the iqrar mentions dinars, the minimum is 20 dinars (nisab of zakat for gold); if it mentions camels, the minimum is 5 camels (nisab of zakat for camels). For non-zakatable items, the value of the zakat nisab is considered. This intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf revolves around what constitutes 'great wealth' – the Sahibayn focus on the zakat nisab, while Abu Hanifa focuses on the theft nisab. The relied-upon position (al-mukhtar) is that of the Sahibayn, i.e., 200 dirhams.

Key Terms
مال (mal): Wealth or property that can be possessed and valued; in iqrar context, it includes anything from one dirham upwards.
مال عظیم (mal 'azim): Great wealth, defined by the nisab of zakat (200 dirhams) or the nisab of theft (10 dirhams) according to different views.
نصاب (nisab): The minimum amount that triggers a legal ruling, such as zakat or theft penalty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon (mufta bihi) Hanafi position, what is the minimum amount for iqrar of 'mal 'azim'?
A) 10 dirhams
B) 200 dirhams
C) 1 dirham
D) 3 dirhams

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school defines 'great wealth' for iqrar by the zakat nisab (200 dirhams), resolving an internal dispute in favor of the Sahibayn's view.

Iqrār bi al-Māl: The Minimum Amount and the Role of Custom
States rulings on iqrār bi al-māl with qiyas/istihsān and intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the minimum amount in iqrār bi al-māl, explain why istihsān overrides qiyas, and distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad.

Core Idea
Custom rules: less than one dirham is not accepted; Imams differed on the exact minimum (10, 3, or custom-based).

When a person acknowledges property without specifying an amount, Hanafi law generally accepts any amount he states. However, juristic preference (istihsān) sets aside this qiyas-based rule for trivial amounts because custom does not treat them as property. This lesson unpacks the three Hanafi opinions on the minimum and identifies the relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Iqrār bi al-māl is an acknowledgment of a financial liability. The general rule is that the acknowledger's statement of the amount is accepted, because the word 'māl' includes any property.
This is the default rule (qiyas).
2
Examine the istihsān exception
By istihsān, an explanation of less than one dirham is not accepted because custom does not consider such a small amount as 'property'. This is based on the strength of custom (ʿurf) over analogy.
Ignorance of custom leads to incorrect rulings.
3
Trace the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Imam Abu Hanifa (in one narration) requires a minimum of ten dirhams (the nisab of theft). Imam Abu Yusuf requires three dirhams. Imam Muhammad, as reported in Nawādir Hishām, allows the acknowledgment of one dirham, which aligns with the custom-based approach.
Each imam used a different benchmark: theft nisab, a moderate threshold, and custom.
4
Apply the tarjih (preferment)
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that less than one dirham is not accepted. The specific numbers (3,10) are not binding; the criterion is custom.
This is the view that later Hanafi jurists adopted for fatwa.
5
Understand the practical consequence
In litigation, if a person acknowledges property and later claims it was less than a dirham, his claim is rejected. If he acknowledges one dirham or more, it is binding.
Different opinions lead to different outcomes; knowing the mufta bihi is crucial.

تصدیق نہ ہوگی۔ کیونکہ عرف میں اس کو مال شمار نہیں کیا جاتا۔ اور اگر کہا ماں عظیم ہے۔ تو دوسو درہم سے کم میں تصدیق نہیں کی جائے گی۔ اس لئے کہ اس نے مال موصوف کا اقرار کیا ہے کو وصف کو لغو کرنا جائز نہ ہوگا۔ اور نصاب مال عظیم ہے۔ اور امام ابو حنیفہ سے روایت ہے کہ دس درہم سے کم میں تصدیق نہ ہوگی۔ اور وہ نصاب سرقہ ہے جو بایں حیثیت عظیم ہے کہ اس کی چوری میں محترم ہاتھ کاٹا جاتا ہے۔ اور ان سے دوسری روایت جواب کتاب کے مثل ہے اور یہ اس وقت ہے جب اس نے من الدرا ہم کہا ہوا گر من الدنانیہ کہا۔ تو اس میں اندازہ ہیں سے ہوگا۔ اور من الابل کہنے میں پچیس سے
کیونکہ یہ کمتر نصاب ہے۔ جس میں اسی جنس کا جانور زکوۃ میں واجب ہوتا ہے۔ اور مال زکوۃ کے علاوہ میں نصاب کی قیمت معتبر ہوگی۔ تشریح قوله و يقال له اور مقرکسی مجہول چیز کا اقرار کرے تو اقرار صحیح ہو گا اور اس سے کہا جائے گا کہ اس مجہول کو بیان کر ۔ کیونکہ اجمال وتجہیل اسی کی جانب سے واقع ہوئی ہے تو بیان اس کے ذمہ ہو گا۔ جیسے کوئی اپنے دوغلاموں کی نسبت کہے کہ ان میں سے ایک آزاد ہے تو اس ایک کی تعیین اسی کے ذمہ ہے۔ اب اگر وہ بیان کرنے سے باز رہے تو قاضی اس کو بیان پر مجبور کر سکتا ہے۔ کیونکہ اس کے صحیح اقرار سے جو چیز اس پر لازم آئی ہے۔ اس ذمہ داری سے باہر ہونا بھی اس پر لازم ہے۔ اور اس کی صورت یہی ہے۔ کہ اس کو بیان کرے۔ یہ مسئلہ اجماعی ہے۔ قوله لفلان على شئى. لفلان على شئی کہنے میں شئی کا بیان ایسی چیز سے ضروری ہوگا جو قیمتی ہو ۔گو کمتر ہو۔ کیونکہ لفظ علی ایجاب و الزام کے لئے ہوتا ہے۔ اور جس چیز کی کوئی قیمت نہ ہو وہ آدمی کے ذمہ واجب نہیں ہوتی۔ پس اگر اس نے یہ بیان کیا کہ گیہوں کا ایک دانہ ہے تو صحیح نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ یہ تو اقرار سے رجوع کرنا ہے۔ محیط میں ہے۔ کہ اگر مقریہ کہے کہ میں نے حق اسلام کا ارادہ کیا ہے تو اس کی تصدیق نہ ہوگی۔ (جب کہ مفصولاً کہا ہو۔ اگر موصولاً کہا تو تصدیق کی جائے گی۔ ائمہ ثلاثہ کے نزدیک دونوں صورتوں میں تصدیق نہ ہوگی ) ۔ اور اگر مردہ یا اسور یا شراب مراد لیا تو مشائخ ماوراء انہر کے نزدیک تصدیق نہ ہوگی۔ کیونکہ ان چیزوں کی کوئی قیمت نہیں۔ ایک وجہ میں امام مالک و شافعی اسی کے قائل ہیں۔ اور مشائخ عراق کے نزدیک تصدیق کی جائے گی۔ اور اگر یہ کہا کہ ایک پیسہ مراد ہے تو تصدیق ہوگی۔
قوله لفلان علی مال ... اس اقرار میں مقر کم و بیش جو بھی بیان کرے معتبر ہو گا۔ اس لئے کہ وہ قلیل ہو یا کثیر ۔ بہر حال مال ہے ۔ کیونکہ مال تو اسی کو کہتے ہیں جس سے انسان دولت مندی حاصل کرے۔ پھر شیخ الاسلام خواہر زادہ نے اپنی مبسوط میں ذکر کیا ہے۔ کہ بمقتضائے قیاس ایک در ہم سے کم کا بیان بھی مقبول ہونا چاہئے۔ کیونکہ یہ بھی مال ہے۔ لیکن استحسانا تصدیق نہیں کی جائے گی ۔ کیونکہ عرف میں اس کو مال نہیں کہتے ۔ اسیجابی نے شرح کافی میں لو قال له على مال كان القول قوله فيه و در هم مال ذکر کرنے کے بعد لکھا ہے کہ اس سے یہ وہم ہوتا ہے کہ ایک درہم سے کم میں اس کا قول مقبول نہ ہوگا۔ اور بعض نے کہا ہے کہ مقبول ہونا چاہیئے ۔ کیونکہ مال کا اطلاق تو نصف وسدس درہم پر بھی ہوتا ہے۔ لیکن صحیح یہ ہے کہ مقبول نہ ہو گا اس لئے کہ جو مال تحت الالزام داخل ہوتا ہے وہ بحکم عادت ایک درہم سے کم نہیں ہوتا۔ شیخ باطفی نے اجناس میں نوادر ہشام سے امام محمد کا قول لو قال لفلان على مال له ان يقر بدرهم، نقل کرنے کے بعد شیخ ہارونی کا قول ذکر کیا ہے کہ امام ابوحنیفہ وزٹر کے
قول میں دس کھرے دراہم سے کم میں تصدیق نہ ہوگی۔ اور امام ابو یوسف فرماتے ہیں کہ تین دراہم میں تصدیق ہوگی اس سے کم میں نہیں۔ قوله مال عظیم . مال عظیم کے اقرار میں نصاب زکوۃ دو سو درہم سے کم میں تصدیق نہ ہوگی۔ امام شافعی کے نزدیک یہ بھی اعلی مال کے مثل ہے۔ ہم یہ کہتے ہیں کہ اس نے مال کو صفت عظیم کے ساتھ موصوف کیا ہے۔ تو اس وصف کو لغو نہیں کیا جاسکتا۔ پھر شریعت میں نصاب زکوۃ مال . عظیم ہے کہ شرع نے صاحب نصاب کو غنی قرار دیا ہے۔ اور عرف میں بھی اس کو فنی سمجھتے ہیں۔ لہذا اسی کا اعتبار ہوگا۔ یہی اصح ہے۔ (اختیار) پھر یہ صاحبین کا قول ہے۔ اس کی بابت امام محمد نے مبسوط میں امام ابو حنیفہ کا قول ذکر نہیں کیا۔ اسی لئے مشائخ کی روایات مختلف ہوگئیں۔ چنانچہ ایک روایت تو یہ ہے۔ کہ نصاب سرقہ یعنی دس درہم سے کم میں تصدیق نہ ہوگی۔ کیونکہ یہ بھی مال عظیم ہے کہ اس کی چوری میں محترم عضو (ہاتھ) کا ٹا جاتا ہے۔ اور دوسری روایت وہی ہے جو کتاب میں صاحبین کا قول مذکور ہوا۔
His statement will be accepted. Because it is all property. Because property is that by which wealth is obtained. It will not be accepted, because in custom it is not considered property. And if he said 'great property', then less than two hundred dirhams will not be accepted. Because he acknowledged specified property, and it is not permissible to make the description void. And the nisab of zakat is great property. And it is narrated from Imam Abu Hanifa that less than ten dirhams will not be accepted. And that is the nisab of theft, which is great in the sense that for its theft the respected hand is cut. And another narration from him is like the text of the book. And this is when he said 'from dirhams', but if he said 'from dananir', then estimation will be from that. And if he said 'from camels', then from twenty-five, because that is the lowest nisab in which an animal of that type is obligatory in zakat. And apart from zakat property, the value of the nisab will be considered. Explanation of his saying: 'And it is said to him': If a person acknowledges an unknown thing, the acknowledgment is valid, and he will be told to explain that unknown. Because the ambiguity and unknownness are from his side, so explanation is his responsibility. Like if someone says of his two slaves that one of them is free, then the specification of that one is his responsibility. So if he refrains from explaining, the judge can compel him to explain. Because what has become obligatory upon him through his valid acknowledgment, it is also obligatory upon him to exit that liability. And that is by explaining. This issue is by consensus. His saying: 'So-and-so has upon me a thing.' In saying 'so-and-so has upon me a thing', the explanation of 'thing' must be something which has value, even if little. Because the word 'upon' is for obligation and liability. And something that has no value is not obligatory upon a person. So if he explained it as a grain of wheat, it will not be valid, because that is retracting from the acknowledgment. In al-Muhit: if the acknowledger says 'I intended the right of Islam', it will not be accepted (if said separately; if said connectedly, it will be accepted. According to the three Imams, in both cases it will not be accepted). And if he intended a corpse or pig or wine, according to the scholars of Transoxiana it will not be accepted, because these things have no value. In one view, Imam Malik and Shafi'i are of this opinion. According to the scholars of Iraq, it will be accepted. And if he said 'I intended one paisa', it will be accepted. His saying: 'So-and-so has upon me property'... In this acknowledgment, whatever the acknowledger says, little or much, will be accepted. Because whether little or much, in any case it is property. Because property is that by which a person acquires wealth. Then Shaykh al-Islam Khāharzādah mentioned in his Mabsūṭ that by qiyas, an explanation of less than one dirham should be accepted, because that is also property. But by istihsan, it will not be accepted, because in custom it is not called property. Isijābī in Sharḥ al-Kāfī, after mentioning 'if he said: he has upon me property, his statement is accepted regarding it, and a dirham is property', wrote that from this it is understood that less than a dirham his statement will not be accepted. And some said it should be accepted, because the term 'property' applies to half and sixth of a dirham. But the correct view is that it will not be accepted, because property that enters under liability, by custom, is not less than one dirham. Shaykh Bāṭifī, after quoting from Nawādir Hishām the statement of Imam Muhammad 'If he said: so-and-so has upon me property, he may acknowledge one dirham', mentioned the statement of Shaykh Hārūnī that in the statement of Imam Abu Hanifa, less than ten good dirhams will not be accepted. And Imam Abu Yusuf says that three dirhams will be accepted, less than that not. His saying: 'Great property'. In the acknowledgment of great property, less than the zakat nisab of two hundred dirhams will not be accepted. According to Imam Shafi'i, this is like superior property. We say that he described property with the attribute 'great', so that attribute cannot be made void. Then in Shari'ah, the zakat nisab is great property because the Lawgiver has deemed the owner of nisab as rich. And in custom also, he is considered rich. Therefore, this will be considered. This is the most correct. (Ikhtiyār) Then this is the statement of the two companions (Sahibayn). Regarding this, Imam Muhammad did not mention the statement of Imam Abu Hanifa in al-Mabsūṭ. Hence, the narrations of the scholars differed. Thus, one narration is that less than the nisab of theft, i.e., ten dirhams, will not be accepted, because that is also great property since for its theft the respected limb (hand) is cut. And the second narration is that which is mentioned in the book, the statement of the two companions.
Source pages p. 52

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf Ul Hadaya, a commentary on Al-Hidayah, covers multiple rulings on iqrār (acknowledgment/confession). The central theme is how ambiguous terms like 'māl' (property) and 'māl ʿaẓīm' (great property) are interpreted in iqrār, and the minimum amounts that trigger liability. The passage begins by stating the general rule: if someone acknowledges 'he has property upon me', the acknowledger's statement regarding the amount is accepted because the word 'māl' encompasses anything that brings wealth. However, the text notes that custom (ʿurf) does not treat less than a dirham as 'māl', so by istihsan (juristic preference), an explanation of less than a dirham is not accepted, even though qiyas would allow it. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Imam Abu Hanifa is reported to require at least ten dirhams (the nisab of theft), while Imam Abu Yusuf accepts three dirhams. Imam Muhammad's view aligns with the nisab of theft or the text of the book. The passage then addresses iqrār of an unknown thing (shayʿ), ruling that it must be something of value; an explanation of a grain of wheat is invalid as it amounts to retraction. It also mentions the validity of explaining it as a paisa but not as a corpse or wine (according to Transoxianan scholars, but Iraqi scholars accept it). Finally, the passage discusses iqrār by 'māl ʿaẓīm', which requires the nisab of zakat (200 dirhams) because the attribute 'great' cannot be ignored, and the Shari'ah considers that threshold as 'great'. There is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: Sahibayn hold the 200 dirham minimum, while a narration from Abu Hanifa uses the theft nisab (10 dirhams). The relied-upon position is the Sahibayn's view, as noted by the commentator. The passage also includes inter-madhhab disputes: Imam Shafi'i treats 'māl ʿaẓīm' like 'māl' in general, and Imam Malik and Shafi'i agree with Transoxianan scholars on the invalidity of acknowledging a corpse or wine.

Key Terms
اقرار (Iqrār): An acknowledgment or confession of a right or liability, typically of a financial or legal nature, made by one person in favor of another.
مال (Māl): Property or wealth; something that can be owned and has value.
استحسان (Istihsān): Juristic preference; setting aside the result of qiyas in favor of a ruling based on custom, necessity, or public interest.
عرف (ʿUrf): Custom; widespread practice that is accepted as a legal source when not contradicting explicit texts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position (muftā bihī), what is the minimum amount for an iqrār by 'māl' (property) when no specific quantity is mentioned?
A) One dirham or more
B) Three dirhams
C) Ten dirhams
D) Two hundred dirhams

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi iqrār bi al-māl, custom rules: less than one dirham is not accepted, and the specific numbers of the imams are not binding for fatwa.

Iqrār bi al-Māl al-ʿAẓīm: The Zakat Nisab Standard
States ruling on iqrār bi al-māl al-ʿaẓīm with intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf and cross-madhhab comparison

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school requires the zakat nisab (200 dirhams) for iqrār bi al-māl al-ʿaẓīm, and identify the intra-Hanafi dispute with Abu Hanifa's alternative theft nisab.

Core Idea
When property is described as 'great', the Hanafi school binds it to the zakat nisab; a different narration from Abu Hanifa uses the theft nisab.

Acknowledging 'great property' (māl ʿaẓīm) triggers a higher minimum. The Hanafi school primarily links it to the nisab of zakat, because the Lawgiver considers that threshold as making one rich. However, there is a narration from Abu Hanifa that employs the nisab of theft (10 dirhams) because that also is considered 'great' in terms of legal consequence. This lesson examines the evidence and the relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the phrase and its implication
When someone acknowledges 'great property' (māl ʿaẓīm), the attribute 'great' must be given legal effect; it cannot be ignored.
The Arabic word ʿaẓīm qualifies the property, so a specific threshold must be found.
2
Search for a Shari'i definition of 'great'
The passage looks to the Sharīʿa to define what is 'great'. Two candidates emerge: the nisab of zakat (200 dirhams) and the nisab of theft (10 dirhams). Both are considered 'great' in the law.
Zakat nisab makes one rich; theft nisab triggers hand amputation.
3
Examine the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
The two companions (Sahibayn: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) adopt the zakat nisab. A narration from Imam Abu Hanifa adopts the theft nisab (10 dirhams).
The passage notes that Imam Muhammad, in his Mabsūṭ, did not mention Abu Hanifa's narration, leading to differing transmissions.
4
Apply the tarjih
The commentator declares the zakat nisab as 'the most correct' (al-aṣaḥḥ). Thus, the mufta bihi is 200 dirhams or its equivalent in other currencies.
Tarjih is based on the strength of the zakat nisab as a universally recognized standard of wealth in Sharīʿa and custom.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Imam Shafi'i does not treat māl ʿaẓīm differently from ordinary māl; for him, any amount suffices as long as it has value. The Hanafi school imposes a higher threshold due to the descriptive term.
The thamarah: a Shafi'i judge would accept an acknowledgment of 20 dirhams as 'great property', while a Hanafi judge would not.

تصدیق نہ ہوگی۔ کیونکہ عرف میں اس کو مال شمار نہیں کیا جاتا۔ اور اگر کہا ماں عظیم ہے۔ تو دوسو درہم سے کم میں تصدیق نہیں کی جائے گی۔ اس لئے کہ اس نے مال موصوف کا اقرار کیا ہے کو وصف کو لغو کرنا جائز نہ ہوگا۔ اور نصاب مال عظیم ہے۔ اور امام ابو حنیفہ سے روایت ہے کہ دس درہم سے کم میں تصدیق نہ ہوگی۔ اور وہ نصاب سرقہ ہے جو بایں حیثیت عظیم ہے کہ اس کی چوری میں محترم ہاتھ کاٹا جاتا ہے۔ اور ان سے دوسری روایت جواب کتاب کے مثل ہے اور یہ اس وقت ہے جب اس نے من الدرا ہم کہا ہوا گر من الدنانیہ کہا۔ تو اس میں اندازہ ہیں سے ہوگا۔ اور من الابل کہنے میں پچیس سے
کیونکہ یہ کمتر نصاب ہے۔ جس میں اسی جنس کا جانور زکوۃ میں واجب ہوتا ہے۔ اور مال زکوۃ کے علاوہ میں نصاب کی قیمت معتبر ہوگی۔ تشریح قوله و يقال له اور مقرکسی مجہول چیز کا اقرار کرے تو اقرار صحیح ہو گا اور اس سے کہا جائے گا کہ اس مجہول کو بیان کر ۔ کیونکہ اجمال وتجہیل اسی کی جانب سے واقع ہوئی ہے تو بیان اس کے ذمہ ہو گا۔ جیسے کوئی اپنے دوغلاموں کی نسبت کہے کہ ان میں سے ایک آزاد ہے تو اس ایک کی تعیین اسی کے ذمہ ہے۔ اب اگر وہ بیان کرنے سے باز رہے تو قاضی اس کو بیان پر مجبور کر سکتا ہے۔ کیونکہ اس کے صحیح اقرار سے جو چیز اس پر لازم آئی ہے۔ اس ذمہ داری سے باہر ہونا بھی اس پر لازم ہے۔ اور اس کی صورت یہی ہے۔ کہ اس کو بیان کرے۔ یہ مسئلہ اجماعی ہے۔ قوله لفلان على شئى. لفلان على شئی کہنے میں شئی کا بیان ایسی چیز سے ضروری ہوگا جو قیمتی ہو ۔گو کمتر ہو۔ کیونکہ لفظ علی ایجاب و الزام کے لئے ہوتا ہے۔ اور جس چیز کی کوئی قیمت نہ ہو وہ آدمی کے ذمہ واجب نہیں ہوتی۔ پس اگر اس نے یہ بیان کیا کہ گیہوں کا ایک دانہ ہے تو صحیح نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ یہ تو اقرار سے رجوع کرنا ہے۔ محیط میں ہے۔ کہ اگر مقریہ کہے کہ میں نے حق اسلام کا ارادہ کیا ہے تو اس کی تصدیق نہ ہوگی۔ (جب کہ مفصولاً کہا ہو۔ اگر موصولاً کہا تو تصدیق کی جائے گی۔ ائمہ ثلاثہ کے نزدیک دونوں صورتوں میں تصدیق نہ ہوگی ) ۔ اور اگر مردہ یا اسور یا شراب مراد لیا تو مشائخ ماوراء انہر کے نزدیک تصدیق نہ ہوگی۔ کیونکہ ان چیزوں کی کوئی قیمت نہیں۔ ایک وجہ میں امام مالک و شافعی اسی کے قائل ہیں۔ اور مشائخ عراق کے نزدیک تصدیق کی جائے گی۔ اور اگر یہ کہا کہ ایک پیسہ مراد ہے تو تصدیق ہوگی۔
قوله لفلان علی مال ... اس اقرار میں مقر کم و بیش جو بھی بیان کرے معتبر ہو گا۔ اس لئے کہ وہ قلیل ہو یا کثیر ۔ بہر حال مال ہے ۔ کیونکہ مال تو اسی کو کہتے ہیں جس سے انسان دولت مندی حاصل کرے۔ پھر شیخ الاسلام خواہر زادہ نے اپنی مبسوط میں ذکر کیا ہے۔ کہ بمقتضائے قیاس ایک در ہم سے کم کا بیان بھی مقبول ہونا چاہئے۔ کیونکہ یہ بھی مال ہے۔ لیکن استحسانا تصدیق نہیں کی جائے گی ۔ کیونکہ عرف میں اس کو مال نہیں کہتے ۔ اسیجابی نے شرح کافی میں لو قال له على مال كان القول قوله فيه و در هم مال ذکر کرنے کے بعد لکھا ہے کہ اس سے یہ وہم ہوتا ہے کہ ایک درہم سے کم میں اس کا قول مقبول نہ ہوگا۔ اور بعض نے کہا ہے کہ مقبول ہونا چاہیئے ۔ کیونکہ مال کا اطلاق تو نصف وسدس درہم پر بھی ہوتا ہے۔ لیکن صحیح یہ ہے کہ مقبول نہ ہو گا اس لئے کہ جو مال تحت الالزام داخل ہوتا ہے وہ بحکم عادت ایک درہم سے کم نہیں ہوتا۔ شیخ باطفی نے اجناس میں نوادر ہشام سے امام محمد کا قول لو قال لفلان على مال له ان يقر بدرهم، نقل کرنے کے بعد شیخ ہارونی کا قول ذکر کیا ہے کہ امام ابوحنیفہ وزٹر کے
قول میں دس کھرے دراہم سے کم میں تصدیق نہ ہوگی۔ اور امام ابو یوسف فرماتے ہیں کہ تین دراہم میں تصدیق ہوگی اس سے کم میں نہیں۔ قوله مال عظیم . مال عظیم کے اقرار میں نصاب زکوۃ دو سو درہم سے کم میں تصدیق نہ ہوگی۔ امام شافعی کے نزدیک یہ بھی اعلی مال کے مثل ہے۔ ہم یہ کہتے ہیں کہ اس نے مال کو صفت عظیم کے ساتھ موصوف کیا ہے۔ تو اس وصف کو لغو نہیں کیا جاسکتا۔ پھر شریعت میں نصاب زکوۃ مال . عظیم ہے کہ شرع نے صاحب نصاب کو غنی قرار دیا ہے۔ اور عرف میں بھی اس کو فنی سمجھتے ہیں۔ لہذا اسی کا اعتبار ہوگا۔ یہی اصح ہے۔ (اختیار) پھر یہ صاحبین کا قول ہے۔ اس کی بابت امام محمد نے مبسوط میں امام ابو حنیفہ کا قول ذکر نہیں کیا۔ اسی لئے مشائخ کی روایات مختلف ہوگئیں۔ چنانچہ ایک روایت تو یہ ہے۔ کہ نصاب سرقہ یعنی دس درہم سے کم میں تصدیق نہ ہوگی۔ کیونکہ یہ بھی مال عظیم ہے کہ اس کی چوری میں محترم عضو (ہاتھ) کا ٹا جاتا ہے۔ اور دوسری روایت وہی ہے جو کتاب میں صاحبین کا قول مذکور ہوا۔
His statement will be accepted. Because it is all property. Because property is that by which wealth is obtained. It will not be accepted, because in custom it is not considered property. And if he said 'great property', then less than two hundred dirhams will not be accepted. Because he acknowledged specified property, and it is not permissible to make the description void. And the nisab of zakat is great property. And it is narrated from Imam Abu Hanifa that less than ten dirhams will not be accepted. And that is the nisab of theft, which is great in the sense that for its theft the respected hand is cut. And another narration from him is like the text of the book. And this is when he said 'from dirhams', but if he said 'from dananir', then estimation will be from that. And if he said 'from camels', then from twenty-five, because that is the lowest nisab in which an animal of that type is obligatory in zakat. And apart from zakat property, the value of the nisab will be considered. Explanation of his saying: 'And it is said to him': If a person acknowledges an unknown thing, the acknowledgment is valid, and he will be told to explain that unknown. Because the ambiguity and unknownness are from his side, so explanation is his responsibility. Like if someone says of his two slaves that one of them is free, then the specification of that one is his responsibility. So if he refrains from explaining, the judge can compel him to explain. Because what has become obligatory upon him through his valid acknowledgment, it is also obligatory upon him to exit that liability. And that is by explaining. This issue is by consensus. His saying: 'So-and-so has upon me a thing.' In saying 'so-and-so has upon me a thing', the explanation of 'thing' must be something which has value, even if little. Because the word 'upon' is for obligation and liability. And something that has no value is not obligatory upon a person. So if he explained it as a grain of wheat, it will not be valid, because that is retracting from the acknowledgment. In al-Muhit: if the acknowledger says 'I intended the right of Islam', it will not be accepted (if said separately; if said connectedly, it will be accepted. According to the three Imams, in both cases it will not be accepted). And if he intended a corpse or pig or wine, according to the scholars of Transoxiana it will not be accepted, because these things have no value. In one view, Imam Malik and Shafi'i are of this opinion. According to the scholars of Iraq, it will be accepted. And if he said 'I intended one paisa', it will be accepted. His saying: 'So-and-so has upon me property'... In this acknowledgment, whatever the acknowledger says, little or much, will be accepted. Because whether little or much, in any case it is property. Because property is that by which a person acquires wealth. Then Shaykh al-Islam Khāharzādah mentioned in his Mabsūṭ that by qiyas, an explanation of less than one dirham should be accepted, because that is also property. But by istihsan, it will not be accepted, because in custom it is not called property. Isijābī in Sharḥ al-Kāfī, after mentioning 'if he said: he has upon me property, his statement is accepted regarding it, and a dirham is property', wrote that from this it is understood that less than a dirham his statement will not be accepted. And some said it should be accepted, because the term 'property' applies to half and sixth of a dirham. But the correct view is that it will not be accepted, because property that enters under liability, by custom, is not less than one dirham. Shaykh Bāṭifī, after quoting from Nawādir Hishām the statement of Imam Muhammad 'If he said: so-and-so has upon me property, he may acknowledge one dirham', mentioned the statement of Shaykh Hārūnī that in the statement of Imam Abu Hanifa, less than ten good dirhams will not be accepted. And Imam Abu Yusuf says that three dirhams will be accepted, less than that not. His saying: 'Great property'. In the acknowledgment of great property, less than the zakat nisab of two hundred dirhams will not be accepted. According to Imam Shafi'i, this is like superior property. We say that he described property with the attribute 'great', so that attribute cannot be made void. Then in Shari'ah, the zakat nisab is great property because the Lawgiver has deemed the owner of nisab as rich. And in custom also, he is considered rich. Therefore, this will be considered. This is the most correct. (Ikhtiyār) Then this is the statement of the two companions (Sahibayn). Regarding this, Imam Muhammad did not mention the statement of Imam Abu Hanifa in al-Mabsūṭ. Hence, the narrations of the scholars differed. Thus, one narration is that less than the nisab of theft, i.e., ten dirhams, will not be accepted, because that is also great property since for its theft the respected limb (hand) is cut. And the second narration is that which is mentioned in the book, the statement of the two companions.
Source pages p. 52

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf Ul Hadaya, a commentary on Al-Hidayah, covers multiple rulings on iqrār (acknowledgment/confession). The central theme is how ambiguous terms like 'māl' (property) and 'māl ʿaẓīm' (great property) are interpreted in iqrār, and the minimum amounts that trigger liability. The passage begins by stating the general rule: if someone acknowledges 'he has property upon me', the acknowledger's statement regarding the amount is accepted because the word 'māl' encompasses anything that brings wealth. However, the text notes that custom (ʿurf) does not treat less than a dirham as 'māl', so by istihsan (juristic preference), an explanation of less than a dirham is not accepted, even though qiyas would allow it. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Imam Abu Hanifa is reported to require at least ten dirhams (the nisab of theft), while Imam Abu Yusuf accepts three dirhams. Imam Muhammad's view aligns with the nisab of theft or the text of the book. The passage then addresses iqrār of an unknown thing (shayʿ), ruling that it must be something of value; an explanation of a grain of wheat is invalid as it amounts to retraction. It also mentions the validity of explaining it as a paisa but not as a corpse or wine (according to Transoxianan scholars, but Iraqi scholars accept it). Finally, the passage discusses iqrār by 'māl ʿaẓīm', which requires the nisab of zakat (200 dirhams) because the attribute 'great' cannot be ignored, and the Shari'ah considers that threshold as 'great'. There is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: Sahibayn hold the 200 dirham minimum, while a narration from Abu Hanifa uses the theft nisab (10 dirhams). The relied-upon position is the Sahibayn's view, as noted by the commentator. The passage also includes inter-madhhab disputes: Imam Shafi'i treats 'māl ʿaẓīm' like 'māl' in general, and Imam Malik and Shafi'i agree with Transoxianan scholars on the invalidity of acknowledging a corpse or wine.

Key Terms
مال عظیم (Māl ʿAẓīm): Great property; defined in this context as the nisab of zakat (200 dirhams or equivalent).
نصاب زکوة (Nisāb al-Zakāt): The minimum amount of wealth that makes zakat obligatory; for silver, it is 200 dirhams (approx. 600g silver).
نصاب سرقہ (Nisāb al-Sariqah): The minimum value of stolen property that triggers the hadd punishment of hand amputation; according to the Hanafi school, it is 10 dirhams.
وصف (Waṣf): Attribute or description; in iqrār, if a property is described (e.g., 'great'), the description must be given legal effect.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the minimum amount required for an iqrār by 'māl ʿaẓīm' according to the relied-upon Hanafi position (muftā bihī)?
A) 1 dirham
B) 10 dirhams
C) 200 dirhams
D) No minimum; any amount suffices

Key Takeaway
For iqrār bi al-māl al-ʿaẓīm, the Hanafi school requires the zakat nisab (200 dirhams) because the attribute 'great' is defined by Sharīʿa wealth standards.

Interpreting Iqrār by 'Great Wealths' and 'Many Dirhams'
Ruling with proof: minimums for iqrār by ambiguous expressions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the linguistic and sharʿī principles to determine the minimum amount due in an iqrār (acknowledgment) using the expressions 'great wealths', 'many dirhams', and 'dirhams'.

Core Idea
In iqrār, ambiguous terms like 'many dirhams' are interpreted by the least that gives effect to the attribute, guided by plural grammar or Sharʿī benchmarks.

This passage from Ashraf Ul Hadaya tackles practical cases of iqrār (legal acknowledgment). When someone admits owing 'great wealths' or 'many dirhams', what is the minimum amount they must pay? The Hanafi school applies linguistic rules and Sharʿī norms to resolve ambiguity. We'll examine the rulings for three expressions and the reasoning behind them, including a famous intra-madhhab dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the meaning of 'kathīra'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the expression
Determine which of the three expressions was used: 'amwāl ʿiẓām' (great wealths), 'darāhim kathīra' (many dirhams), or 'darāhim' (dirhams). Each has a different minimum.
The words 'iẓām' and 'kathīra' are adjectives that trigger specific interpretations.
2
Apply the least plural rule for 'amwāl ʿiẓām'
Since 'amwāl' is a plural, and 'iẓām' is an adjective applied to it, the least plural (jamaʿ qilla) is three. Therefore, the minimum is three nisabs of the specified type of wealth (e.g., 3×200 dirhams if dirhams are meant).
The text says 'estimation with three nisabs' – this is derived from the linguistic rule that the least plural is three.
3
Recognize the ikhtilāf for 'darāhim kathīra'
Imam Abu Hanifa holds the minimum is ten dirhams (linguistic basis: 10 is the end of the plural of few and the start of plural of multitude). The Sahibayn hold it is two hundred dirhams (sharʿī basis: owner of nisab is considered wealthy).
This is a pure intra-Hanafi ikhtilāf; both views have strong proofs.
4
Apply the least sound plural for 'darāhim'
If only 'darāhim' is said (no adjective), the minimum is three dirhams, as that is the least sound plural (jamaʿ salim). The acknowledger may later specify a larger number if plausible.
This ruling is agreed upon by all Hanafi imams.
5
Evaluate the proofs and criticism
Sadr al-Shariʿah criticized Abu Hanifa's reasoning for 'kathīra' because the linguistic rule about 10 being the end of plural applies only when a number accompanies the noun; in isolation, 'kathīra' could mean more than 10. The author of al-Ghāyah provided a better reasoning: the attribute 'kathīra' must not be rendered vain, so we take the least number that makes sense for 'many', which is the least plural of multitude (11?) but the practical result aligns with the Sahibayn.
This refinement shows how later Hanafi scholars engaged in naqd (scrutiny) and tarjih.

وَلَوْ قَالَ أَمْوَالٌ عِظَامٌ فَالتَّقْدِيرُ بِثَلَاثَةٍ نُصُبٍ مِنْ جِنسِ وفي نسخة : من اى فن) مَا سَمَّاهُ اعْتِبَارَ الْأَدْنَى الْجَمْعِ وَلَوْ قَالَ دَرَاهِمُ كَثِيرَةٌ لَمْ يُصَدَّقْ فِى أَقَلَّ مِنْ عَشَرَةِ وَهَذَا عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيْفَةٌ وَعِنْدَهُمَا لَمْ يُصَدَّقْ فِي أَقَلَّ مِنْ مِائَتَيْنِ لِاَنَّ صَاحِبَ النِّصَابِ مُكْثِرٌ حَتَّى وَجَبَ عَلَيْهِ مُوْاسَاةُ غَيْرَهُ بِخِلَافِ مَا دُونَهُ وَلَهُ أَنَّ الْعَشَرَةَ أَقْصَى مَا يَنْتَهِي إِلَيْهِ اِسْمُ الْجَمْعِ يُقَالُ عَشَرَةُ دَرَاهِمَ ثُمَّ يُقَالُ اَحَدَ عَشَرَ دِرْهَمًا فَيَكُونُ هُوَ الْأَكْثَرُ مِنْ حَيْثُ اللَّفْظِ فَيَنْصَرِفْ إِلَيْهِ وَلَوْ قَالَ دَرَاهِمُ فَهِيَ ثَلَاثَةٌ لِأَنَّهَا أَقَلُّ الْجَمْعِ الصَّحِيحِ إِلَّا أَنْ يُبَيِّنَ اَكْثَرَ مِنْهَا لَانَّ اللَّفْظَ يَحْتَمِلُهُ وَيَنْصَرِفُ إِلَى الْوَزْنِ الْمُعْتَادِ
ترجمہ اور اگر اموال عظام کہا تو اس نے جس جنس کے اموال بیان کئے ہیں اس کے تین نصابوں سے اندازہ ہو گا۔ ادنی جمع کا اعتبار کرتے ہوئے اور اگر کہا کہ دراہم کثیرہ ہیں تو دس سے کم میں تصدیق نہ ہوگی اور یہ امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک ہے۔ صاحبین کے نزدیک دو سو سے کم میں تصدیق نہ ہوگی۔ کیونکہ صاحب نصاب کثیر مال والا ہے۔ یہاں تک کہ اس پر دوسروں کی مواساة لازم ہے۔ بخلاف اس سے کم کے، امام ابوحنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ دس کا عدد انتہا ہے اس کی جس پر اسم جمع منتہی ہوتا ہے۔ بولتے ہیں عشرة دراہم پھر کہتے ہیں احد عشر درہنما تو لفظ کی حیثیت سے دس اکثر ہوا تو اسی کی جانب پھیرا جائے گا۔ اگر کہا کہ دراہم ہیں تو یہ تین ہوں گے۔ کیونکہ یہ جمع صحیح کا کمتر ہے۔ مگر یہ کہ وہ اس سے زیادہ بیان کرے۔ کیونکہ لفظ اس کا بھی محتمل ہے اور درہم وزن معتاد کی طرف منصرف ہوگا۔
تشریح قوله اموال عظام اس اقرار میں اس نے جس جنس کے اموال ( درہم، دینار، اونٹ وغیرہ) ذکر کئے ہوں۔ اسی جنس کے تین نصاب بیان کرنے سے اندازہ ہوگا بائیں لحاظ کہ ادنی جمع تین ہے اور دراہم کثیرہ کے اقرار میں امام صاحب کے نزدیک دس در اہم لازم ہوں گے اور صاحبین کے نزدیک نصاب زکوۃ سے کم میں تصدیق نہ ہوگی۔ کیونکہ شریعت کی نظر میں مکرہ ( مالدار ) صاحب نصاب ہی ہے۔ امام صاحب یہ فرماتے ہیں کہ دس کا عدد جمع کثرت کے مصداق کا ادنیٰ مرتبہ اور جمع قلت کا منتہی ہے تو لفظ کے اعتبار سے یہی اکثر ٹھہرا۔ فانه يقال عشرة دراهم ثم يقال احد عشر درهما یعنی جب عد دوس سے بڑھ جائے تو اس کا مینز مفرد آتا نہ کہ جمع ۔
قوله ان العشرة اقضى .... اس پر یہ اعتراض ہوتا ہے کہ دس کے عدد کامنتہی جمع ہونا اس وقت ہے جب اسم جمع عدد کے ساتھ مقترن ہو۔ ور نہ افراد کی حالت میں جمع کثرت سے مراد دس سے زیادہ الی الا نہایہ ہوسکتا ہے۔ اور یہاں مسئلہ حالت انفراد ہی کا ہے ۔ اس لئے صدرالشریعہ نے شرح وقایہ میں امام ابوحنیفہ کے قول کی تعلیل لان جمع الكثرة اقله عشرة کی بابت کہا ہے کہ یہ دو وجہ سے صحیح نہیں اولا اس لئے کہ جمع کثرت کا قول عدد گیارہ ہے نہ کہ دس چنانچہ محقق رضی نے بیان کیا ہے کہ مطلق جمع دو طرح پر ہے۔ جمع کثرت جمع قلت، اور جمع قلت سے مراد تین سے دس تک ہے۔ جس میں دونوں حدمیں داخل ہیں۔ اور کثیر سے مراد ما فوق العشر ہ ہے۔ ثانیا اس لئے کہ اگر قول امام کی حلت ، اقل جمع کثرت کا دس ہونا ہو تو لازم آتا ہے کہ وصف کثرت ذکر کئے بغیر کہ علی در اہم" کہنے کی صورت میں بھی آپ کے نزدیک دس سے کم میں تصدیق نہ ہو۔ حالانکہ اس صورت میں بالاتفاق تین مراد ہونے میں تصدیق ہوتی ہے کما سیاتی۔ پس بہتر تعلیل صاحب غایہ کی ہے کہ مقر کے کلام میں کثرت بحیثیت حکم نصا مذکور نہیں ہے۔ بلکہ اس کا ثبوت بایں ضرورت ہے کہ صفت کثرت کا ذکر لغو نہ ہو جائے۔ کیونکہ عرف و حقیقت کے اعتبار سے اس پر عمل متعذر ہے اور جو چیز صحت غیر کے مقتضاء سے ثابت ہو۔ وہ اتنی کمتر ثابت ہوتی ہے جس سے غیر کی صحت ہو سکے اور بحیثیت حکم جمع کا ادنیٰ مرتبہ جس سے
And if he said 'great wealths', then the estimation is with three nisabs from the genus (and in a copy: from whatever type) that he mentioned, considering the least plural. And if he said 'many dirhams', he will not be believed for less than ten (dirhams). And this is according to Abu Hanifa. According to the two companions (Sahibayn), he will not be believed for less than two hundred, because the owner of nisab is one of many wealth, so helping others is obligatory upon him, unlike what is less than that. And for him (Abu Hanifa) is that ten is the limit to which the name of plural ends. It is said 'ten dirhams', then it is said 'eleven dirhams'. So it is the most by way of wording, so it is turned to it. And if he said 'dirhams', then they are three, because it is the least of the sound plural, unless he explains more than that, because the wording can bear it. And it is turned to the usual weight. Translation: And if he said 'great wealths', then estimation will be by three nisabs of that which he specified, considering the least plural. And if he said 'many dirhams', then less than ten will not be accepted, and this is according to Imam Abu Hanifa. According to Sahibayn, less than two hundred will not be accepted, because the owner of nisab is one of many wealth, so helping others is obligatory upon him, unlike what is less. The proof of Imam Abu Hanifa is that the number ten is the end to which the noun of plural reaches. They say 'ten dirhams', then they say 'eleven dirhams'. So wording-wise it is the most, so it is turned to it. If he said 'dirhams', then they are three, because it is the least of the sound plural, unless he explains more, because the wording can bear it, and it is turned to the usual weight. Explanation of his saying: 'great wealths': In this acknowledgment, he mentioned wealths of a certain genus (dirhams, dinars, camels, etc.). The estimation will be by three nisabs of that genus, because the least plural is three. And in the acknowledgment of 'many dirhams', according to Imam Sahib, ten dirhams will be obligatory; according to Sahibayn, less than the zakat nisab will not be accepted, because in the view of Shari'ah, the rich person is the owner of nisab. Imam Sahib says that the number ten is the lowest level of the plural of multitude (jama' kathra) and the end of the plural of few (jama' qilla), so wording-wise it is the most. For example, they say 'ten dirhams', then 'eleven dirhams'. That is, when the count increases beyond ten, the modifier comes in singular, not plural. His saying: 'ten is the limit...' Objection is raised that ten being the end of plural is only when the noun of plural is accompanied by a number. Otherwise, in isolation, the plural of multitude may refer to more than ten ad infinitum. And here the issue is in the state of isolation. Therefore, Sadr al-Shari'ah in Sharh al-Wiqayah said regarding the reasoning of Imam Abu Hanifa that 'the plural of multitude has ten as its least' is not correct for two reasons: first, because the lowest plural of multitude is eleven, not ten, as verified by Muhaqqiq Radi: absolute plural is of two types: plural of multitude and plural of few. Plural of few refers to three to ten, including both limits. And 'kathīr' (many) means above ten. Second, because if the reason were that the least plural of multitude is ten, then it would follow that even without mentioning the attribute 'many', as in the case of saying simply 'dirhams', the acknowledger would not be believed for less than ten. But in that case, by consensus, three dirhams is accepted. So the better reasoning is by the author of al-Ghāyah: that 'many' in the speech of the acknowledger is not mentioned as a legal ruling; rather its proof is necessitated so that the description of 'many' is not void. Because it is impossible to act upon it by custom and reality. And something established by necessity of validity of another is established to the least extent that suffices to validate the other. And legally, the least level of plural is that which...
Source pages p. 53

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf Ul Hadaya deals with iqrār using the expressions 'amwāl ʿiẓām' (great wealths) and 'darāhim kathīra' (many dirhams). It also covers the simple plural 'darāhim' (dirhams). The commentator explains the rulings and the proofs, particularly the linguistic arguments. For 'amwāl ʿiẓām', if someone acknowledges 'great wealths', the minimum is three nisabs (e.g., three times the zakat nisab of the specified type) because the least plural (jama' qilla) is three, and the adjective 'great' is applied to each wealth unit. For 'darāhim kathīra', there is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the minimum is ten dirhams, because the term 'kathīra' (many) grammatically refers to the plural of multitude (jama' kathra), whose lowest is ten (or eleven according to some linguists). The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that 'many' means the owner of a nisab (200 dirhams), as the Shari'ah considers such a person rich and liable for zakat and support of others. The text then presents a grammatical analysis: the plural of few (jama' qilla) covers 3-10, and the plural of multitude starts from 11. Imam Abu Hanifa's proof uses the fact that 'ten dirhams' is said with plural, while 'eleven dirhams' switches to singular, indicating that ten is the maximum for plural form. The commentator refines this reasoning by citing Sadr al-Shari'ah, who objects that this rule applies only when the noun is accompanied by a number; in isolation (as in 'darāhim kathīra'), 'kathīra' can mean more than ten. The better reasoning is that the attribute 'kathīra' must be given effect, but since it cannot be precisely quantified, it is taken at the minimum that prevents it from being void, which is the least level of plural (three or ten depending on context). Finally, for the absolute 'darāhim', the minimum is three dirhams (the least sound plural), unless the acknowledger specifies more. The passage also emphasizes that the dirham is the standard weight (wazn mu'tād). The commentator mentions that the grammatical analysis is from al-Ghāyah and other authorities.

Key Terms
جمع قلت (Jama' Qilla): The plural of few, referring to three to ten items. In Arabic grammar, it is used for numbers 3-10.
جمع کثرت (Jama' Kathra): The plural of multitude, referring to eleven or more items. The lowest number for jama' kathra is eleven according to some scholars, but Abu Hanifa considers ten as the end of jama' qilla and thus the start of kathra.
نصاب (Nisab): The minimum amount of wealth that triggers obligations like zakat or the hadd punishment for theft. Here, it is used as a benchmark for 'great' property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the minimum amount for an iqrār by 'amwāl ʿiẓām' (great wealths)?
A) One nisab
B) Three nisabs
C) Ten dirhams
D) Two hundred dirhams

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi iqrār, ambiguous quantity expressions are interpreted by giving effect to the adjective, using either the least plural of few or a Shar'ī benchmark like the zakat nisab.

Interpreting Ambiguous Plural in Iqrar: Amwal 'Izam
Ruling on minimum for ambiguous plural in iqrar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the minimum amount required when a confession uses the phrase 'amwal 'izam' and apply it to any specified wealth type.

Core Idea
An ambiguous plural in iqrar is interpreted as the minimum plural: three nisabs.

When a person confesses to owing 'great wealths' without specifying a number, the law must fix a definite minimum. This lesson explains the Hanafi rule: the least plural (three) is taken, multiplied by the nisab of the wealth type mentioned. This ensures certainty in obligations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ambiguous element
The phrase 'amwal 'izam' is an indefinite plural with no number. Determine the wealth type (e.g., dirhams, camels).
The type must be named in the confession.
2
Apply the 'least plural' principle
According to Hanafi usul, the minimum plural is three. Multiply the nisab of the specified type by three.
One nisab is the zakat threshold for that wealth (e.g., 200 dirhams, 5 camels).
3
Calculate the amount due
Multiply: 3 × nisab of the named type. This is the minimum the confessor must pay.
If the confession is for multiple types, each is treated separately.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَوْ قَالَ أَمْوَالٌ عِظَامٌ فَالتَّقْدِيرُ بِثَلَاثَةٍ نُصُبٍ مِنْ جِنْسِ [وفي نسخة : من اى فن] مَا سَمَّاهُ اعْتِبَارَ الْأَدْنَى الْجَمْعِ
And if he said 'amwal 'izam', then the estimation is by three nisabs of the type he named, considering the least plural.
Source pages p. 53

Commentary
This ruling from the Book of Iqrar establishes that when a person confesses to owing 'amwal 'izam' (great wealths of a particular type, e.g., dirhams, dinars, camels), the minimum amount he must be held liable for is three nisabs of that type. The reason is that the Arabic plural 'amwal' is indefinite and the description 'izam' (great) does not specify a number; by default, it is taken to mean the minimum plural, which is three. This is the Hanafi position based on linguistic principles. There is no mention of disagreement here; it is a standard ruling.

Key Terms
أَمْوَالٌ عِظَامٌ (amwal 'izam): Great wealths — an ambiguous plural expression used in iqrar.
نَصَب (nisab): The threshold for zakat; used here as a measure of quantity for each type of wealth.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person confesses 'I owe amwal 'izam of dirhams' without specifying number, what is the minimum amount he must pay according to the Hanafi school?
A) 1 dirham
B) 3 dirhams
C) 200 dirhams (one nisab)
D) Three nisabs of dirhams (600 dirhams)

Key Takeaway
When a confession uses the ambiguous plural 'amwal 'izam', the Hanafi school fixes liability at three nisabs of the specified wealth type.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on 'Many Dirhams' (Darahim Kathirah)
Intra-Hanafi dispute on interpreting 'darahim kathirah'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the minimum for 'darahim kathirah' and explain each proof.

Core Idea
For Abu Hanifa, minimum is 10 dirhams (linguistic); for Sahibayn, minimum is 200 (nisab-based).

An ambiguous confession of 'many dirhams' requires a minimum number. This lesson examines the intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two students on what that minimum should be, exploring both linguistic and shariah-based reasoning.

Guided Path
1
State the issue
Identify the ambiguous phrase 'darahim kathirah' in an iqrar and the need to set a minimum enforceable amount.
The phrase triggers a dispute because 'kathirah' has no fixed numerical meaning.
2
Explain Abu Hanifa's position
He requires a minimum of 10 dirhams. Understand his linguistic proof: the plural form in Arabic extends up to ten; beyond ten the singular is used with the number.
Example: 'asharat darahim' (ten dirhams) but 'ahada 'ashara dirhaman' (eleven dirhams).
3
Explain the Sahibayn's position
They require a minimum of 200 dirhams (nisab). Understand their shariah-based proof: a person is not considered wealthy (mukthir) unless they possess a full nisab, as zakat and support obligations attach to that amount.
Nisab for silver is 200 dirhams.
4
Identify the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
The difference affects the rights of the claimant: under Abu Hanifa, the confessor pays at least 10 dirhams; under the Sahibayn, at least 200.
This could significantly alter the outcome in a court case.
5
Note the mufta bihi position
Later Hanafi scholars generally prefer Abu Hanifa's view due to the strength of the linguistic principle, though both views are valid within the school.
Tarjih authority: Commentators like al-Marghinani in al-Hidayah discuss the reasoning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَوْ قَالَ دَرَاهِمُ كَثِيرَةٌ لَمْ يُصَدَّقْ فِى أَقَلَّ مِنْ عَشَرَةِ وَهَذَا عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيْفَةٌ وَعِنْدَهُمَا لَمْ يُصَدَّقْ فِي أَقَلَّ مِنْ مِائَتَيْنِ لِاَنَّ صَاحِبَ النِّصَابِ مُكْثِرٌ حَتَّى وَجَبَ عَلَيْهِ مُوْاسَاةُ غَيْرَهُ بِخِلَافِ مَا دُونَهُ وَلَهُ أَنَّ الْعَشَرَةَ أَقْصَى مَا يَنْتَهِي إِلَيْهِ اِسْمُ الْجَمْعِ يُقَالُ عَشَرَةُ دَرَاهِمَ ثُمَّ يُقَالَ اَحَدَ عَشَرَ دِرْهَمًا فَيَكُونُ هُوَ الْأَكْثَرُ مِنْ حَيْثُ اللَّفْظُ فَيَنْصَرِفْ إِلَيْهِ
And if he said 'darahim kathirah' (many dirhams), he is not believed in less than ten—this is according to Abu Hanifa. And according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), he is not believed in less than two hundred, because the owner of nisab is considered wealthy such that he must support others, unlike less than that. And for him (Abu Hanifa) [the proof is] that ten is the maximum limit to which the name of plural reaches; one says 'asharat darahim' then one says 'ahada 'ashara dirhaman', so it is the most by way of wording, so it is referred to it.
Source pages p. 53

Commentary
This passage covers an important intra-Hanafi dispute on how to interpret 'many dirhams' in an iqrar. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the minimum that must be accepted is ten dirhams, because in Arabic, when you use the word 'darahim' (plural of dirham) with the adjective 'kathirah' (many), the word 'jam'' (plural) is normally used for numbers up to ten. After ten, you switch to the singular with the number (e.g., ahada 'ashara dirhaman). So the maximum plural is ten, and 'many' defaults to the maximum of the plural. The Sahibayn argue that a person is not considered wealthy (mukthir) unless he possesses at least one nisab (200 dirhams for silver), because the Shariah makes zakat obligatory on nisab, implying that the owner is wealthy and must support others. Therefore, a confession of 'many dirhams' is not binding for less than 200. The text presents both proofs. The later scholarly discussion in the book weighs the arguments, with many preferring Abu Hanifa's linguistic proof. The practical consequence: a person who says 'I owe you many dirhams' will be obligated to pay at least 10 dirhams according to Abu Hanifa, but 200 according to the Sahibayn.

Key Terms
دَرَاهِمُ كَثِيرَة (darahim kathirah): Many dirhams — an ambiguous expression indicating a large but unspecified number of dirhams.
مُكْثِر (mukthir): One who possesses a large amount of wealth; specifically the owner of nisab.
مُواسَاة (muwasah): Financial support for others, such as zakat or maintenance obligations.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, what is the minimum number of dirhams that constitutes 'darahim kathirah' in an iqrar?
A) 3
B) 10
C) 200
D) 600

Key Takeaway
The minimum for 'darahim kathirah' is 10 dirhams (Abu Hanifa, mufta bihi) or 200 (Sahibayn), with the difference arising from linguistic versus shariah reasoning.

Minimum Dirhams in Unqualified Confession
Specifies the minimum for the simple plural 'darahim' in iqrar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the minimum number of dirhams owed when a person confesses 'darahim' without qualification, and explain the basis in the Arabic plural.

Core Idea
A confession of 'darahim' binds you to at least three dirhams — the minimum plural.

This short passage settles a common ambiguity: when someone admits a debt of 'dirhams' without a number, how much must they pay? The Hanafi school answers with a clear rule grounded in Arabic grammar and customary weight. Understanding this ruling protects both the confessor and the claimant from uncertainty.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is an iqrar (confession) using the word 'darahim' without qualification. The ruling: the confessor must pay at least three dirhams.
2
Locate the linguistic basis
Why three? Because 'darahim' is a plural, and the least plural in Arabic is three. The text uses 'aqall al-jam' al-sahih' (least of the sound plural).
Although 'darahim' is a broken plural, the term 'jam' sahih' is used technically.
3
Note the exception
The confessor may specify a larger number because the word can bear it. If he specifies, that number applies.
4
Identify the weight standard
The dirham refers to the customary weight (wazn mu'tad), approximately 2.975 grams in the Hanafi school.
This ensures uniformity in payment.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَوْ قَالَ دَرَاهِمُ فَهِيَ ثَلَاثَةٌ لِأَنَّهَا أَقَلُّ الْجَمْعِ الصَّحِيحِ إِلَّا أَنْ يُبَيِّنَ اَكْثَرَ مِنْهَا لَانَّ اللَّفْظَ يَحْتَمِلُهُ وَيَنْصَرِفُ إِلَى الْوَزْنِ الْمُعْتَادِ
And if he said 'darahim' (dirhams), then it is three, because it is the least of the sound plural, unless he specifies more than that, because the word can bear it, and it is referred to the customary weight.
Source pages p. 53

Commentary
This ruling addresses the simple plural 'darahim' without any adjective. The minimum number that must be accepted is three, because the Arabic plural can denote three or more, and the least is three. However, the confessor is allowed to specify a larger number if he chooses, because the word is ambiguous and can bear more. Also, when it comes to weight, the dirham refers to the standard customary weight (about 2.975 grams per dirham in the Hanafi school). So if someone says 'I owe darahim', he must pay at least three dirhams of standard weight, unless he clarifies otherwise. The term 'jam' sahih' here is used in a broader sense to mean the minimum plural, even though 'darahim' is a broken plural; later commentaries clarify this point.

Key Terms
جَمْع صَحِيح (jam' sahih): Sound plural; used here to mean the minimum plural number (three), even though 'darahim' is a broken plural.
وَزْن مُعْتَاد (wazn mu'tad): Customary weight of a dirham, which in Hanafi fiqh is approximately 2.975 grams.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) 1
B) 2
C) 3
D) 10

Key Takeaway
When a person confesses 'darahim' without a number, the Hanafi school binds him to at least three dirhams of standard weight.

Determining the Minimum Owed with 'Kadha' in Acknowledgments
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the minimum owed when acknowledging debt with 'kadha'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the minimum owed when using the word 'kadha' in an acknowledgment, and evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute over whether the minimum is one, two, eleven, or twenty.

Core Idea
In ambiguity, the minimum certain is due: the Hanafi school settles on one dirham for 'kadha dirhaman' despite multiple views.

The word 'kadha' is a common kinayah for an unspecified number in acknowledgments. This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah explores the many possible interpretations and settles on the relied-upon view. We'll walk through the logical steps to determine the minimum owed, apply the principle of bará'at al-dhimmah, and understand why the Hanafi school ultimately opts for one dirham.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is an acknowledgment (iqrar) using the ambiguous word 'kadha'. The ruling is that the acknowledger owes the minimum number that the words can certainly bear, because iqrar is binding.
The ruling is wajib; the amount is determined by interpretation.
2
Understand the ambiguity of 'kadha'
'Kadha' is a kinayah for an unspecified number. It does not denote a specific quantity; its meaning is determined by context and linguistic principles.
The ambiguity triggers the principle of taking the least certain (aql mutayaqqin).
3
Apply the principle of bará'at al-dhimmah
The default is that the debtor's conscience is free from obligation. The words of acknowledgment must be interpreted in the way that imposes the least burden, as long as it is linguistically possible.
This principle tilts towards the minimum number.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi views
There are four main views within the Hanafi school: one dirham (Al-Hidayah), two dirhams (Jami' al-Saghir, etc.), eleven dirhams (Sahib al-Ghayah), and twenty dirhams (Ibn Qudamah from Imam Muhammad). Each relies on different interpretations of what 'kadha' can mean.
The disagreement is based on whether one is considered a number, the role of the accusative case, and the least number that can be interpreted by a singular accusative noun.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Al-Hidayah's view of one dirham is the relied-upon position because it adheres strictly to bará'at al-dhimmah and the linguistic fact that one is indeed a number.
This view is authoritative in the later school (fatawa mutakhkhirin).

Along with 'kadha', 21 dirhams would be obligatory. Because in the first case, he mentioned two numbers together without a conjunction. The least number interpreted in such a case is eleven, and the most is nineteen, so the least certain will be binding. In the second case, he mentioned them with a conjunction, whose least example is twenty-one. So each case will be applied to its example.  His statement: 'and he said, 'kadha dirhaman'... And if he says 'ala kadha dirhaman', then according to the relied-upon view, only one dirham is binding. Because the word 'dirham' is an interpretation of an ambiguous thing, and that is 'kadha'. Because it is a kinayah for an ambiguous number, and its least certain is one. So it will be applied to that. Imam Sharf al-Din Abu Hafs Umar ibn Muhammad al-Ansari al-Uqayli said in al-Minhaj that in this case, whatever he explains is binding.  First notice: The issue of 'ala kadha dirhaman' is mentioned in authoritative books like Jami' al-Saghir, Dhakhirah, Muhit, Tamh, and Fatawa Qadi Khan contrary to what the author of al-Hidayah mentioned. Thus in Jami' al-Saghir: 'If he says, I owe so-and-so kadha dirhaman, then two dirhams are due because this is rarely counted, because one is not counted until it is with something else.' Similarly in Fatawa Qadi Khan: 'If he says, I owe so-and-so kadha dinaran, then one dinar is due because 'kadha' is a kinayah for a number, and the least number is two.' Meaning, in the mentioned statement, two dirhams (or two dinars) would be binding, because one is not counted as a number until it is with something else.  Sahib al-Nata'ij objected that one not being a number is according to the terminology of arithmetic. In terms of linguistic usage, one is certainly a number. From this, the imams of language and grammar determined the basic number words to be twelve: from one to ten and the words 'hundred' and 'thousand'. In al-Sihah: 'al-ahad means al-wahid, and it is the first number.' In al-Radi: 'There is no disagreement among grammarians that the words wahid and ithnan are names of numbers. In arithmetic, one is not from the number because in their view number is what is more than one. Some even prevented two from being a number.' And it is clear that the word 'kadha' being a kinayah for number is not based on the terminology of arithmetic. Rather, it runs on the original linguistic usage. So arithmeticians' view that two is the least number does not require that in this mentioned issue two dirhams are wajib upon the acknowledger.  Second notice: Sahib al-Ghayah said that in the mentioned issue, eleven dirhams should be wajib, because it is the first number whose specific noun is in the accusative case. Therefore, one dirham should not be verified. And what qiyas requires is what is mentioned in Mukhtasar al-Asrar: 'He owes ten dirhams would be binding' (and Ibn Abd al-Hakam al-Maliki is the one who said it). The reason is that he mentioned one sentence and interpreted it by bringing the word 'dirham' in the accusative, and this occurs from tens to nineties, so the least certain, which is twenty, would be wajib.  Taj al-Shari'ah responded that the principle is the freedom of the dhimma (from obligation), so the least is established, because it is the certain. Sahib al-Nata'ij says this response is incomplete, because the principle of the dhimma being free requires that the least of what the acknowledger's words bear is established, not that the absolute least is established. So the correct response is that the acknowledger's mentioned statement in terms of having the specific noun in the accusative is similar to 'ahad 'ashar', but in the sense that 'ahad 'ashar' is a composed number, and the word 'kadha' is not composed. In this respect, it is not a likeness to 'ahad 'ashar' itself.  Third notice: Sahib al-Mi'raj said that Ibn Qudamah in the same meaning and Sahib al-Hilyah transmitted from Imam Muhammad: 'If he says 'kadha dirhaman', twenty dirhams are binding because it is the least number interpreted by the singular accusative.' This is contrary to al-Hidayah, Dhakhirah, Tamh, and Khaniyyah, and we have not found this in the well-known books of our associates. Sahib al-Nata'ij says: Perhaps the revered one did not see what is mentioned in Mukhtasar al-Asrar and Sharh al-Mukhtar, or he did not consider those among well-known books.
