If it is not interpreted, then if he mentions the word 'kadha' three times without conjunction, saying 'laha alayya kadha wa kadha aw kadha dirhaman', then 121 dirhams would be binding. Because with 'waw', the least of three numbers is 121? And if he says four times, then 1121 dirhams would be binding. Because its least expression is 1000 and 121? And for five times, 11,121, and six times, 111,121, and seven times, 1,111,121 dirhams would be binding. And so on as per its example.  His statement: 'and if three times 'kadha''... If the acknowledger said the word 'kadha' three times without a conjunction, then the same eleven dirhams would be binding. Because like that ambiguous number? [؟] besturdubo
Source pages p. 55

Commentary
This passage from the Book of Iqrar in Ashraf al-Hidayah discusses the interpretation of the word 'kadha' when used in an acknowledgment (iqrar) of a debt. The author begins by noting two scenarios: (1) if the acknowledger says 'kadha' twice without a conjunction, the minimum is eleven dirhams; (2) if with 'waw', the minimum is twenty-one. Then he discusses the basic case where someone says 'kadha dirhaman' (with accusative). The relied-upon view (mu'tamad) is that only one dirham is due, because 'kadha' is an ambiguous word referring to an indefinite number, and the minimum certain is one. However, Imam Sharf al-Din held that whatever he explains is due. The text then presents a tanbih (notice) that many esteemed books like Jami' al-Saghir, Dhakhirah, Muhit, and Fatawa Qadi Khan contradict al-Hidayah's view. They argue that 'kadha' is a kinayah for number, and the least number is two, because one is not counted as a number in common usage. Sahib al-Nata'ij objects that in linguistics, one is indeed a number. Another view from Sahib al-Ghayah says that the minimum is eleven, because the accusative case (nasb) indicates a number from eleven to ninety-nine. Sahib al-Mi'raj reports that Ibn Qudamah and al-Hilyah transmitted from Imam Muhammad that twenty is due, but the author says this is not found in well-known books of the school. Taj al-Shari'ah responds that the principle is to adhere to the minimum (bará'at al-dhimmah), but Sahib al-Nata'ij counters that the minimum of what the words can bear is not absolute. The passage then discusses repetitions of 'kadha' multiple times, with calculations for three, four, five, six, seven times without conjunction. Finally, it mentions that if 'kadha' is said three times without conjunction, eleven dirhams are due. The overall lesson is that the word 'kadha' is ambiguous, and the Hanafi school has multiple views on its interpretation, with the mufta bihi generally being the minimum one dirham in the basic case, but the issue remains complex.

Key Terms
كذا (kadha): An ambiguous word used as a kinayah for an unspecified number in acknowledgments.
إقرار (iqrar): A legal acknowledgment or confession of a right or debt.
اقل متيقن (aql mutayaqqin): The minimum number that is certain or verified, used as a basis for determining liability.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, when someone says 'له على كذا درهما' without any explanation, how many dirhams are owed according to the mu'tamad view?
A) One
B) Two
C) Eleven
D) Twenty

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, the minimum owed when acknowledging with the word 'kadha' is one dirham, despite multiple intra-Hanafi views, due to the principle of bará'at al-dhimmah.

Acknowledgment of Debt vs Trust: Key Arabic Words
Differentiating debt and trust acknowledgments

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between debt and trust acknowledgments based on the Arabic words used ('ala, qibli, indi, etc.) and apply the Hanafi principle of taking the lesser (akhdh al-aqall) where applicable.

Core Idea
The word used in an acknowledgment determines whether it is debt or trust; 'ala' and 'qibli' indicate debt, 'indi' etc. indicate trust.

This passage from the Book of Iqrar (Acknowledgment) in al-Hidayah addresses a critical distinction: the words 'ala', 'qibli', 'indi', and similar terms each carry specific legal implications. The Hanafi school, through rigorous linguistic analysis and reliance on Quranic usage, determines whether these words establish a debt (dayn) or a trust (amanah). Understanding this distinction is essential for proper adjudication of claims and for issuing accurate fatwas in financial disputes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two main categories of acknowledgment words
The passage divides words into two groups: those that indicate debt ('ala, qibli) and those that indicate trust (indi, ma'i, fi bayti, etc.). Note the reasoning for each.
Debt words impose obligation; trust words indicate possession.
2
Analyze the proof for 'ala'
'Ala' is proven to be a formula of obligation (sighat ijab) by the Quranic verse (Al-Imran 3:97). Obligation on the dhimma means debt.
The verse: 'ولله على الناس حج البيت' shows 'ala' for obligation.
3
Examine the dispute over 'qibli'
Some copies of Mukhtasar al-Quduri consider 'qibli' as trust; the Hanafi mufta bihi is debt, supported by derivation from 'qabala' meaning guarantee.
The tarjih by al-Hidayah declares the debt view 'asahh' (more correct).
4
Apply the lesser principle to possession words
For words like 'indi', possession can be debt or trust; since the lesser is trust (amanah), the acknowledgment is taken as trust unless evidence of debt.
This is akhdh al-aqall, a standard Hanafi principle.
5
Explore the connected vs. separated exception
If the acknowledger immediately adds 'it is a trust' after 'ala' or 'qibli', he is believed because the word metaphorically allows it. If separated, not believed.
Connected (mawsul) clarification is accepted; disconnected (mafsul) is not.

Source Text

قَالَ وَأنْ قَالَ لَهُ عَلَيَّ اَوْ قِبَلِي فَقَدْ أَقَرَّ بِالدِّينِ لِاَنَّ عَلَى صِيغَةُ إِيجَابِ وَقِبْلِي يُنبِيءُ عَنِ الضَّمَانِ عَلَى مَامَرَّ فِي الْكِفَالَةِ وَلَوْ قَالَ الْمُقِرُّ هُوَ وَدِيعَةٌ وَوَصَلَ صُدِقَ لاَنَّ اللَّفْظَ يَحْتَمِلُهُ مَجَازًا حَيْثُ يَكُونُ الْمَضْمُونَ حَفِظَهُ وَالْمَالُ مَحَلَّهُ فَيُصَدَقَ مَوْصُوْ لا لَا مَفْصُوْلًا قَالَ وَفِي بَعْضِ نُسَخِ الْمُخْتَصَرِ فِي قَوْلِهِ قِبَلِي أَنَّهُ إِقْرَارٌ بِالْآمَانَةِ لَانَّ اللَّفْظَ يَنْتَظِمُهَا حَتَّى صَارَ قَوْلَهُ لَا حَقَّ لِى قِبَلَ فُلَانِ إِبْرَاء عَنِ الدَّيْنِ وَالْآمَانَةِ جَمِيعًا وَالْآمَانَةُ أَقَلَّهُمَا وَالْأَوَّلُ أَصَحَ وَلَوْ قَالَ عِنْدِي أَوْ مَعِي أَوْ فِي بَيْتِي أَوْ فِي كِيْسِى اَوْ فِي صُندُوقِي فَهُوَ إِقْرَارٌ بِإِمَانَةٍ فِي يَدِهِ لِاَنَّ كُلَّ ذَالِكَ إِقْرَارٌ بِكُونِ الشَّيءِ فِي يَدِهِ وَذَالِكَ يَتَنَوَّعُ إِلَى مَضْمُونِ وَآمَانَةٍ فَيَثْبُتُ أَقَلُّهُمَا
ترجمہ اگر کہا کہ فلاں کا مجھے پر یا میری طرف ہے تو اس نے قرض کا اقرار کر لیا۔ کیونکہ کلہ علی صیغہ ایجاب ہے اور لفظ قبلی ضمان کی خبر دیتا ہے جیسا کہ کفالہ میں گذر چکا۔ اگرچہ مقر نے کہا کہ وہ ودیعت ہے۔ اور اس کو متصل کیا تو تصدیق کی جائے گی۔ کیونکہ لفظ مجاڑا اس کا مشتمل ہے کہ حفظ و دیعت کا ضامن ہوتا ہے۔ اور مال محل حفاظت ہے تو تصدیق کی جائے گی۔ موصولاً۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ مختصر القدوری کے بعض نسخوں میں ہے کہ قبلی کہنے میں امانت کا اقرار ہے۔ کیونکہ لفظ دونوں کو شامل ہے۔ یہاں تک کہ اس کا یہ کہنا کہ فلاں کی جانب میر احق کچھ نہیں قرض وامانت دونوں سے بری کرنا ہے۔ اور ان میں امانت کمتر ہے۔ لیکن پہلا قول اصبح ہے۔ اگر کہا کہ میرے پاس یا میرے ساتھ یا میرے گھر یا میری تھیلی یا میرے صندوق میں ہے۔ تو یہ اس کے قبضہ میں امانت ہونے کا اقرار ہے۔ اس لئے کہ ہر لفظ سے شئی کے اپنے قبضہ میں ہونے کا اقرار ہے اور قبضہ دو طرح کا ہوتا ہے۔ مضمون اور امانت تو ان میں سے کمتر ثابت ہو جائے گا۔
تشریح قوله علی او قبلی اگر میر نے له على كذا ياله قبلی کذا کہا تو یہ قرضہ کا اقرار ہوگا۔ پہلی صورت میں تو اس لئے کہ اس کے قول میں دین اگرچہ صراحت مذکور نہیں۔ تا ہم کلہ علی ایجاب میں مستعمل ہے۔ قال الله تعالى "والله على الناس حج البيت" اورمحل ایجاب ذمہ ہے۔ اور ثابت فی الذمہ دین ہوتا ہے نہ کہ عین، اور دوسری صورت میں اس لئے کہ لفظ قبلی ضامن ہونا بتلاتا ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ نز دم سے عبارت ہے۔ اس لئے ضمانت کے کاغذ کو قبالہ اور کفیل کو قبیل کہتے ہیں۔ قوله ولو قال المقر اگر میر نے لہ علی یا بیلی کے بعد متصلا یہ کہا۔ " ھو ودیعت تو اس کی تصدیق کی جائے گی۔ کیونکہ آغاز کلام حیثیت مجاز اس کا محتمل ہے۔ بایں معنی کہ وہ حفاظت ودیعت کا ضامن ہوتا ہے۔ اور مال محل حفاظت ہے۔ پس اس نے محل ودیعت بول کر حال یعنی حفاظت کا ارادہ کیا ہے جو مجاڑ ا جائز ہے كما يقال نهر جار ۔
قوله و في بعض نسخ ... یعنی مختصر القدوری کے بعض نسخوں میں ہے کہ قبیلی کہنا امانت کا اقرار ہے اس لئے کہ لفظ قبل امانت اور قرضہ ہر دو کو شامل ہے۔ یہاں تک کہ اگر کوئی یہ کہے کہ لاحق کی قبل فلان تو یہ قرضہ اور امانت دونوں سے بری کرنا ہوتا ہے۔ جس کی تصریح مبسوط میں موجود
He said: And if he says 'he owes me' or 'what is towards me', then he has acknowledged a debt, because 'ala' is a formulation of obligation, and 'qibli' indicates guarantee as passed in the chapter of kafalah. If the acknowledger says 'it is a trust' and connects it, he is believed, because the word metaphorically allows it, as the guaranteed thing is its preservation, and the wealth is the place of preservation. So he is believed when connected, not when separated. He said: In some copies of al-Mukhtasar regarding his saying 'qibli', it is an acknowledgment of a trust, because the word includes it, to the extent that his saying 'I have no right towards so-and-so' is a discharge from both debt and trust, and the trust is the lesser of the two. The first is more correct. And if he says 'with me' or 'in my possession' or 'in my house' or 'in my purse' or 'in my chest', then it is an acknowledgment of a trust in his hand, because all of that is an acknowledgment of the thing being in his hand, and that is divided into guaranteed and trust, so the lesser of the two is established.  Translation: If he said 'so-and-so has upon me' or 'towards me', then he has acknowledged a debt. Because the word 'ala' is the formula of obligation, and the word 'qibli' indicates guarantee, as passed in kafalah. If the acknowledger said 'it is a trust' and connected it, he is believed. Because the word metaphorically contains that he is the guarantor of preservation, and the wealth is the place of preservation. So he is believed when connected. The author of al-Hidayah says: In some copies of Mukhtasar al-Quduri regarding 'qibli', it is an acknowledgment of a trust, because the word includes both. To the extent that his saying 'I have no right towards so-and-so' is a discharge from both debt and trust, and among them the trust is lesser. But the first statement is more correct. If he said 'in my possession' or 'with me' or 'in my house' or 'in my purse' or 'in my chest', then it is an acknowledgment of a trust in his possession. Because every word is an acknowledgment of the thing being in his possession, and possession is of two types: guaranteed and trust. So the lesser of the two will be established.  Explanation of his statement: 'Ala' or 'Qibli': If the acknowledger said 'laha alayya kadha' or 'la qibli kadha', then it is an acknowledgment of debt. In the first case, because in his statement 'debt' is not explicitly mentioned, but 'ala' is used in the sense of obligation. Allah says: 'And for Allah upon the people is the pilgrimage to the House.' And the place of obligation is the dhimma, and what is established in the dhimma is debt, not a specific item. In the second case, because the word 'qibli' indicates being a guarantor, as it is derived from 'nadm' (?) so the guarantee document is called 'qabalah' and the guarantor is called 'qabil'. His statement: 'and if the acknowledger said': If the acknowledger connectedly said after 'ala' or 'qibli' 'it is a trust', then he is believed. Because the beginning of the speech metaphorically allows it, in the sense that he is the guarantor of the preservation of the trust, and the wealth is the place of preservation. So by saying 'trust' he intended the condition, i.e., preservation, which is metaphorically permissible, as it is said 'a flowing river'.  His statement: 'and in some copies': That some copies of Mukhtasar al-Quduri say that saying 'qibli' is an acknowledgment of a trust, because the word 'qibl' includes both trust and debt. To the extent that if someone says 'there is no right for me towards so-and-so', it is a discharge from both debt and trust. The clarification of which is present in al-Mabsut.
Source pages p. 56

Commentary
This passage from the Book of Iqrar discusses how different Arabic words used in an acknowledgment indicate whether the speaker is acknowledging a debt (dayn) or a trust (amanah). The matn (original text) states that if someone says 'علي' (upon me) or 'قبلي' (towards me), it is an acknowledgment of a debt (dīn). The reason: 'علي' is a formula of obligation, and 'قبلي' indicates guarantee (ḍamān), as established in the chapter of kafālah. If the acknowledger immediately adds that it is a trust (وديعة), he is believed, because the word 'علي' can metaphorically be interpreted as being responsible for preservation. However, if he separates the statements, he is not believed. The text then notes a variation: in some copies of Mukhtasar al-Quduri, 'قبلي' is considered an acknowledgment of a trust, because the word covers both debt and trust, and the lesser (trust) is taken. The author of al-Hidayah favors the first view (debt). Finally, the passage covers words like 'عندي' (with me), 'معي' (in my possession), 'في بيتي' (in my house), 'في كيسي' (in my purse), 'في صندوقي' (in my chest). These indicate possession, and possession can be either as a guarantee (debt) or trust. Since the lesser is trust, such acknowledgments are taken as acknowledgment of a trust (amanah). The commentary further explains that for 'علي', the proof is the Quranic verse about Hajj, where 'على' imposes an obligation, and obligation is on the dhimma, which is the place of debt. For 'قبلي', it is derived from 'قبال' meaning guarantee.

Key Terms
علي (ala): A preposition meaning 'upon', used in acknowledgments to indicate an obligation or debt.
قبلي (qibli): A preposition meaning 'towards me' or 'in my possession', used in acknowledgments to indicate a guarantee.
أمانة (amanah): Trust; an item held for safekeeping without liability for loss unless negligence occurs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if someone says 'عندي كذا', what is the default interpretation?
A) Debt
B) Trust
C) Ambiguous
D) Invalid

Key Takeaway
The Arabic word used in an acknowledgment determines its legal nature: 'ala' and 'qibli' signal debt, while 'indi' and similar words signal trust, with the possibility of rebuttal by connected clarification.

8 min
Ali and Qibli as Admission of Debt: Hanafi Ruling and Proof
Ruling that 'ali' and 'qibli' indicate debt admission

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that saying 'ali' or 'qibli' constitutes an admission of debt, explain the linguistic proof from Qur'an and kafalah, and identify when the confessor's immediate clarification of deposit is accepted.

Core Idea
Ali and qibli are clear admissions of debt; only immediate clarification can shift to trust.

When someone says 'upon me' or 'towards me' regarding property, does that mean they admit a debt or merely that they hold a trust? The Hanafi school has a clear ruling with a precise linguistic proof. In this lesson, we will explore how the words 'ali' and 'qibli' act as formulas of obligation, and examine an exception that allows the confessor to reduce his liability if he clarifies immediately. We will also look at a internal disagreement within the school on the interpretation of 'qibli' alone.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is saying 'upon me' (علي) or 'towards me' (قبلي) in relation to property. The ruling is that this constitutes an admission of debt (دين), not trust (أمانة).
The admission is sahih (valid) and binding on the speaker.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof for 'ali' is that it is the formula of obligation (صيغة إيجاب) in Arabic, as used in Quran 3:97. The proof for 'qibli' is that it derives from 'qabala' (to accept guarantee) and is used in kafalah (suretyship).
The dalil is linguistic and qiyas from established usage.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
For 'ali': the imperative (al-amr) implies obligation in Hanafi usul. The word 'ala' places the debt in the dhimmah. For 'qibli': it indicates guarantee, and guarantee entails debt liability.
The word 'ala' itself is a sarīḥ (clear) indication of obligation.
4
Analyze the exception
If the confessor immediately (متصلاً) says 'it is a deposit' (وديعة), he is believed because the word 'ali' can be interpreted metaphorically as 'responsibility of preservation'.
This is a majāz (metaphorical) interpretation, accepted only when the clarification is connected.
5
Evaluate the intra-madhhab dispute
Some copies of Mukhtasar al-Quduri state that 'qibli' alone indicates trust, because the word encompasses both debt and trust and the lesser (trust) is established. The author of Hidayah declares the first opinion (debt) as more correct.
The mufta bihi is the debt interpretation, ruling in favor of the claimant.

علی اور قبلی کے الفاظ سے اقرار کیا تو اقرار بالدین ہے
قَالَ وَأنْ قَالَ لَهُ عَلَيَّ اَوْ قِبَلِي فَقَدْ أَقَرَّ بِالدِّينِ لِاَنَّ عَلَى صِيغَةُ إِيجَابِ وَقِبْلِي يُنبِيءُ عَنِ الضَّمَانِ عَلَى مَامَرَّ فِي الْكِفَالَةِ وَلَوْ قَالَ الْمُقِرُّ هُوَ وَدِيعَةٌ وَوَصَلَ صُدِقَ لاَنَّ اللَّفْظَ يَحْتَمِلُهُ مَجَازًا حَيْثُ يَكُونُ الْمَضْمُونَ حَفِظَهُ وَالْمَالُ مَحَلَّهُ فَيُصَدَقَ مَوْصُوْ لا لَا مَفْصُوْلًا قَالَ وَفِي بَعْضِ نُسَخِ الْمُخْتَصَرِ فِي قَوْلِهِ قِبَلِي أَنَّهُ إِقْرَارٌ بِالْآمَانَةِ لَانَّ اللَّفْظَ يَنْتَظِمُهَا حَتَّى صَارَ قَوْلَهُ لَا حَقَّ لِى قِبَلَ فُلَانِ إِبْرَاء عَنِ الدَّيْنِ وَالْآمَانَةِ جَمِيعًا وَالْآمَانَةُ أَقَلَّهُمَا وَالْأَوَّلُ أَصَحَ وَلَوْ قَالَ عِنْدِي أَوْ مَعِي أَوْ فِي بَيْتِي أَوْ فِي كِيْسِى اَوْ فِي صُندُوقِي فَهُوَ إِقْرَارٌ بِإِمَانَةٍ فِي يَدِهِ لِاَنَّ كُلَّ ذَالِكَ إِقْرَارٌ بِكُونِ الشَّيءِ فِي يَدِهِ وَذَالِكَ يَتَنَوَّعُ إِلَى مَضْمُونِ وَآمَانَةٍ فَيَثْبُتُ أَقَلُّهُمَا

ترجمہ اگر کہا کہ فلاں کا مجھے پر یا میری طرف ہے تو اس نے قرض کا اقرار کر لیا۔ کیونکہ کلہ علی صیغہ ایجاب ہے اور لفظ قبلی ضمان کی خبر دیتا ہے جیسا کہ کفالہ میں گذر چکا۔ اگرچہ مقر نے کہا کہ وہ ودیعت ہے۔ اور اس کو متصل کیا تو تصدیق کی جائے گی۔ کیونکہ لفظ مجاڑا اس کا مشتمل ہے کہ حفظ و دیعت کا ضامن ہوتا ہے۔ اور مال محل حفاظت ہے تو تصدیق کی جائے گی۔ موصولاً۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ مختصر القدوری کے بعض نسخوں میں ہے کہ قبلی کہنے میں امانت کا اقرار ہے۔ کیونکہ لفظ دونوں کو شامل ہے۔ یہاں تک کہ اس کا یہ کہنا کہ فلاں کی جانب میر احق کچھ نہیں قرض وامانت دونوں سے بری کرنا ہے۔ اور ان میں امانت کمتر ہے۔ لیکن پہلا قول اصبح ہے۔ اگر کہا کہ میرے پاس یا میرے ساتھ یا میرے گھر یا میری تھیلی یا میرے صندوق میں ہے۔ تو یہ اس کے قبضہ میں امانت ہونے کا اقرار ہے۔ اس لئے کہ ہر لفظ سے شئی کے اپنے قبضہ میں ہونے کا اقرار ہے اور قبضہ دو طرح کا ہوتا ہے۔ مضمون اور امانت تو ان میں سے کمتر ثابت ہو جائے گا۔

تشریح قوله علی او قبلی اگر میر نے له على كذا ياله قبلی کذا کہا تو یہ قرضہ کا اقرار ہوگا۔ پہلی صورت میں تو اس لئے کہ اس کے قول میں دین اگرچہ صراحت مذکور نہیں۔ تا ہم کلہ علی ایجاب میں مستعمل ہے۔ قال الله تعالى "والله على الناس حج البيت اورمحل ایجاب ذمہ ہے۔ اور ثابت فی الذمہ دین ہوتا ہے نہ کہ عین، اور دوسری صورت میں اس لئے کہ لفظ قبلی ضامن ہونا بتلاتا ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ نز دم سے عبارت ہے۔ اس لئے ضمانت کے کاغذ کو قبالہ اور کفیل کو قبیل کہتے ہیں۔ قوله ولو قال المقر اگر میر نے لہ علی یا بیلی کے بعد متصلا یہ کہا۔ " ھو ودیعت تو اس کی تصدیق کی جائے گی۔ کیونکہ آغاز کلام حیثیت مجاز اس کا محتمل ہے۔ بایں معنی کہ وہ حفاظت ودیعت کا ضامن ہوتا ہے۔ اور مال محل حفاظت ہے۔ پس اس نے محل ودیعت بول کر حال یعنی حفاظت کا ارادہ کیا ہے جو مجاڑ ا جائز ہے كما يقال نهر جار ۔

قوله و في بعض نسخ ... یعنی مختصر القدوری کے بعض نسخوں میں ہے کہ قبیلی کہنا امانت کا اقرار ہے اس لئے کہ لفظ قبل امانت اور قرضہ ہر دو کو شامل ہے۔ یہاں تک کہ اگر کوئی یہ کہے کہ لاحق کی قبل فلان تو یہ قرضہ اور امانت دونوں سے بری کرنا ہوتا ہے۔ جس کی تصریح مبسوط میں موجود ہے
If he says: 'upon me' or 'towards me' then he has admitted debt because 'ala' is a formula of obligation and 'qibli' indicates guarantee as passed in kafalah. If the confessor says it is a deposit and connects (his statement), he is believed because the word can bear it metaphorically, as the guarantor is the one who preserves and the property is the place of preservation, so he is believed if connected, not if disconnected. He said: In some copies of al-Mukhtasar it says that saying 'qibli' is an admission of trust because the word encompasses both, so much so that his saying 'I have no right towards so-and-so' is an acquittal from both debt and trust, and trust is the lesser of them, and the first is more correct. And if he says 'in my possession' or 'with me' or 'in my house' or 'in my purse' or 'in my box' then it is an admission of trust in his hand because all of that is an admission of the thing being in his hand, and that is divided into guaranteed and trust, so the lesser of them is established. Translation: If he said 'so-and-so is upon me' or 'towards me', then he admitted debt because 'ala' is a formula of obligation and 'qibli' informs of guarantee as passed in kafalah. If the confessor said it is a deposit and connected it, he is believed because the word metaphorically includes that he is the guarantor of preservation and the property is the place of preservation, so he is believed when connected. The author of Hidayah says: In some copies of Mukhtasar al-Quduri it states that saying 'qibli' is an admission of trust because the word encompasses both, so much so that his saying 'I have no right towards so-and-so' is an acquittal from both debt and trust, and the lesser of them is trust, but the first opinion is more correct. If he said 'in my possession' or 'with me' or 'in my house' or 'in my purse' or 'in my box', then it is an admission of trust in his possession because each word is an admission of the thing being in his possession, and possession is of two types: guaranteed and trust, so the lesser of them is established. Elaboration on 'ala' and 'qibli': If someone said 'he has upon me such-and-such' or 'towards me such-and-such', it is an admission of debt. In the first case, because the word 'ala' is used for obligation. Allah says 'And upon Allah is the Hajj of the House' (3:97) and the place of obligation is the dhimmah (liability) and what is established in the dhimmah is debt, not a specific object. In the second case, because the word 'qibli' indicates being a guarantor, as it is from 'qabala' (to accept), so the document of guarantee is called 'qabalah' and the guarantor is called 'qabil'. His statement: 'If the confessor ...' If the confessor after saying 'upon me' or 'towards me' immediately says 'it is a deposit', he is believed because the beginning of the statement can bear it metaphorically, meaning that he is the guarantor of preserving the deposit, and the property is the place of preservation, so he intended the deposit's place, i.e., preservation, which is permissible metaphorically, as in the saying 'a flowing river' (nahar jarin). His statement: 'And in some copies...' meaning that in some copies of Mukhtasar al-Quduri, it is stated that saying 'qibli' is an admission of trust because the word 'qibal' includes both trust and debt, so much so that if someone says 'I have no right towards so-and-so', it is an acquittal from both debt and trust, as explicitly stated in al-Mabsut.
Source pages p. 56

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Kitab al-Iqrar (Book of Confession) in the Hanafi school. The author first states the rule: when someone says 'upon me' (علي) or 'towards me' (قبلي) in relation to property, it constitutes an admission of debt (دين), not trust (أمانة). The proof is linguistic: 'على' is the formula of obligation (إيجاب) in Arabic, as used in the Qur'anic verse 'ولله على الناس حج البيت' (And upon Allah is the Hajj of the House), and the place of obligation is the dhimmah (legal liability), which contains debt, not a specific object. The word 'قبلي' indicates guarantee (ضمان), as it derives from 'قبالة' (a document of guarantee) and 'قبيل' (guarantor). This was explained earlier in the chapter on kafalah (suretyship). The passage then addresses an exception: if the confessor immediately (متصلاً) clarifies that the property is a deposit (وديعة) and he is merely its guardian, he is believed because the word 'upon me' can be interpreted metaphorically as 'upon me is the responsibility of preservation' (حفظ). This is a permissible metaphorical usage, like saying 'a flowing river' (نهر جار), where the adjective describes the river's continuous flow, not a separate attribute. The condition is that the clarification must be connected (موصولاً) and not separate (مفصولاً), otherwise it is not accepted. The text then records a disagreement within the Hanafi school: in some copies of Mukhtasar al-Quduri, it is reported that 'قبلي' alone indicates trust, because the word encompasses both debt and trust. The evidence is that the phrase 'لا حق لي قبل فلان' (I have no right towards so-and-so) is used as a complete acquittal from both debt and trust, implying that 'قبل' covers both. Among the two possibilities, trust is the lesser (أقل), so when the word is ambiguous, the lesser is established (as a default to avoid excess liability). However, the author of Hidayah declares the first opinion (that it indicates debt) to be more correct (الأول أصح). Finally, the passage rules that phrases like 'at my side' (عندي), 'with me' (معي), 'in my house' (في بيتي), etc., are admissions of trust (أمانة) because they only affirm possession (يد), which can be either guaranteed (مضمون = debt) or trust, and the lesser (trust) is established. This is a default principle in Hanafi fiqh: when a word is ambiguous between a binding and a non-binding obligation, the lesser is taken.

Key Terms
على (‘alā): A preposition meaning 'upon', used as a formula of obligation (صيغة إيجاب) in admissions of debt.
قبلى (qiblī): A prepositional phrase meaning 'towards me' or 'in my direction', interpreted as an admission of debt due to its connection with guarantee.
إقرار (iqrār): A legal confession or admission of a right (such as debt) that creates a binding obligation.
وديعة (wadī‘ah): A deposit: property entrusted to someone for safekeeping without compensation.
أمانة (amānah): Trust: property held in one's possession without liability for loss unless due to negligence or violation.
ضمان (ḍamān): Guarantee or liability: the obligation to compensate for loss or to pay debt.
مجاز (majāz): Metaphorical usage: a word used in a sense other than its literal meaning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as presented in this passage, if someone says 'I have a thousand towards you' and the respondent says 'Weigh it' (اتزنها) with the pronoun 'ha', what is the ruling?
A) It is an admission of the debt because the pronoun refers to the claimed amount.
B) It is not an admission because the response is ambiguous.
C) It is an admission only if the respondent says 'I owe you' explicitly.
D) It is an admission of trust, not debt.

Key Takeaway
The words 'ali' and 'qibli' are clear admissions of debt in Hanafi law, with immediate clarification of deposit as the only accepted exception.

Implicit Admissions in Debt Claims: Responses as Iqrar
Ruling that responses like 'weigh it' imply admission of debt

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that certain responses (with the pronoun 'ha') to a debt claim constitute an admission and distinguish cases where the pronoun is omitted.

Core Idea
Saying 'weigh it' or 'test it' with the pronoun admits the debt — the pronoun ties the response to the claim.

When a creditor says 'You owe me a thousand,' how should the debtor's reply be interpreted? In Hanafi law, certain replies contain an implicit admission. This lesson explores which responses create a binding admission and why the presence or absence of a pronoun is crucial.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
Determine what the respondent said and whether it counts as an admission (iqrar). The passage lists several responses.
2
Locate the proof (dalil)
Find the reasoning: linguistic (pronoun reference) and rational (presupposition of obligation).
The pronoun 'ha' is key for 'atzen' and 'intaqid'; for others, the verbs themselves imply the debt.
3
Understand the linguistic condition
Note that without the pronoun 'ha', 'atzen' or 'intaqid' do not refer back to the claim and thus are not admissions.
This distinguishes Hanafi position from those who always deny admission.
4
Note the ikhtilaf (inter-madhhab dispute)
Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Ahmad hold that even with 'ha', these phrases are not admissions. Recognize their argument and the Hanafi response.
The Hanafi response: the pronoun makes it a direct response affirming the claim.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is the Hanafi view, adopted by al-Marghinani in al-Hidayah.
This is a consistent Hanafi approach to implicit admissions.

And if a man says to him: 'I have a thousand owed to me by you' and he says: 'Weigh it' or 'Test it' or 'Give me a deferment for it' or 'I have paid you' then that is an admission because the 'ha' in the first and second is a pronoun referring back to the mentioned in the claim, as if he said 'Weigh the thousand that you have upon me' so that if he does not mention the letter of the pronoun, it is not an admission because of the lack of reference to the mentioned. And deferment only occurs for a due right, and payment follows obligation, and the claim of acquittance is like payment as we have explained, and likewise the claim of charity and gift because making someone owner requires precedence of obligation. And likewise if he said: 'I have transferred it to so-and-so' because it is a transfer of debt. Translation: Someone said to him: 'I have a thousand owed to me by you.' He said: 'Weigh them' or 'Test them' or 'Give me a deferment for them' or 'I have paid you' then this is an admission because the pronoun 'ha' in the first two refers back to what was mentioned in the claim, so it is as if he said 'Weigh the thousand that you have upon me.' And if he does not mention the pronoun, it is not an admission because it does not refer back to the mentioned. And deferment is only for a due right, and payment follows obligation. And the claim of acquittance is like payment. Similarly, the claim of charity and gift, because making someone owner requires prior obligation. Similarly, if he said: 'I have transferred it to so-and-so' because it is a transfer of debt. Elaboration: A person said to Zayd: 'I have a thousand upon you.' Zayd replied: 'Weigh them, test them, give me a deferment for them, or I have paid you, or I have transferred them to so-and-so' in all these cases Zayd has admitted the thousand to that person because the pronoun 'ha' in 'atzenha' and 'intaqidha' refers back to that thousand, so it is a response to his speech i.e., affirmation, not denial or independent speech. If Zayd said without the pronoun 'atzin' or 'intaqid', then nothing becomes binding because it is independent speech and not a response. Imam Shafi'i and Imam Ahmad say 'atzen' and 'intaqid' with or without 'ha' are not admissions. Some Malikis also hold this view. Ibn Sahnun al-Maliki says it is an admission in both forms. Some followers of Shafi'i also narrate our view. As for the issue of term (muhlat), giving deferment can only be for a right that is due. The benefit of the issue is a general principle: words that are capable of being a response and not capable of being an independent statement are considered a response. Words capable of being an independent statement but not a response, or not capable of either, are considered independent speech. His statement: 'Claim of acquittance etc.' If the confessor claims in the mentioned speech that he was acquitted, it is like claiming payment, i.e., it is an admission of the obligation. Because acquittance occurs only after obligation. Also if he said 'You gave me as charity or gift', it is still an admission of obligation because making him owner requires prior obligation.
Source pages p. 57

Commentary
This passage from Kitab al-Iqrar presents a ruling with proof on how certain responses to a debt claim constitute an admission (iqrar). The scenario: a claimant says 'You owe me a thousand.' If the respondent says 'Weigh it' (اتزنها), 'Test it' (انتقدها), 'Give me time' (أجلني بها), 'I have paid you' (قضيتكها), or 'I have transferred it to so-and-so' (أحلتك بها على فلان), all these are admissions of the debt. The proof is linguistic and rational: the pronoun 'ha' (ها) in the first two phrases refers back to the claimed thousand, so the respondent is essentially saying 'Weigh the thousand that you claim upon me.' This shows acknowledgment. If the pronoun is omitted, e.g., just 'weigh' (اتزن) without 'ha', it is not an admission because there is no reference to the claim. For deferment (أجلني), it logically presupposes an existing due obligation, so saying 'give me time' admits the debt. Payment (قضيتكها) also presupposes a prior obligation. Similarly, acquittance (إبراء) and gifting (صدقة/هبة) imply that the debt existed first, because one cannot be acquitted of something that is not owed, and one cannot gift what one does not own. Transfer of debt (حوالة) is also a conversion of an existing debt. The passage then records the inter-madhhab dispute: Imam Shafi'i and Imam Ahmad hold that 'weigh' or 'test' even with the pronoun is not an admission, while the Hanafi position (supported by some Shafi'i followers and Ibn Sahnun al-Maliki) is that it is an admission with the pronoun. The commentary concludes with a general principle (قاعدة كلية): words that can function as a response (جواب) to a preceding statement and cannot stand alone as an independent statement are treated as a response (admission). Words that can stand alone are independent and not an admission. The Hanafi ruling is mufta bihi.

Key Terms
إقرار (iqrār): A legal admission that creates an obligation; here it arises from responses that presuppose a pre-existing debt.
كناية (kināyah): A pronoun or expression that refers indirectly to something; here the pronoun 'ha' is a kinayah for the claimed thousand.
تحويل الدين (taḥwīl al-dayn): Transfer of debt to another person (hawalah); saying 'I have transferred it to so-and-so' admits the original debt.
إبراء (ibrā’): Acquittance or release from a debt; claiming it admits the debt existed.
أجل (ajal): Deferment or grace period; requesting it implies the debt is due and recognized.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if someone is told 'you owe me a thousand' and he responds 'I have transferred it to Zayd' (أحلتك بها على زيد), what is the ruling?
A) It is not an admission because transfer of debt is a separate transaction.
B) It is an admission because the transfer presupposes the debt was owed.
C) It is an admission only if the transfer is proven by witnesses.
D) It is a denial of the debt.

Key Takeaway
A response that presupposes the existence of a debt, either through a pronoun referencing the claim or through the nature of the verb (e.g., deferment, payment), is a valid admission in Hanafi law.

Responses That Constitute Iqrār: The Role of the Pronoun
Ruling on phrases that imply acknowledgment of a debt

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on which verbal responses constitute iqrār and distinguish between responses with and without a pronoun, applying the principle to new scenarios.

Core Idea
A response with a pronoun referencing the claimed amount is iqrār; without it, it is not.

When someone claims a debt, the respondent's words can unintentionally create a binding admission. The Hanafi school carefully analyses the wording: a simple 'weigh it' without a pronoun is not an admission, but 'weigh it' with a pronoun ('utznha') is. This lesson unpacks the linguistic reasoning (talil) behind this ruling and the practical difference it makes across madhahib.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and responses
The claimant says: 'You owe me a thousand.' List all responses given in the text that are deemed iqrār (e.g., 'Weigh it', 'Take it in cash', etc.). Notice they all contain a pronoun referring to 'the thousand'.
2
Locate the legal reasoning (talil)
The author explains why these responses are iqrār: the pronoun 'haa' is a kināyah (indirect reference) that points back to the claimed amount. Thus the response affirms the claim rather than denying or remaining silent.
3
Analyze the role of the pronoun
If the pronoun is omitted (e.g., just 'utzn' without 'haa'), the statement is separate and does not constitute iqrār. The pronoun is the decisive factor because it creates a direct link to the debt.
Also note the extension to ibra', sadaqah, hibah, and hawalah – each presupposes the debt's existence.
4
Identify the ikhtilaf
Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Ahmad hold that even with the pronoun, the response is ambiguous and not an iqrār. Some Malikis agree with them, while others and some Shafi'i followers align with the Hanafi view.
5
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf
In practice, under Hanafi law, saying 'utznha' binds you to the debt; under Shafi'i law, it does not. This affects litigation and financial obligations.
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَوْ قَالَ لَهُ رَجُلٌ لِي عَلَيْكَ اَلَفٌ فَقَالَ اتَّزَنْهَا أوْ انْتَقِدْهَا أَوْ أَجَّلَنِي بِهَا أَوْ قَدْ قَضَيْتُكَهَا فَهُوَ إِقْرَارٌ لِاَنَّ الْهَاءَ فِي الْأَوَّلِ وَالثَّانِي كِنَايَةٌ عَنِ الْمَذْكُورِ فِى الدَّعْوى فَكَانَّهُ قَالَ اَتَزِنْ الألْفَ التِي لَكَ عَلى حَتَّى لَوْ لَمْ يَذْكُرْ حَرَقَ الْكِنَايَةِ لَا يَكُونُ إِقْرَارًا لِعَدَمِ اِنْصِرَافِهِ إِلَى الْمَذْكُورِ وَالتَّاجِيلُ إِنَّمَا يَكُونُ فِي حَقِّ وَاجِبِ وَالْقَضَاءُ يَتْلُو الْوُجُوبَ وَدَعْوى الْإِبْرَاءِ كَالْقَضَاءِ لِمَا بَيَّنَّا وَكَذَا دَعْوَى الصَدَقَةِ وَالْهِبَةِ لِاَنَّ التَّمْلِيْكَ يَقْضِي سَابَقَةُ الوُجُوْب وَكَذَا لَوْ قَالَ أحَلْتُكَ بِهَا عَلَى فُلان لِأَنَّهُ تَحويل الدين ترجمہ: کسی نے اس سے کہا کہ میرے تجھے پر ہزار ہیں۔ اس نے کہا۔ ان کو تول لے یا پر کچھ لے یا ان کی مجھے مہلت دے یا میں تجھ کو دے چکا ہوں۔ تو یہ اقرار ہے اس لئے کہ ہا ضمیر اول و دوم میں اسی سے کنایہ ہے جو دعویٰ میں مذکور ہے تو گویا اس نے کہ کہا کہ تقول لے وہ ہزار جو تیرے مجھ پر ہیں۔ یہاں تک کہ اگر وہ حرف کنایہ ذکر نہ کرے تو اقرار نہ ہوگا۔ مذکور کی طرف منصرف نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے اور مہلت دینا حق واجب ہی میں ہوتا ہے اور چکانا وجوب کے پیچھے ہوتا ہے۔ اور بری کرنے کا دعوی مثل چکانے کے ہے۔ ایسے ہی صدقہ اور ہبہ کا دعویٰ ہے۔ کیونکہ مالک بنانا سابقیت وجوب کو چاہتا ہے۔ ایسے ہی اگر یہ کہا ۔ کہ میں نے اس کو فلاں پر احاطہ کیا تھا۔ کیونکہ یہ دین کی تحویل ہے۔ تشریح قوله ولو قال له رجل ایک شخص نے زید سے کہا کہ میرے تجھ پر ایک ہزار ہیں۔ زید نے جواب میں کہا کہ ان کو وزن کر لے پارکھ لے یا ان کی مہلت دے یا میں تجھ کو دے چکا ہوں یا میں ان کا فلاں پر حوالہ کر چکا ہوں تو ان سب صورتوں میں زید کی طرف سے اس شخص کے لئے ایک ہزار کا اقرار ہے۔ کیونکہ اتر نہا، انتقد ہا، جملوں میں ہار ضمیر انہیں ہزار کی طرف راجع ہے تو یہ اس کے کلام کا جواب یعنی اثبات ہوانہ کہ انکار یا کوئی جدا گانہ کلام ہاں اگر زید نے بلا ضمیر یوں کہا کہ اتزن انتقد تو کچھ لازم نہ ہوگا کیونکہ یہ جدا گانہ کلاء ہے نہ کہ اس کے کلام کو جواب ، امام شافعی اور امام احمد فرماتے ہیں کہ اتزن اور انتقد میں اقرار نہ ہوگا۔ ہاء کے ساتھ ہو یا بلا ہاء، امام مالک کے بعض اصحاب بھی اسی کے قائل ہیں۔ ابن سحنون مالکی کہتے ہیں کہ دونوں صورتوں میں اقرار ہوگا اور بعض اصحاب امام شافعی سے ہمارے قول کے مثل بھی منقول ہے۔ رہا میعاد کا مسئلہ سومہلت دینا اسی حق اور کامسئلہ دینا میں ہو سکتا ہے جو واجب ہو۔ فائدہ مسئلہ کا قاعدہ کلیہ یہ ہے کہ جو کلام جواب ہوے کی صلاحیت رکھتا ہو۔ اور ابتداء کلام ہونے کی صلاحیت نہ رکھتا ہے اور جو ابتداء کلام ہونے کی صلاحیت رکھتا ہو۔ تو اس کو جواب ٹھہرایا جاتا ہے۔ اور جو ابتداء کلام ہونے کی صلاحیت رکھتا ہو۔ اور جواب ہونے کی صلاحیت نہ رکھتا ہو یا دونوں کی صلاحیت نہ رکھتا ہو تو اس کو جدا گانہ کلام مظہرایا جاتا ہے۔ قوله دعوى الابراء.. الخ اگر مقر نے قول مذکور میں بری کر دینے کا دعوی کیا تو یہ ایساہی ہے جیسے ادا کر دینے کا دعوی کرنا۔ یعنی واجب ہونے کا اقرار ہوگا۔ کیونکہ بری کرنا وجوب کے بعد ہی ہوگا۔ نیز اگر اس نے کہا کہ تو نے مجھے صدق یا ہبہ کر دیے تھے۔ تب بھی واجب ہونے کا اقرار ہوگا۔ اس لئے کہ پہلے وہ واجب ہوئے تب اس نے قرضدار کو مالک کیا۔
And if a man said to him, 'I have a thousand against you,' and he said, 'Weigh it' or 'Take it in cash' or 'Give me time for it' or 'I have paid it to you,' it is iqrār because the pronoun in the first and second is a kināyah of the mentioned in the claim, so it is as if he said, 'Weigh the thousand that you have over me.' But if he did not mention the letter of kināyah, it is not iqrār due to lack of reference to the mentioned. And deferment is only in a right that is obligatory, and payment follows obligation. The claim of discharge is like payment, as we explained. Similarly, the claim of charity and gift, because ownership requires prior obligation. Similarly, if he said, 'I have transferred it to so-and-so,' because it is a transfer of debt. Translation: Someone said to him, 'You owe me a thousand.' He said, 'Weigh them, or take them in cash, or give me time for them, or I have paid them to you.' So this is iqrār because the pronoun 'ha' in the first and second is a kināyah of what was mentioned in the claim, so it is as if he said, 'Weigh the thousand that you have over me.' But if he did not mention the letter of kināyah, it would not be iqrār due to lack of reference. And deferment is only in a right that is obligatory, and payment follows obligation. The claim of discharge is like payment. Similarly, the claim of charity and gift, because ownership requires prior obligation. Similarly, if he said, 'I have transferred it to so-and-so,' because it is a transfer of debt. Commentary: Regarding his statement 'And if a man said to him...' A person said to Zayd, 'You owe me a thousand.' Zayd replied, 'Weigh them, test them, give me time for them, or I have paid them to you, or I have transferred them to so-and-so.' In all these cases, Zayd has acknowledged the thousand. Because the pronoun 'ha' in the phrases 'weigh them' etc. refers to that thousand, so it is a response to his speech affirming the claim, not a denial or separate statement. If Zayd said without the pronoun, 'Weigh' or 'Test,' nothing is binding because it is a separate statement, not a response. Imam Shafi'i and Imam Ahmad say that 'weigh' and 'test' do not constitute iqrār, whether with 'ha' or without. Some Maliki scholars also hold this view. Ibn Sahnun al-Maliki says that both forms constitute iqrār. Some followers of Shafi'i also narrate a view similar to ours. As for the issue of the term: granting time can only be for a right that is obligatory. Benefit: The general principle is that speech that is capable of being a response and not capable of being an initial statement is considered a response. And speech that is capable of being an initial statement and not capable of being a response, or incapable of both, is considered a separate statement.
Source pages p. 57

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the Kitab al-Iqrār. It states that when a claimant says 'You owe me a thousand,' the respondent's reply with phrases like 'Weigh it' or 'Take it in cash' or 'Give me time' or 'I have paid it' constitutes an acknowledgment (iqrār) of the debt. The reasoning is that the pronoun 'haa' in these responses refers back to the claimed amount, so the statement effectively affirms the claim. If the respondent omits the pronoun and simply says 'Weigh' or 'Take,' it is not iqrār because the statement is not connected to the claim. The ruling extends to claims of discharge (ibra'), charity (sadaqah), gift (hibah), and transfer (hawalah) because each of these presupposes the existence of a prior obligation. The commentary then discusses a general principle: a statement that can serve as a response but cannot stand alone as an initial utterance is considered a response. It also records an ikhtilaf: Imams Shafi'i and Ahmad hold that 'utzn' and 'intiqid' do not constitute iqrār even with the pronoun, while some Maliki scholars agree with the Hanafi position. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school is that such responses do constitute iqrār when the pronoun is used, based on the principle that the pronoun establishes reference to the claimed amount.

Key Terms
إقرار (iqrār): Acknowledgment of a right or debt owed to another.
كناية (kināyah): Indirect reference via pronoun; here the pronoun 'haa' refers to the claimed amount.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if someone claims a debt of 1000 and the respondent says 'Weigh it' without a pronoun, is that an iqrār?
A) Yes
B) No
C) Depends on intention
D) Only if witness present

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a verbal response that includes a pronoun referencing the claimed amount constitutes an iqrār, binding the respondent to the debt.

Iqrār of Deferred Debt: When the Creditor Denies the Deferment
Ruling on iqrār of deferred debt

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that an iqrār of a deferred debt becomes immediately due when the creditor denies the deferment, and explain the qiyas to the slave-and-lease case.

Core Idea
The debtor's acknowledgment creates immediate liability; a claim of deferment is a contradictory right not accepted.

When someone acknowledges a debt but claims it is deferred, and the creditor denies the deferment, Hanafi fiqh holds the debt is due at once. This ruling is derived through qiyas on the case of acknowledging a slave in one's hand while claiming a lease. The underlying principle is that the acknowledgment establishes a right for the beneficiary, and any contradictory claim by the acknowledger is not accepted. An exception exists for qualities like blackness in coins, which do not affect the immediate obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the ruling
The text presents: a person acknowledges a deferred debt (dayn mu'ajjal). The creditor confirms the debt but denies the deferment. The Hanafi ruling: the debt is due immediately (lāzimun hālan).
This is the core rule.
2
Locate the qiyas (analogy) used
The ruling is based on qiyas to the case of iqrār of a slave in one's hand with a claim of lease (ijārah). In that case, the claim of lease is not accepted, and the slave is considered owned by the beneficiary. Similarly here, the claim of deferment is not accepted.
The qiyas is jaliy (clear) because the 'illa is evident.
3
Extract the 'illa (effective cause)
The 'illa is that the acknowledger acknowledges a right belonging to another (the debt/slave) and simultaneously claims a right for himself (deferment/lease) that contradicts the immediate effect of the acknowledgment. This contradiction renders his claim invalid.
The 'illa is 'contradiction between acknowledgment and additional claim'.
4
Note the exception: black dirhams
The text distinguishes the case of black dirhams (black coins). Blackness is a quality (sifah) that does not create a separate contradictory right. The issue was already discussed in the chapter of kafālah.
Exception shows that only claims that contradict the acknowledgment itself are rejected, not mere descriptions.
5
Recognize the procedural element: oath
The creditor (muqarru lahu) is to take an oath (yamīn) that there was no deferment. This is because the creditor is the one denying the deferment, and the oath falls on the denier.
The oath confirms the immediate nature of the debt.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَمَنْ اَقَرَّ بِدَيْنِ مُؤَجَّلٍ فَصَدَقَهُ الْمُقَرُ لَهُ فِي الدَّيْنِ وَكَذَبَهُ فِي التَّاجِيْلِ لَزِمَهُ الدَّيْنُ حَالًا لِأَنَّهُ أَقَرَّ عَلَى نَفْسِهِ بِمَالٍ وَادَّعَى حَقًّا لِنَفْسِهِ فِيْهِ فَصَارَ كَمَا إِذَا أَقَرَّ بَعِبْدِ فِي يَدِهِ وَادَّعَى الْإِجَارَةِ بِخِلَافِ الْإِقْرَارِ بِالدَّرَاهِم السُّودِ لِأَنَّهُ صِفَةُ فِيْهِ وَقَدْ مَرَّتِ الْمَسْأَلَةُ فِي الْكِفَالَةِ. قَالَ وَيَسْتَحْلِفُ الْمُقَرُّ لَهُ عَلَى الْأَجَلِ لِأَنَّهَ مُنْكَرٌ حَقًّا عَلَيْهِ وَالْيَمِينُ عَلَى الْمُنْكَرِ ترجمہ: جس نے اقرار کیا دین میعادی کا اور تصدیق کی اس کی مقرلہ نے دین میں اور تکذیب کی میعاد میں تو لازم ہوگا۔ اس کو دین فی الحال کیونکہ خود پر اس نے مال کا اقرار کر کے اس میں اپنے لئے حق کا دعویٰ کیا ہے تو ایسا ہو گیا ہے جیسے اس غلام کا اقرار کیا جو اس کے قبضہ میں ہے۔ اور اجارہ کا دعویٰ کیا۔ بخلاف سیاہ درہموں کے اقرار کے کیونکہ سیاہ ہونا ان کی ایک صفت ہے۔ اور یہ مسئلہ باب الکفالہ میں گزر چکا اور مدت میں مقرلہ سے قسم لی جائے گی۔ کیونکہ وہ اپنے اوپر ایک حق کا منکر ہے اور قسم منکر پر ہی ہوتی ہے تشریح قوله وان اقرب دین ایک شخص نے دین مؤجل کا اقرار کیا اور مقلہ نے دعوی کیا کہ دین مؤجل نہیں فوری ہے تو مقر پر دین فوری لازم ہوگا۔ اور مقرلہ سے اس بات پر قسم لی جائے گی۔ کہ دین کی کوئی مدت نہیں تھی۔ کیونکہ مقر نے حق غیر کے اقرار کے ساتھ اپنے لئے حق تا جیل کا دعوی کیا ہے۔ پس یہ ایسا ہو گیا جیسے کوئی دوسرے کے لئے غلام کا اقرار کرے اور ساتھ ساتھ یہ بھی دعویٰ کرے کہ میں نے اس سے یہ غلام بطریق اجارہ لیا ہے کہ اس صورت میں مقر کی تصدیق نہیں ہوتی۔ تو یہاں بھی تصدیق نہ ہوگی۔ امام احمد کے نزدیک اور ایک قول کے لحاظ سے امام شافعی کے
He said: Whoever acknowledges a deferred debt, and the beneficiary confirms the debt but denies the deferment, the debt becomes due immediately, because he acknowledged a sum against himself and claimed a right for himself in it. So it is like when he acknowledges a slave in his hand and claims lease (ijarah). Unlike acknowledgment of black dirhams because it is a quality in them, and this issue has passed in the chapter of kafalah. He said: And the beneficiary shall be made to take an oath regarding the term, because he is denying a right against himself, and the oath is upon the denier. Translation: Whoever acknowledged a deferred debt, and the beneficiary confirmed the debt but denied the term, the debt becomes due immediately, because he acknowledged wealth against himself and claimed a right for himself in it. So it becomes like when he acknowledged a slave in his hand and claimed lease. Unlike acknowledgment of black dirhams, because blackness is a quality in them. This issue has passed in the chapter of kafalah. And the beneficiary will be made to take an oath regarding the term, because he is denying a right upon himself, and the oath is upon the denier. Commentary: Regarding his statement 'And whoever acknowledges a deferred debt,' a person acknowledged a deferred debt and the beneficiary claimed that the debt is not deferred but immediate, so the immediate debt becomes binding on the acknowledger. And the beneficiary will be made to take an oath on this matter that the debt had no term. Because the acknowledger, along with acknowledging the right of another, claimed a right for himself (the right of deferment). So this becomes like when someone acknowledges a slave for another and simultaneously claims that he has taken the slave on lease from him: in that case, his acknowledgment is not believed. Similarly here, his claim of deferment is not believed. According to Imam Ahmad and according to one narration from Imam Shafi'i.
Source pages p. 58

Commentary
This passage deals with the scenario where a person acknowledges a debt but claims it is deferred (mu'ajjal), and the creditor denies the deferment. The Hanafi ruling is that the debt is due immediately (hālan). The reasoning is based on qiyas to the case of iqrār of a slave: if someone says 'This slave in my hand belongs to so-and-so' and then claims 'I have leased him from that person,' his claim of lease is not accepted because it contradicts his prior acknowledgment. Similarly, here the acknowledgment of the debt implies immediate liability, and the additional claim of deferment is a separate right that the acknowledger is asserting for himself, which is not accepted because it contradicts the immediate obligation. An exception is made for black dirhams (black coins), which are considered a quality that does not affect the liability. The ruling also includes that the creditor must take an oath (yamin) regarding the term, since he is denying a right (the deferment) and the oath is incumbent on the denier. The commentary notes that Imam Ahmad and some narrations from Imam Shafi'i agree with this ruling.

Key Terms
دين مؤجل (dayn mu'ajjal): A debt with a fixed future payment date.
تاجيل (ta'jīl): Deferment, postponement of payment.
يمين (yamīn): Oath sworn by the creditor denying the deferment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The debt is due after one year.
B) The debt is due immediately and the creditor takes an oath.
C) The debtor's claim of deferment is accepted on his oath.
D) The case goes to a judge to decide.

Key Takeaway
An acknowledgment of debt creates immediate obligation; any contradictory claim by the acknowledger is rejected by qiyas to the slave-lease case.

The General Principle: Movable vs Immovable Containers
Ruling with talil on acknowledgment in containers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that acknowledgment of an item in a movable container includes both container and content, while for an immovable container only the content is included per Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
Acknowledgment in a movable container includes both; an immovable container only the content.

When someone acknowledges that they owe an item described as being inside a container, the legal ruling depends on whether the container can be moved. This lesson explains the principle articulated by Imam Muhammad and the two shaykhs, and how to determine liability in such cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acknowledgment statement
The person says 'I owe/I acknowledge dates in a basket' or 'a horse in a stable.' The container is specified.
The key is the description of the item as being 'in' something.
2
Determine if the container is movable
If the container can be physically transported (e.g., basket, handkerchief), it is movable. If it is fixed (e.g., stable, house), it is immovable.
This is the primary distinction in the Hanafi school.
3
Apply the ruling per the two shaykhs
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf rule: for movable containers, both container and content are owed. For immovable containers, only the content is owed.
They consider that for immovables, the container is not generally included.
4
Apply Imam Muhammad's ruling
Imam Muhammad rules that both container and content are owed regardless of movability, because the preposition 'fi' indicates inclusion.
This is a stricter view, giving more weight to the literal wording.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله ومن اقر بتمر في زنبيل فعليه التمر والزنبيل عند محمد. ولو اقر بفرس في اصطبل فعليه الفرس فقط عند ابي حنيفة وابي يوسف، وعند محمد الفرس والاصطبل. والاصل ان ما كان ظرفا قابلا للنقل فالاقرار به يلزم الظرف والمظروف، وما لا يقبل النقل كالاصطبل فعند الشيخين يلزم المظروف فقط، وعند محمد يلزمان. ولو قال غصبت من قوصرة فعليه التمر فقط لان من للانتزاع. ولو قال غصبت تمرا في زنبيل فعليه التمر والزنبيل لان في للظرفية. ولو اقر بخاتم فعليه حلقة وفصه لان الاسم شامل. ولو اقر بسرير فعليه الخشب والستر لان العرف يشمله. ولو اقر بثوب في منديل فعليه الثوب والمنديل لان المنديل ظرف. ولو قال ثوب في ثوب فعليها في العشرة لان الثوب ليس ظرفا للثوب بل كل ثوب مظروف بالنسبة لغيره.
And whoever acknowledges dates in a basket, then upon him are the dates and the basket according to Muhammad. And if he acknowledges a horse in a stable, then upon him is only the horse according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, and according to Muhammad, the horse and the stable. The principle is that whatever is a container capable of being moved, the acknowledgment necessitates both the container and the content; and what is not capable of being moved like a stable, then according to the two shaykhs only the content is necessary, and according to Muhammad both are necessary. And if he said 'I usurped from a basket,' then upon him is only the dates because 'min' indicates extraction. And if he said 'I usurped dates in a basket,' then upon him are the dates and the basket because 'fi' indicates containment. And if he acknowledged a signet ring, then upon him is its band and its stone because the name includes both. And if he acknowledged a bed, then upon him are the wood and the curtain because custom covers it. And if he acknowledged a garment in a handkerchief, then upon him are the garment and the handkerchief because the handkerchief is a container. And if he said 'a garment in a garment,' then [the ruling] is as in ten garments because a garment is not a container for another garment but each garment is contained relative to another.
Source pages p. 60

Commentary
This lesson presents the Hanafi rulings on acknowledgments where the subject is described as being in a container (zarf). The key distinction is whether the container is movable (manqul) or immovable. For movable containers like a basket (zambil) or handkerchief (mindil), Imam Muhammad holds that both the container and the content are owed, while the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) agree in such cases? Actually the text indicates that for movable containers Muhammad's position is that both are owed; the two shaykhs differ only for immovable containers like a stable. The text then gives examples: 'ghasabtu min' (usurped from) only obligates the thing taken, while 'ghasabtu fi' (usurped in) obligates both. For items like a ring (khatam) or bed (sarir), the name in custom includes both parts. The principle is that the word 'fi' (in) is interpreted as containment only if the container is properly so.

Key Terms
ظرف (zarf): Container; the object that holds something else.
مظروف (mazruf): Contents; the item that is contained.
قابل للنقل (qabil lil-naql): Capable of being moved, transportable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, if someone acknowledges a horse in a stable, what is owed?
A) Only the horse
B) Both the horse and the stable
C) Only the stable
D) Neither

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes movable and immovable containers in acknowledgments; the two shaykhs' view, which excludes immovable containers, is the mufta bihi.

Prepositions and Composite Items in Acknowledgment
Rulings on acknowledgment with examples of prepositions and composite items

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rulings for acknowledgment cases involving the prepositions 'min' and 'fi', and for composite items like rings and beds that are customarily referred to as a whole.

Core Idea
Preposition 'fi' includes the container; 'min' excludes it; customary names cover composite parts.

The Arabic language and custom play a key role in Hanafi fiqh. This lesson examines how prepositions affect liability in acknowledgment cases, and how composite items (like a ring or bed) are treated because their names encompass all components.

Guided Path
1
Identify the preposition in the acknowledgment
If the person says 'ghasabtu min' (I usurped from), only the item taken is owed. If 'ghasabtu fi' (I usurped in), both container and content are owed.
The preposition is legally significant.
2
Distinguish composite items
For items like a ring (khatam) or bed (sarir), the name in custom includes all parts (band and stone, wood and curtain).
No need to specify each part; the name suffices.
3
Apply the container rule to other examples
Garment in handkerchief: both owed because handkerchief is a movable container. Garment in garment: each is a zawf relative to the other, so the ruling is like ten garments (details follow).
The last example shows that if the item is not a proper container, different rules apply.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And whoever acknowledges dates in a basket, then upon him are the dates and the basket according to Muhammad. And if he acknowledges a horse in a stable, then upon him is only the horse according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, and according to Muhammad, the horse and the stable. The principle is that whatever is a container capable of being moved, the acknowledgment necessitates both the container and the content; and what is not capable of being moved like a stable, then according to the two shaykhs only the content is necessary, and according to Muhammad both are necessary. And if he said 'I usurped from a basket,' then upon him is only the dates because 'min' indicates extraction. And if he said 'I usurped dates in a basket,' then upon him are the dates and the basket because 'fi' indicates containment. And if he said 'a garment in a garment,' then [the ruling] is as in ten garments because a garment is not a container for another garment but each garment is contained relative to another.

This lesson presents the Hanafi rulings on acknowledgments where the subject is described as being in a container (zarf). The key distinction is whether the container is movable (manqul) or immovable. Actually the text indicates that for movable containers Muhammad's position is that both are owed; the two shaykhs differ only for immovable containers like a stable. The text then gives examples: 'ghasabtu min' (usurped from) only obligates the thing taken, while 'ghasabtu fi' (usurped in) obligates both. Key Terms
من (min): Preposition meaning 'from'; indicates extraction, not inclusion.
في (fi): Preposition meaning 'in'; indicates containment.
خاتم (khatam): Signet ring; in custom includes the band (hallaqah) and stone (fass).

Acknowledgment of a Garment Among Ten: The ‘Fi’ Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on an ambiguous acknowledgment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad regarding an acknowledgment of 'a garment among ten garments,' explain the linguistic basis of their disagreement, and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
The meaning of 'fi' in an acknowledgment determines liability—one or eleven garments.

In this lesson, we examine an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad concerning an ambiguous acknowledgment. A person says, 'I owe you a garment among ten garments.' Does he owe one garment or eleven? The answer hinges on whether the Arabic preposition 'fi' is interpreted as 'contained in' or 'among.' We will analyze the linguistic arguments and determine the relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
State the acknowledgment and the two rulings
Write down exactly what was acknowledged and the two conflicting outcomes—one garment (Abu Yusuf) vs. eleven garments (Muhammad).
2
Understand Muhammad’s argument
Muhammad argues that 'fi' can indicate containment, as a precious garment may be wrapped in ten others. Thus, all eleven are owed.
The key is the possibility of being a container (zarf).
3
Understand Abu Yusuf’s argument
Abu Yusuf cites Qur’anic usage where 'fi' means 'among' (Surah Al-Fajr 89:29). He also notes that each of the ten is a mazruf (contained) and cannot be a zarf, making containment impossible. So doubt occurs.
The Qur’an citation is: 'So enter among My servants.'
4
Apply the principle of bara’at al-dhimma
Because the meaning is ambiguous and containment is impossible, doubt remains. The default is freedom from liability, so only one garment is owed.
Bara’at al-dhimma: the original presumption is no liability.
5
Determine the mufta bihi position
The relied-upon view is that of Abu Yusuf (and Abu Hanifa): only one garment is due.
This is the operative fatwa in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن قال ثوب في عشرة أثواب لم يلزمه إلا ثوب واحد عند أبي يوسف. وقال محمد لزمه أحد عشر ثوبا لأن النفيس من الثياب قد يلف في عشرة أثواب فأمكن حمله على الظرف. ولأبي يوسف أن حرف في يستعمل في البين والوسط أيضا قال الله تعالى فادخلي في عبادي أي بين عبادي فوقع الشك والأصل براءة الذمة. على أن كل ثوب مظروف وليس بظرف فتعذر حمله على الظرف فتعين الأول محملا.
And if he said 'a garment among ten garments,' it is not obligatory upon him except one garment according to Abu Yusuf. And Muhammad said, 'Eleven garments are obligatory upon him because a precious garment may be wrapped in ten garments, so it is possible to interpret it as a container.' And for Abu Yusuf, the letter 'fi' is also used for 'between' and 'midst,' as Allah said, 'So enter among My servants,' i.e., between My servants. So doubt occurred, and the principle is freedom of liability. Moreover, every garment is a mazruf (contained) and not a zarf (container), so interpreting it as a container is impossible. Thus the first interpretation is determined.
Source pages p. 60

Commentary
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad. The acknowledgment is 'a garment among ten garments' (thawb fi 'asharat athwab). Muhammad argues that since valuable garments are sometimes wrapped in multiple layers, the word 'fi' can indicate containment, so all eleven are owed. Abu Yusuf counters that 'fi' can also mean 'among' or 'between' (as in the Qur'anic verse), so there is doubt, and the original presumption (bara'at al-dhimma) is that no extra liability exists. Additionally, each of the ten is itself a contained item, not a container for the one, so interpreting 'fi' as containment is impossible. Therefore, only one garment is owed. The relied-upon position is that of Abu Yusuf and Abu Hanifa (as mentioned in the commentary) that one garment is due.

Key Terms
مظروف (mazruf): The contained item; in this context, each of the ten garments is a mazruf, not a zarf.
ظرف (zarf): A container; something that can hold another item.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi position, if someone says 'I owe you a garment among ten garments,' how many garments is he liable for?
A) One
B) Ten
C) Eleven
D) None

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, an ambiguous acknowledgment ('a garment among ten') results in liability for only one garment due to the default meaning of 'fi' and the principle of bara'at al-dhimma.

The Dispute on Including Endpoints: From One to Ten Dirhams
Ruling on acknowledgment 'from one dirham to ten'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi positions on the acknowledgment 'from one dirham to ten' and explain the reasoning behind including or excluding endpoints.

Core Idea
In Hanafi fiqh, the inclusion of endpoints in an acknowledgment 'from X to Y' is disputed: the starting point may be included or excluded, affecting the total owed.

This passage presents an intra-Hanafi disagreement about the interpretation of the phrase 'from one dirham to ten' in an acknowledgment of debt. Abu Hanifa, the Sahibayn, and Zufar each derive a different amount based on whether the starting or ending limit is included. Understanding this dispute helps clarify how Hanafi scholars approach ambiguous contractual language.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal act
Recognize that this is an acknowledgment of debt (iqrar) using the phrase 'from one dirham to ten'. The ambiguity lies in whether the limits are included.
The phrase is 'min dirham ila 'ashara'.
2
Understand the linguistic issue
The key is how the Arabic particles 'min' (from) and 'ila' (to) are interpreted in legal context. Does 'ila' include the endpoint or not?
Arabic grammar often treats 'ila' as exclusive of the endpoint in ranges.
3
List the three positions
Memorize the amounts: Abu Hanifa (9), Sahibayn (10), Zufar (8). Each corresponds to a different inclusion rule.
Abu Hanifa: include start, exclude end. Sahibayn: include both. Zufar: exclude both.
4
Analyze the reasoning
Consider why each Imam adopted his view. Abu Hanifa follows the default linguistic rule. Sahibayn may favor the creditor. Zufar takes a strict literal approach.
No explicit proofs are given in the passage; the views are based on usul principles.
5
Note the practical difference
The amount owed can vary by up to 2 dirhams depending on the view. This shows the importance of interpretation in contractual language.
In practice, a judge or mufti must choose one of these positions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو قال له علي من درهم إلى عشرة أو قال ما بين درهم إلى عشرة لزمه تسعة عند أبي حنيفة فيلزمه الابتداء وما بعده وتسقط الغاية. وقالا يلزمه العشرة كلها فيدخل الغايتان. وقال زفر يلزمه ثمانية ولا يدخل الغايتان.
And if he said, 'I owe him from one dirham to ten' or he said 'what is between one dirham to ten,' then nine is obligatory upon him according to Abu Hanifa - so the beginning and what follows it are obligatory and the endpoint falls. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: the full ten is obligatory, so both endpoints are included. And Zufar said: eight is obligatory, and neither endpoint is included.
Source pages p. 61

Commentary
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the acknowledgment 'from one dirham to ten' (min dirham ila 'ashara). Abu Hanifa holds that the starting point (one) is included, and everything after it up to but not including the endpoint (ten) is due, so nine. The two shaykhs (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that both endpoints are included, so ten. Zufar holds that neither endpoint is included, so eight. The passage also mentions a parallel ruling for 'between this wall and that wall' where the walls themselves are not included, but that is a separate context. The relied-upon position is not explicitly stated here, but the commentary in the original work may indicate that one of these views is preferred.

Key Terms
الغايتين (al-ghayatayn): The two endpoints: the starting point and the ending point in a phrase like 'from X to Y'.
الإقرار (al-iqrar): Acknowledgment or confession of a debt or right.
من...إلى (min...ila): The Arabic construction 'from...to' used to indicate a range.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, if someone says 'I owe you from one dirham to ten dirhams,' how many dirhams does he owe?
A) 10
B) 9
C) 8
D) 1

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, an acknowledgment 'from one dirham to ten' is subject to three interpretations: nine (Abu Hanifa), ten (Sahibayn), or eight (Zufar), based on inclusion or exclusion of endpoints.

Acknowledgment of 'Five in Five' – Hanafi Interpretation
Explains the legal meaning of 'five in five' in acknowledgment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on the phrase 'five in five' in an acknowledgment and apply the distinction between literal and intended meanings.

Core Idea
The word 'fi' does not multiply; only five is owed unless addition is explicitly intended.

This passage addresses a common phrasing in acknowledgment: 'I owe so-and-so five in five.' Does it mean twenty-five or just five? The Hanafi school, following Abu Hanifa, holds that only five dirhams are owed, because multiplication does not increase the actual corpus of money. This lesson unpacks the linguistic and legal reasoning behind this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ambiguous phrase
The phrase 'five in five' (خمسة في خمسة) is ambiguous: does it mean five with five (addition) or five times five (multiplication)? The Hanafi default is that 'fi' does not indicate multiplication.
The word 'fi' primarily means 'in' or 'with'.
2
State the Hanafi ruling
According to Abu Hanifa, only five dirhams are owed because multiplication does not increase the actual wealth; it is a mathematical operation on a single number.
The intention of multiplication does not change the physical quantity.
3
Analyze the minority view
Al-Hasan ibn Ziyad holds that twenty-five are owed, taking the phrase literally as multiplication.
This view is not the mufta bihi.
4
Apply the tarjih mechanism
The majority view is preferred because it aligns with the literal meaning of 'fi' and the principle of bara'at al-dhimma (immunity of the debtor until proven otherwise).
The mufta bihi is that only five are owed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَوْ قَالَ لِفُلَانٍ عَلَيَّ خَمْسَةٌ فِي خَمْسَةٍ يُرِيدُ الضَّرْبَ وَالْحِسَابَ لَزِمَهُ خَمْسَةٌ لِأَنَّ الضَّرْبَ لَا يُكْثِرُ الْمَالَ وَقَالَ الْحَسَنُ يَلْزَمُهُ خَمْسَةٌ وَعِشْرُونَ وَقَدْ ذَكَرْنَاهُ فِي الطَّلَاقِ وَلَوْ قَالَ أَرَدْتُ خَمْسَةً مَعَ خَمْسَةٍ لَزِمَهُ عَشَرَةٌ لِأَنَّ اللَّفْظَ يَحْتَمِلُهُ
And if he said, 'So-and-so has five in five upon me,' intending multiplication and calculation, five is binding upon him because multiplication does not increase the wealth. And al-Hasan said, twenty-five is binding upon him, and we have mentioned it in (the book of) divorce. And if he said, 'I intended five with five,' ten is binding upon him because the word is susceptible to that meaning.
Source pages p. 61

Commentary
This passage addresses the interpretation of the word 'fi' (in) in an acknowledgment. If someone says, 'I owe so-and-so five in five,' and he intends multiplication (i.e., 5 × 5), the Hanafi position is that only five dirhams are owed, not twenty-five. The reason is that multiplication does not increase the actual corpus of the money; it merely increases the number of units in calculation. Al-Hasan ibn Ziyad, a transmitter from Abu Hanifa, held the view that twenty-five are owed, treating it as literal multiplication. The text also clarifies that if the person says he intended 'five with five' (addition), then ten are owed because the word 'fi' can also mean 'with' (ma'a). The issue has parallels in the book of divorce, where a similar linguistic point is discussed. The correct ruling in the Hanafi school is that only five are due when the word 'fi' is used without additional clarification, as the primary meaning of 'fi' is container (zarfhiyya), and it cannot be taken to mean multiplication unless explicitly intended.

Key Terms
إقرار (iqrar): Acknowledgment or confession of a right or debt against oneself.
خمسة في خمسة (khamsat fi khamsa): A phrase whose legal meaning depends on intention; default is not multiplication.
الضرب (al-darb): Multiplication; here used as a mathematical operation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) 10 dirhams
B) 5 dirhams
C) 25 dirhams
D) Nothing, because it's unclear

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, the word 'fi' in an acknowledgment does not imply multiplication; only the base number is owed unless addition is intended.
